General Rule of Dividing Joint Land
States the primary rule for dividing jointly owned land among partners

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi method for dividing jointly owned land and apply it to a given scenario.

Core Idea
Divide joint land by naming shares, casting lots, and assigning each share its pathway and water right.

In joint ownership (mushāʿ), disputes often arise. The Hanafi school prescribes a clear procedure to avoid conflict: partition by lottery after defining shares, ensuring each share has independent access and water rights. This passage presents that method.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act being ruled
The passage rules on the procedure for dividing jointly owned land (qisma) among partners.
Qisma here refers to partition of joint property, not inheritance shares.
2
Outline the method
The steps are: make distinct shares, name each share, cast lots (qur'a) to assign them, and give each share its own pathway (tariq) and water channel (shurb).
Lottery ensures fairness; naming avoids confusion.
3
Note the inclusion of other assets
The passage indicates that if the partners also have shared currency (dirhams, daniqs), these can be included in the division along with the land.
This allows a comprehensive partition when multiple asset types are involved.
4
Recognize the hukm level
Partition by this method is recommended (sunnah muakkadah) to prevent disputes, not obligatory, but a judge can compel it if a partner demands division of divisible property.
The ruling is based on the need to remove harm and facilitate use.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صل في كيفية القسمة
زمین کے حصے بنا کر اور ان کے نام کر پھر قرعہ اندازی کرے تقسیم کرنے کا قاعدہ کلیہ
ہر حصہ کو اس کے راستے اور شرب کل کرے
زمین کی تقسیم میں درا ہم اور دنا نیر کو شر کا ء رضاعی سے شریک کر سکتا ہے
Section on the method of division. Make shares of land and name them, then cast lots: this is the general rule of division. Give each share its pathway and water channel. In division of land, he may include dirhams and daniqs with the sharers of the share.
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage states the general ruling on partitioning jointly owned land. The method is to divide the land into distinct shares, assign each share a name or identifier, and then use a lottery (qur'a) to assign shares to partners. Each share must be given its own right of way and water access (shurb). This prevents future disputes. The passage also indicates that in a land division, if the partners also have shared currency (dirhams, daniqs), the division can include them along with the land shares. This is the basic procedure in Hanafi fiqh for dividing joint property (mushāʿ).

Key Terms
قسمة (qisma): Partition of jointly owned property into separate shares assigned to each partner.
قرعہ (qur'a): Lottery or drawing lots to assign shares randomly to ensure fairness.
شرب (shurb): Right of irrigation or water channel for the land.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what must be given to each land share in a partition?
A) Independent ownership
B) Its pathway and water channel
C) A monetary value
D) A representative

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi method for dividing joint land requires naming shares, casting lots, and ensuring each share has its own pathway and water access.

Shared Pathways and Drainage After Land Division
Ruling on continuing shared access rights after land partition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on shared access rights after land partition and apply it to cases where rights were or were not mentioned at the time of division.

Core Idea
Partition does not cancel existing rights of access and drainage unless new ones are explicitly assigned.

When land is divided among partners, what happens to the existing shared pathways and drains? This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a common dispute: one partner's plot becomes landlocked after division. The Hanafi school rules based on whether these rights were mentioned at division, and on the principle of preventing harm (la darar). The judge must ensure no partner suffers loss of access or drainage due to the partition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Dispute
After land division, one partner passes through another's plot and drains water. No mention of these rights (tah wa sail) was made at the time of the lottery (division).
2
Determine if Rights Were Mentioned
If at division the rights of way and water were specifically mentioned, and it is physically possible to give each partner a separate path and drain, then this must be done. Providing separate access is wajib.
Separate paths must be feasible without excessive cost or harm.
3
If Rights Not Mentioned or Separate Paths Impossible
If no mention was made, or if separate access is not possible despite being mentioned, the original shared rights continue. Partners must allow each other to pass and drain as before.
The default is preservation of existing arrangements to prevent harm.
4
Handle Disagreement Among Partners
If partners disagree about leaving the shared path, and it is impossible to open individual paths, they must keep the original shared path. The judge does not force a change.
If individual paths become possible later, the ruling may be revisited.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جس جگہ کی شر کا تقسیم چاہتے ہیں اس عمارت اور کچھ خالی پلاٹ ہے قاضی اسے کیسے تقسیم کرے شرکاء میں تقسیم کر دی گئی اور بوقت قسمت تہ اور سیل کا کوئی تذکرہ نہیں ہوا اور ایک دوسرے کے حصہ سے گذرتا ہے اور نالی بہاتا ہو تو اب کیا
اگر قسمت میں حقوق کا ذکر آیا ہو اور راستہ دل پھیر نا ممکن بھی ہے تو ہر ایک کو الگ راستہ اور نالی پھیرنا ضروری ہے
دوسری صورت
اگر راستہ چھوڑنے میں شرکاء کا اختلاف ہو تو کیا جائے اگر انفرادی راستہ کھولنا ممکن نہ ہو تو مشتر کہ راسطولا جائے
If a place whose share they want to divide, it has a building and some empty plot, the judge how shall he divide? The division was carried out among partners and at the time of the lot no mention was made of under (tah) and flow (sail), and one passes through the other's share and channels water, then what? If in the division rights were mentioned and it is possible to reroute the path, then each must be given a separate path and drain. Second case: If there is disagreement about leaving the path, what should be done? If it is not possible to open individual paths, then a shared path should be used.
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage deals with a practical problem in land partition: after the division, one partner's plot has no independent access or drainage. The ruling: If at the time of division no mention was made of rights of way and water (tah wa sail), then the partners continue to share those rights as before. If rights were specifically mentioned and it is feasible to give each a separate path and drain, that must be done. If partners disagree about whether to leave a shared path, and it is impossible to open individual paths, then they keep the original shared path. This is based on the Hanafi principle that partition should not cause harm (la darar wa la dirar).

Key Terms
تہ (tah): Underneath or the lower part; here it likely refers to underground water rights or a drain.
سیل (sail): Flow; here it refers to surface water flow or drainage.
تہ اور سیل (tah wa sail): A compound term covering both underground and surface water rights; essentially the entire drainage and water flow rights.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, if at the time of land division no mention was made of pathways and water rights, and after division one partner's plot lies landlocked, what is the ruling?
A) That partner must buy a path from the other partner.
B) The previous shared rights of access and drainage continue.
C) The judge cancels the division and orders a new one.
D) The landlocked partner must accept the loss and use alternative means.

Key Takeaway
Silence at partition preserves existing access and drainage rights; only explicit mention and feasibility can mandate separate paths.

Testimony of Qasims in Dispute After Division
Ruling on accepting testimony of two qasims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on accepting the testimony of two qasims when a partner disputes receiving his share, and explain the legal basis for that ruling.

Core Idea
The testimony of two appointed qasims outweighs a partner's bare claim.

In disputes over property division, the court relies on the evidence of the appointed surveyors (qasims) who performed the partition. This lesson examines a specific scenario: after division, a partner claims he did not receive his allocated share, but the two qasims testify that he did. The Hanafi ruling is that the qasims' testimony is accepted, even though they are not ordinary witnesses. Let's understand why.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is a partner claiming non-receipt of his share after division. The ruling is that the testimony of two qasims (surveyors) that he did receive is accepted, and the partner's claim is rejected.
The ruling is procedural, not substantive.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is qiyas (analogy) to the general principle of accepting the testimony of two just witnesses.
The source does not quote a text; the basis is the general principle.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The qasims are appointed by the judge and are neutral; their testimony is equivalent to that of any two just witnesses. Their official role does not disqualify them.
The key is impartiality.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is an intra-Hanafi difference: Imam Muhammad may have held that qasims have an interest in upholding their own division, thus their testimony is not accepted without corroboration. The majority (Shaykhayn) accepts it unconditionally.
The text references Shaykhayn as the accepted position.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The mufta bihi (operative view) is that of Shaykhayn: the testimony of two qasims is accepted. This is based on their neutral appointment and the need to ensure finality of partitions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قاسمین نے شرکاء کے درمیان تقسیم کر دی پھر شرکاء میں اختلاف ہوا کسی نے کہا ر ا حصہ مجھے نہیں ملا حالانکہ میرے حصہ میں فلاں کمرہ داخل ہے اور دو قاسموں نے گواہی دی کہ اس نا لے لیا ہے تو گواہی قبول کی جائے گی
The qasims (surveyors/partitioners) performed the division among the partners, then the partners disagreed. One said: I did not get my share, although my share includes such-and-such room. And the two qasims testified that he took it. Then their testimony will be accepted.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage gives a rule of evidence in partition disputes. After the two appointed surveyors (qasiman) have divided the joint property and the partners have received their shares, if a partner later claims he did not receive his share, but the two qasims testify that he did, then their testimony is accepted. The reason is that the qasims are appointed by the judge and they are reliable witnesses; their testimony outweighs the partner's bare claim. This is in line with the Hanafi rule that a party's claim against clear evidence of the qasims is not accepted. The dispute is about fact (delivery), not about the validity of the division.

Key Terms
قاسم (qasim): A surveyor appointed by the judge to carry out the partition (plural: qasimin).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
After division, a partner claims he did not receive his share, but the two qasims testify that he did. What is the ruling?
A) The partner's claim is accepted because he is an owner
B) The qasims' testimony is accepted
C) Both testimonies are rejected
D) The judge rules arbitrarily

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the testimony of two court-appointed qasims after division is accepted over a partner's bare claim.

Conditions and Rulings for Invalid Muzara'ah
Lists validity conditions and invalid contract rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify conditions that invalidate a Muzara'ah contract and state the rulings on produce distribution and worker's wage for an invalid Muzara'ah.

Core Idea
Any condition removing commonality (shuyu') in produce shares invalidates Muzara'ah.

This passage from Ashraf Ul Hadaya outlines key validity conditions for Muzara'ah (sharecropping) and the consequences when the contract becomes invalid. You will learn that commonality (shuyu') in the produce is essential, and how certain stipulations break it. The passage also provides specific rulings on distribution of grain and straw, and the entitlements in an invalid contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core validity condition
Note that commonality (shuyu') in the produce share is necessary. Any condition that eliminates this commonality makes the contract invalid.
Shuyu' means the produce must be divided in unspecified, common shares, not allocated to specific portions.
2
Recognize examples that violate commonality
If one party stipulates that produce from certain areas (e.g., near canals) belongs exclusively to him, commonality is removed and the contract is void.
These are conditions that specify portions of the harvest for one party, breaking the shared nature.
3
Distinguish valid vs invalid based on grain and straw
If grain is shared equally and straw is not mentioned, the contract is valid because the main crop is shared. If one party gets all the grain and the other all the straw, it is invalid.
Equal division of the primary product (grain) preserves commonality even if byproduct (straw) is unmentioned or given to a third party.
4
Apply the ruling for invalid Muzara'ah
When the contract is fasid (invalid), all produce goes to the landowner. The worker only gets an equivalent wage (ujrat al-mithl) if the seed was provided by the landowner.
The passage emphasizes that if the landowner provided the seed, he gets all the produce; the worker gets his market wage for labor.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مزارعت کی صحت کیلئے آٹھ شرائط میں سے پہلی شرط دوسری اور تیسری شرط چوتھی شرط پانچویں شرط چٹھی شرط صاحبین کے نزدیک مزارعت کے جواز کی چار صورتوں میں سے پہلی صورت دوسری صورت تیسری صورت چوتھی صورت پانچویں صورت چٹھی صورت جن صورتوں میں مزارعت فاسد ہے ان میں پیداوار کس کی ہے دو تفریعات کا تذکرہ ہر وہ شرط جو شیوع کو ختم کر دے مفسد مزارعت ہوگی ہر ایک نے یہ شرط لگائی کہ جو پیداوار نالیوں کے آس پاس ہوگی وہ میں ہوگی یا کھیت کے متعین کونہ کی پیداوار میری ہوگی ان صورتوں میں مزارعت باطل ہے ایک کیلئے غلہ دوسرے کیلئے بھوسہ کی شرط لگائی تو بھی مزارعت فائر ہے بھوسہ دونوں کیلئے نصف نصف اور غلہ ایک کا مزارعت سد ہے غلہ نصف نصف اور بھوسہ کا تذکرہ نہیں کیا تو مزارعت درست غلہ نصف نصف اور بھوسہ کی بیچ والے کیلئے شرط لگائی تو مزارعت درست ہے مزارعت صحیح ہونے کی صورت میں پیداوار شرط کے مطابق تقسیم ہوگی مزارعت فاسد ہونے کی صورت میں پیداوار بیچنے والے کی ہوگی بیج رب الارض کی جانب سے ہو تو عامل کیلئے اجرت مثل ہوگی زمین اور بیل مالک کے ہوں اور باقی کام عامل کا ہوتو مزارعت فاسد ہے مزارعت فاسدہ میں بیج کی وجہ سے زمین والا کل پیداوار کا مستحق ہے
First condition for validity of Muzara'ah from the eight conditions. Second and third conditions. Fourth condition. Fifth condition. Sixth condition. The first of the four forms of permissibility according to the Sahibayn. Second form. Third form. Fourth form. Fifth form. Sixth form. In the forms in which Muzara'ah is invalid, to whom does the produce belong? Mention of two derivations. Every condition that removes commonality will be a factor invalidating Muzara'ah. Everyone imposed the condition that the produce around the canals is mine, or the produce of a specified corner of the field is mine; in these forms Muzara'ah is void. If they imposed the condition that one gets grain and the other gets straw, then also Muzara'ah is invalid. If straw is half-half for both and grain for one, Muzara'ah is invalid. If grain is half-half and straw is not mentioned, then Muzara'ah is valid. If grain is half-half and straw is conditioned for the middle person, then Muzara'ah is valid. When Muzara'ah is valid, the produce is distributed according to the condition. When Muzara'ah is invalid, the produce belongs to the seller (owner). If the seed is from the landowner, then the worker is entitled to the equivalent wage. If the land and oxen belong to the owner and the remaining work is done by the worker, then Muzara'ah is invalid. In an invalid Muzara'ah, due to the seed the landowner is entitled to the entire produce.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage is a listing of key rulings for Muzara'ah (sharecropping) from the Hanafi text Ashraf Ul Hadaya. It begins by mentioning that there are eight conditions for validity, but only enumerates several without detail. Then it notes that the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) recognize four permissible forms, but six are listed. The core legal principle is stated: any condition that removes commonality (shuyu') in the share of produce invalidates the contract. Examples follow: if one party stipulates that produce from certain areas belongs exclusively to him, the contract is void (batil). Similarly, if one party takes grain and the other straw, it is invalid. However, if the share of grain is half-half and straw is not mentioned, the contract is valid because commonality in grain is preserved. If straw is assigned to a third party, it is also valid. When the contract is valid, produce is divided as stipulated. When it becomes invalid (fasid), the produce belongs to the landowner (who provided the land), and the worker (amil) receives the equivalent wage (ujrat al-mithl) only if the seed was from the landowner. If the land and oxen are from the owner and the worker does the labor, the contract is fasid, and due to the seed, the landowner gets all the produce.

Key Terms
شیوع (shuyu'): Commonality or shared ownership; the produce must be divided in common shares for the contract to be valid.
مزارعت فاسد (muzara'ah fasid): An invalid sharecropping contract; the produce goes to the landowner, and the worker gets equivalent wage if seed is from landowner.
اجرت مثل (ujrat al-mithl): The standard market wage for the work performed by the worker in a fasid Muzara'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a Muzara'ah contract, if the grain is divided equally and the straw is given to a third party, what is the ruling according to the Hanafi school?
A) The contract is invalid because straw is not shared between the parties.
B) The contract is valid because the grain is shared equally.
C) The contract is valid only if the third party is a relative.
D) The contract is invalid because commonality is broken.

Key Takeaway
For a Muzara'ah contract to be valid, the produce must be shared in common shares; any condition removing commonality makes it invalid, and then the landowner gets all produce while the worker gets market wage if seed was from the landowner.

Rulings of Muzara'ah (Sharecropping) Contract
Series of distinct Hanafi rulings on muzara'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the key rulings of the muzara'ah contract regarding death of parties, defective conditions, and compulsory actions, and apply them to new scenarios.

Core Idea
In muzara'ah, the contract ends upon a party's death before sowing, but heirs may continue after sprouting — each scenario has a distinct Hanafi ruling.

The Hanafi school provides detailed guidance for the sharecropping contract (muzara'ah), addressing irregularities like death or refusal to sow. This lesson presents a series of specific rulings from the classical texts, clarifying when the contract remains valid, becomes fasid, or is void.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their obligations
In muzara'ah, the landowner provides land (and often seed), and the cultivator works it. Their obligations are defined by the contract.
The source begins with seed belonging to landowner; refusal to sow may lead to compulsion.
2
Analyze the effect of death before vs after sowing
Compare rulings: landowner dies before any sowing (contract ends), dies after tilling but before sowing (contract ends), dies after crop appears (contract valid for that year, fasid for future years).
Death of either party invalidates the contract generally, but exceptions exist if crop is already in the ground.
3
Distinguish valid vs invalid conditions
Any condition that contradicts the nature of muzara'ah and benefits only one party is mufsid (corrupting) and makes the contract fasid.
This is a crucial Hanafi principle for contract validity.
4
Determine cost sharing and heir rights
Harvest and post-harvest costs are shared proportionally. If the cultivator dies after sprouting, his heirs have the right to continue until harvest.
Heirs' right is established even if landowner refuses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عقد مزارعت طے ہو گیا اور بیج زمین والے کا تھا مگر وہ بیج ڈالنے سے رک گیا تو اسے مجبور کیا جائے گا یا نہیں۔ معاقدین میں سے ایک کی موت سے عقد باطل ہو جاتی ہے۔ زمین مزارعت پر تین سال کیلئے تھی ابھی سال میں کھیتی اگی اور کافی نہیں گئی کہ زمین والا مر گیا اسی سال کے آخر تک مزارعت ہوگی بقیہ دو سال میں مزارعت فاسد ہے رب الارض کاشت سے پہلے مر جائے کہ اس نے ابھی زمین جوتی اور نالیاں بنالیں ابھی بیج نہیں بویا تو مزارعت ختم ہو جائے گی۔ صاحب زمین پر اتنا قرض ہو گیا کہ زمین کے بغیر کوئی چارہ کار نہیں تو اس کیلئے زمین [؟] جائز ہے صاحب ارض مقروض ہے اور زمین [؟] بغیر کو ہار نہیں اور کھیتی اگی ہوئی ہے تو کھیتی کاٹنے تک بیج کو مؤخر کیا جائے گا مزارعت کی ملک ختم ہوگئی اور کھیتی کی نہیں [کا شیکا سنائی؟] تک زمین کی اجرت مثل لازم ہے زمین والے نے کچی کھیتی لینے کا ارادہ کیا تو [اس کا مہیں؟]۔ کھیتی اگنے کے بعد کاشتکار مر گیا اس کے ورثا نے کہ کھیتی کٹنے تک ہم کام کریں گے اور زمین والے نے انکار کیا تو وارثین کیلئے کام کا حق ہے۔ کٹائی کھلیان میں لانے کا [؟] اور اڑانے کی اجرت [نہ ونوں پر بقد رحصہ؟] ہوگی۔ عقد میں ایسی شرط لگائی جو [مقتنا؟]، عقد کے خلاف ہے عاقدین میں سے کسی ایک کا فائدہ ہو تو ایسی شرط مفسد عقد ہے۔ مسائل مذکورہ کا خلاصہ۔ کچی کھیتی کاٹنی چاہے یا پھل توڑنا چاہے تو کام کون کرے گا۔
The contract of muzara'ah was concluded and the seed belonged to the landowner, but he refrained from sowing, will he be compelled or not? The contract becomes void by the death of one of the contracting parties. The land was given on muzara'ah for three years; in the first year the crop grew but did not ripen and the landowner died: the muzara'ah will remain for the end of that year, for the remaining two years the muzara'ah is fasid. If the landowner dies before cultivation, having only plowed the land and dug canals but not sown seeds, the muzara'ah ends. If the landowner becomes so indebted that he has no recourse except the land, then it is permissible for him [to sell/lease?] the land. The landowner is in debt and has no alternative without the land, and the crop has grown, then the seed [payment] will be deferred until the harvest. The ownership of muzara'ah ended but not ownership of the crop; [until?] the ujrat al-mithl for the land is obligatory. The landowner intended to take the green crop, then [؟]. After the crop sprouted, the cultivator died; his heirs said we will work until the harvest, and the landowner refused; the heirs have the right to work. The cost of harvesting and bringing to the threshing floor and winnowing will be [proportionate?] to their shares. In the contract, a condition was inserted that is against the contract and beneficial to one party; such a condition is corrupting (mufsid) the contract. Summary of the mentioned issues: If one wants to cut the green crop or pluck fruit, who will do the work?
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage presents a series of distinct rulings regarding the contract of muzara'ah (sharecropping) as per the Hanafi school. Each ruling addresses a specific scenario. First, if the seed owner (landowner) refuses to sow after the contract, he may be compelled to do so, as the contract obligates him. Second, the contract is invalidated by the death of either party—this is a general rule. Third, if the contract is for multiple years and the landowner dies after the crop appears in the first year but before ripening, the contract remains valid for that year but becomes fasid for the remaining years. Fourth, if the landowner dies before any sowing (only tilling done), the contract ends entirely. Fifth, if the landowner is in severe debt and the land is his only asset, he may dispose of it (e.g., sell) to pay the debt; if the crop is already grown, the seed payment is deferred until harvest. Sixth, after the crop sprouts, if the cultivator dies, his heirs have the right to continue working until harvest, even if the landowner refuses. Seventh, the costs of harvesting, transporting, and winnowing are shared proportionally according to each party's share. Eighth, any condition that contradicts the nature of the contract and benefits only one party is invalidating (mufsid). The passage ends with a summary question: who performs the cutting of green crops or fruit plucking? This likely indicates a need for specification in the contract.

Key Terms
مزارعت (muzāra‘ah): A contract of sharecropping where one party provides land and the other works it, sharing the produce.
فاسد (fāsid): A contract that is legally defective, not completely void but requiring correction or yielding different consequences.
عقد (‘aqd): A legal contract or agreement between two parties.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In muzara'ah, if the landowner dies before sowing but after tilling, what happens to the contract?
A) The contract remains valid and the heirs continue.
B) The contract ends because the landowner's death before sowing invalidates it.
C) The contract becomes fasid and the worker gets ujrat al-mithl.
D) The contract continues only if the heirs agree.

Key Takeaway
The validity of a muzara'ah contract hinges on timing of death and presence of contract-consistent conditions; death before sowing voids the contract, while heirs of a deceased cultivator may continue after sprouting.

Three Categories of Shuf'ah Beneficiaries and Their Proof from Hadith
Lists three types of shafī' and provides three hadith proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three categories of shuf'ah beneficiaries in Hanafi fiqh and cite the three hadith proofs for their right.

Core Idea
Shuf'ah is wajib for three types: partner in property, partner in rights, and neighbor, in that order.

This lesson presents the foundational ruling on shuf'ah (pre-emption) from the Hanafi tradition. Imam al-Quduri's matn states that shuf'ah is established for three types of claimants in a specific order of priority. The author of al-Hidayah then provides three hadith proofs to ground each category in the Sunnah. Understanding this framework is essential for applying shuf'ah correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
Read Quduri's statement and note the three beneficiaries: partner in the property itself, partner in rights (water/path), and neighbor. Understand that these are not equal; there is a priority order.
2
Examine the order of priority
The partner in the property is strongest, then partner in rights, then neighbor. The weaker claimant cannot pre-empt against a stronger one.
3
Review the first hadith proof
The hadith 'Al-shuf'atu li-sharīkin lam yuqāsim' establishes shuf'ah for the co-owner who has not divided.
4
Review the second hadith proof
The hadith 'Jār al-dār ahaqqu bil-dār...' establishes shuf'ah for the neighbor who shares a path (partner in rights).
5
Review the third hadith proof
The hadith 'Al-jār ahaqqu bi suqbihi' where the Prophet explained al-suqb as shuf'ah, establishes shuf'ah for the neighbor.
Note the alternative narration 'Al-jār ahaqqu bi shuf'atihi'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشفعة
شفعہ کی ترتیب
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۳
قال الشفعة واجبة للخليط فى نفس المبيع ثم للخليط فى حق المبيع كالشرب والطريق ثم للجار افاد هذا اللفظ ثبوت حق الشفعة لكل واحد من هؤلاء وافاد الترتيب
ترجمہ فرمایا امام قدوری نے ، شفعہ ثابت ہے شریک فی نفس امبیع کیلئے پھر حق مبیع میں شریک کیلئے ۔ جیسے شرب اور راستہ پھر پڑوسی کیلئے فائدہ دیا اس لفظ نے حق شفعہ کے ثبوت کا ان میں سے ہر ایک کیلئے اور فائدہ دیا ترتیب کا۔
تشریح جن لوگوں کو شفعہ ملتا ہے اتصال کی بنیاد پر ملتا ہے اور اتصال میں تین فریق شامل ہیں: ا جس کی مین مبیع میں شرکت ہو۔
- شرکت تھی مگر اب ہزارہ ہو گیا اور راستہ اور پانی میں شرکت باقی ہے۔
- پروی
ان تینوں کو قدوری نے بیان فرمایا ہے اب صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ قدوری کا قول للخليط الخ دوباتوں کا فائدہ دے رہا ہے۔ ا۔ ان میں سے تینوں کو حق شفعہ ملے گاوہ دوسری بات ہے کہ اقومی کے سامنے ضعیف محروم ہو جائے۔ ۲۔ ثبوت حق شفعہ کی ترتیب ان کے درمیان یہی ہے جوذ کر کی گئی یعنی شریک فی نفس السمیع سب سے مقدم ہے اور پھر شریک فی حق اسمع اول سے کمزور اور آخر سے قوی ہے اور جارسب سے ضعیف ہے۔ بہر حال کلام قدوری سے نفس ثبوت اور ترتیب ثابت ہوئی۔ سے اب مصنف ان دونوں پر دلائل قائم کریں گے۔
شفعہ کے ثبوت پر نقلی دلائل
اما الثبوت فلقوله عليه السلام الشفعة لشريك لم يقاسم ولقوله عليه السلام جار الدار احق بالدار والارض ينتظر له وان كان غائبا اذا كان طريقهما واحدا و لقوله عليه السلام الجار احق بسقبه قيل يا رسول الله ما سقبه قال شفعته ويروى الجار احق بشفعته
ترجمہ بہر حال ثبوت نبی علیہ السلام کے فرمان الشفعة ... الخ کی وجہ سے ہے اور نبی علیہ السلام کے فرمان جار الدار ... الخ کی جہ سے ہے اور نبی علیہ السلام کے فرمان الجار احق بسقبہ کی وجہ سے ہے۔ عرض کیا گیا یا رسول اللہ سقبۂ کیا چیز ہے فرمایا: شفعته اور روایت کیا گیا ہے الجار احق بشفعته
تشریح چونکہ شفیع تین قسم کے ہیں اسلئے ان کیلئے شفعہ کے ثبوت کیلئے تین حدیثیں پیش فرمائیں گے :-
ا شفعہ ایسے شریک کیلئے ہے جس نے ہوارہ نہ کیا ہو، اس حدیث سے شریک کیلئے شفعہ کا ثبوت ہو گیا۔ گھر کا پڑوسی گھر اور زمین کا زیادہ حقدار ہے اس کا انتظار کیا جائے گا۔ اگر چہ غائب ہو جبکہ ان دونوں کا راستہ ایک ہو، اس حدیث سے شریک فی حق اسمیع کیلئے شفعہ کا ثبوت ہو گیا۔ ۔ پڑوسی اپنے سقب کا زیادہ مستحق ہے اور ایک روایت میں الجار احق بشفعته مروی ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے تینوں حدیثیں پیش فرما
Kitab al-Shuf'ah. Arrangement of Shuf'ah. Ashraf al-Hidaya Sharh Urdu Hidaya Volume 13. He said: 'Shuf'ah is obligatory for the partner in the very property sold, then for the partner in the right of the sold property, such as share of water and path, then for the neighbor.' This phrasing indicates the establishment of the right of shuf'ah for each of these, and indicates the order. Translation: Imam Quduri said: Shuf'ah is established for the partner in the very property sold, then for the partner in the right of the sold property, like water and path, then for the neighbor. This word indicates the establishment of the right of shuf'ah for each of them, and indicates the order. Explanation: Those who receive shuf'ah receive it on the basis of connection, and connection includes three parties: 1. One whose partnership is in the property itself; 2. One who had partnership but it has ceased, and partnership in path and water remains; 3. The neighbor. These three have been mentioned by Quduri. Now the author of al-Hidayah says that Quduri's statement 'for the partner etc.' gives two benefits: 1. All three will receive the right of shuf'ah, though it is another matter that a weaker one may be excluded in front of a stronger one; 2. The order of the right of shuf'ah among them is as mentioned: the partner in the property itself is most preferred, then the partner in the right is weaker than the first and stronger than the last, and the neighbor is the weakest. In any case, from the words of Quduri, both the establishment and the order are proven. Now the author will establish proofs for both. Proofs from transmitted sources for the establishment of shuf'ah: As for the establishment, it is due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'Shuf'ah is for a partner who has not divided' and his saying, peace be upon him: 'The neighbor of the house has more right to the house and land; he is waited for even if he is absent, when their path is one' and his saying, peace be upon him: 'The neighbor has more right to his suqb.' It was said: O Messenger of Allah, what is suqb? He said: 'His shuf'ah.' And it is narrated: 'The neighbor has more right to his shuf'ah.' Translation: In any case, the establishment is due to the Prophet's statement 'Al-shuf'ah...' etc., and due to the Prophet's statement 'Jar al-dar...' etc., and due to the Prophet's statement 'Al-jar ahaqqu bi suqbihi.' It was asked: O Messenger of Allah, what is suqb? He said: 'His shuf'ah.' And it is narrated: 'Al-jar ahaqqu bi shuf'atihi.' Explanation: Since the shafī' is of three types, three hadiths are presented for their shuf'ah: 1. Shuf'ah is for a partner who has not divided. This hadith establishes shuf'ah for the partner. 2. The neighbor of the house has more right to the house and land; he is waited for even if absent, when their path is one. This hadith establishes shuf'ah for the partner in the right of the sold property. 3. The neighbor has more right to his suqb. And in one narration: 'Al-jar ahaqqu bi shuf'atihi.' The author of al-Hidayah has presented these three hadiths.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage presents the core ruling and proof for shuf'ah. The matn (from Quduri) states that shuf'ah is wajib (obligatory) for three types of eligible parties in order of priority: first, the partner in the very property that was sold (sharīk fī nafs al-mabī'); second, the partner in the rights attached to the property, such as share in water (shirb) or right of way (tarīq) (sharīk fī haqq al-mabī'); third, the neighbor (jār). The commentary explains that this order reflects the strength of connection: the partner in the property itself has the strongest claim, followed by the one who shares rights, and finally the neighbor. Then three hadiths are cited as proof. The first hadith: 'Al-shuf'atu li-sharīkin lam yuqāsim' (Shuf'ah is for a partner who has not divided) establishes shuf'ah for the co-owner. The second: 'Jār al-dār ahaqqu bil-dār wal-ard...' (The neighbor of the house has more right to the house and land...) establishes shuf'ah for the sharer in rights (since they share a path). The third: 'Al-jār ahaqqu bi suqbihi' (The neighbor has more right to his suqb), where suqb is explained by the Prophet as shuf'ah, establishes shuf'ah for the neighbor. The author (al-Hidayah) uses these to ground the Quduri classification in sunnah.

Key Terms
الخليط (al-khalīṭ): Partner: one who shares in ownership of property or its rights.
الشرب (al-shirb): Share of water: a right to water from a well, stream, etc.
السقب (al-suqb): In the hadith, it is interpreted as shuf'ah; linguistically it may mean adjacency or something else.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, who has the strongest right of shuf'ah?
A) The neighbor
B) The partner in the property itself
C) The partner in the right of water
D) All are equal

Key Takeaway
Shuf'ah is an established right for three categories in order of connection: partner in property, partner in rights, and neighbor, each supported by a specific hadith.

Categories and Order of Pre-emptors (Shuf'ah)
Stating the ruling on who qualifies for shuf'ah and their order

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three categories of pre-emptors in shuf'ah according to the Hanafi school and explain the order of priority.

Core Idea
Shuf'ah is established for three: partner in property, partner in rights, then neighbor — each with a weaker claim.

In this lesson we examine the matn of Quduri on shuf'ah, which lists who has the right of pre-emption. The author of Hidayah explains that this passage gives two benefits: the existence of the right for all three and their order of priority. We will parse each category and understand why the weaker one is later.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Shuf'ah is a right (wajib in the sense of established) for certain persons upon a sale.
It is not a ritual obligation but a legal right.
2
List the categories in order
First: partner in the very thing sold (sharik fi nafs al-mabi'). Second: partner in a right of the thing sold (sharik fi haqq al-mabi'), like water share (sharb) or path (tariq). Third: neighbor (al-jar).
The order is explicitly stated: then (thumma) indicates priority.
3
Understand the basis of priority
The strength of connection (ittisal) determines the strength of the right. The partner in the property has the strongest connection, then the partner in rights, then the neighbor.
Weaker pre-emptors are deprived if a stronger one claims.
4
Note the authority weight
This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah, the core Hanafi texts.
5
Note cross-madhhab difference
Imam al-Shafi'i only recognizes the first category (partner in property), rejecting shuf'ah for partners in rights and neighbors.
This difference affects practical fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشفعة
شفعہ کی ترتیب
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۳
قال الشفعة واجبة للخليط فى نفس المبيع ثم للخليط فى حق المبيع كالشرب والطريق ثم للجار افاد هذا اللفظ ثبوت حق الشفعة لكل واحد من هؤلاء وافاد الترتيب
ترجمہ فرمایا امام قدوری نے ، شفعہ ثابت ہے شریک فی نفس امبیع کیلئے پھر حق مبیع میں شریک کیلئے ۔ جیسے شرب اور راستہ پھر پڑوسی
کیلئے فائدہ دیا اس لفظ نے حق شفعہ کے ثبوت کا ان میں سے ہر ایک کیلئے اور فائدہ دیا ترتیب کا۔
تشریح جن لوگوں کو شفعہ ملتا ہے اتصال کی بنیاد پر ملتا ہے اور اتصال میں تین فریق شامل ہیں: ا جس کی مین مبیع میں شرکت ہو۔
- شرکت تھی مگر اب ہزارہ ہو گیا اور راستہ اور پانی میں شرکت باقی ہے۔
- پروی
ان تینوں کو قدوری نے بیان فرمایا ہے اب صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ قدوری کا قول للخليط الخ دوباتوں کا فائدہ دے رہا ہے۔ ا۔ ان میں سے تینوں کو حق شفعہ ملے گاوہ دوسری بات ہے کہ اقومی کے سامنے ضعیف محروم ہو جائے۔ ۲۔ ثبوت حق شفعہ کی ترتیب ان کے درمیان یہی ہے جوذ کر کی گئی یعنی شریک فی نفس السمیع سب سے مقدم ہے اور پھر شریک فی حق اسمع اول سے کمزور اور آخر سے قوی ہے اور جارسب سے ضعیف ہے۔ بہر حال کلام قدوری سے نفس ثبوت اور ترتیب ثابت ہوئی۔
He said: Shuf'ah is obligatory for the partner in the very thing sold, then for the partner in the right of the thing sold, like water share and path, then for the neighbor. This expression indicates the establishment of the right of shuf'ah for each of these, and it indicates the order. Translation: Imam Quduri said: Shuf'ah is established for the partner in the very thing sold, then for the partner in the right of the thing sold, like water share and path, then for the neighbor. This expression benefits the establishment of the right of shuf'ah for each of them and benefits the order. Explanation: Those who receive shuf'ah receive it on the basis of connection, and connection includes three parties: (1) one who has partnership in the thing sold itself; (2) partnership existed but now has been divided and partnership in path and water remains; (3) neighbor. These three are stated by Quduri. Now the author of Hidayah says: Quduri's words 'for the partner etc.' give two benefits: (1) all three will receive the right of shuf'ah, though it is another matter that the weaker is deprived in front of the stronger; (2) the order of establishment of shuf'ah among them is as mentioned: the partner in the very thing sold is foremost, then the partner in the right of the thing sold is weaker than the first and stronger than the last, and the neighbor is the weakest. In any case, from Quduri's words, the mere establishment and the order are proven.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn of Quduri, explaining who qualifies for the right of pre-emption (shuf'ah) and the order of priority. The author begins by citing the matn: 'Shuf'ah is obligatory (established) for the partner in the very thing sold, then for the partner in the right of the thing sold—like water share and path—then for the neighbor.' This indicates both the existence of the right for each category and the hierarchy among them. The Urdu commentary elaborates that connection (ittisal) is the basis: first is the co-owner in the property itself (sharik fi nafs al-mabi'), even if the property is undivided; second is the co-owner in a right attached to the property, such as a shared water channel or right of way, even after division of the land; third is the neighbor whose property is adjacent. The author of Hidayah notes that the matn gives two benefits: (1) all three have a right to pre-emption, though the stronger (first category) may deprive the weaker; (2) the order is as given—the first category is strongest, the second intermediate, and the neighbor weakest. Later proofs will be provided.

Key Terms
الشفعة (al-shuf'ah): The right of pre-emption: a legal right allowing a partner or neighbor to purchase property that has been sold to an outsider, by paying the price, in order to avoid harm (dharar).
الخليط (al-khalit): The partner or associate; one who shares ownership or right in something.
المبيع (al-mabi'): The thing sold; the property that is the subject of sale.
الشرب (al-sharb): The right to water; a share in a water source or irrigation channel.
الطريق (al-tariq): Path or right of way; a shared access route.
الجار (al-jar): Neighbor; one whose property is adjacent (mulas) to the sold property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi matn, what is the correct order of priority for the right of pre-emption?
A) Neighbor, then partner in rights, then partner in property.
B) Partner in property, then partner in rights, then neighbor.
C) Partner in rights, then partner in property, then neighbor.
D) All have equal right with no order.

Key Takeaway
Shuf'ah belongs to three categories in descending order of strength: partner in property, partner in rights, neighbor.

Hadith Proofs and the Shafi'i Dispute on Neighbor's Pre-emption
Inter-madhhab dispute on neighbor's shuf'ah with hadith proofs and rational arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi proof for neighbor's shuf'ah and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
The neighbor's shuf'ah is proven by hadith and justified by istihsan to prevent harm, despite being contrary to qiyas.

This lesson examines the Hanafi school's proof for granting the right of pre-emption (shuf'ah) to a neighbor, and the objections raised by Imam al-Shafi'i. By analyzing the hadith evidence and the rational arguments on both sides, you will understand how the Hanafi school uses istihsan to extend a ruling beyond its original scope.

Guided Path
1
1. State the Hanafi position
Identify the three categories of shafi' and the status of the neighbor's shuf'ah as the weakest.
The text begins by presenting three hadith for each category.
2
2. Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i denies shuf'ah by mere neighborhood, restricting it to co-owners of undivided property.
The text then presents Shafi'i's argument.
3
3. Follow the opponent's proof
Shafi'i cites a hadith that shuf'ah is only in undivided property, and argues it is an exception to qiyas.
He also uses a rational argument that exceptions stay confined.
4
4. Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds by citing their own hadith and using istihsan based on the harm (dharar) of bad neighbors.
They argue that permanent connection is a cause for harm, analogous to co-ownership.
5
5. Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: in Hanafi fiqh, a neighbor can claim shuf'ah; in Shafi'i, he cannot.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اما الثبوت فلقوله عليه السلام الشفعة لشريك لم يقاسم ولقوله عليه السلام جار الدار احق بالدار والارض ينتظر له وان كان غائبا اذا كان طريقهما واحدا و لقوله عليه السلام الجار احق بسقبه قيل يا رسول الله ما سقبه قال شفعته ويروى الجار احق بشفعته
ترجمہ بہر حال ثبوت نبی علیہ السلام کے فرمان الشفعة ... الخ کی وجہ سے ہے اور نبی علیہ السلام کے فرمان جار الدار ... الخ کی جہ سے ہے اور نبی علیہ السلام کے فرمان الجار احق بسقبہ کی وجہ سے ہے۔ عرض کیا گیا یا رسول اللہ سقبۂ کیا چیز ہے فرمایا: شفعته اور روایت کیا گیا ہے الجار احق بشفعته
تشریح چونکہ شفیع تین قسم کے ہیں اسلئے ان کیلئے شفعہ کے ثبوت کیلئے تین حدیثیں پیش فرمائیں گے :-
ا شفعہ ایسے شریک کیلئے ہے جس نے ہوارہ نہ کیا ہو، اس حدیث سے شریک کیلئے شفعہ کا ثبوت ہو گیا۔ گھر کا پڑوسی گھر اور زمین کا زیادہ حقدار ہے اس کا انتظار کیا جائے گا۔ اگر چہ غائب ہو جبکہ ان دونوں کا راستہ ایک ہو، اس حدیث سے شریک فی حق اسمیع کیلئے شفعہ کا ثبوت ہو گیا۔ ۔ پڑوسی اپنے سقب کا زیادہ مستحق ہے اور ایک روایت میں الجار احق بشفعته مروی ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے تینوں حدیثیں پیش فرما
دی ہیں۔
۳۱
شفعہ، امام شافعی کا نقطہ نظر
كتاب الشفعة
وقال الشافعي لاشفعة بالجوار لقوله عليه السلام الشفعة فيما لم يقسم فاذا وقعت الحدود وصرفت الطرق فلا شفعة ولان حق الشفعة معدول به عن سنن القياس لما فيه من تملك المال على الغير من غير رضاه وقدورد الشرع به فيما لم يقسم وهذا ليس في معناه لأن مؤنة القسمة تلزمه في الاصل دون الفرع
ترجمہ اور فرمایا شافعی نے پڑوس کی وجہ سے شفعہ نہیں ہے نبی علیہ السلام کے فرمان الشفعتہ الخ کی وجہ سے اور اس لئے کہ حق شفعہ ہٹا ہوا ہے قیاس کی روشوں سے اسلئے کہ اس میں غیر کے مال کا مالک ہوتا ہے بغیر اس کی رضامندی کے حالانکہ شریعت وارد ہوئی ہے اس کے ساتھ (حق شفعہ ) ایسی زمین میں جس کی تقسیم نہ ہوئی ہو اور یہ (جار) نہیں ہے اس کے معنی میں ( مورد شرع کے معنی میں ) اسلئے کہ ہوارہ کی مشقت لازم آتی ہے شفیع کو اصل میں نہ کہ فرع میں۔
تشریح امام شافعی فقتها شریک فی مین اسمیع کیلئے شفعہ کے قائل ہیں لہذا انہوں نے جوار کی وجہ سے ثبوت شفعہ کا انکار فرمایا۔ پھر اس پر انہوں نے ایک حدیث پیش فرمائی ، کہ شفعہ ایسی زمین میں ہے جس میں بلوارہ نہ ہوا ہو جب حدود واقع ہو گئیں اور راستے پھیر لئے گئے تو پھر شفعہ نہیں ملے گا۔ بہر حال اس حدیث سے بظاہر صاف یہ معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ نفس جوار کی وجہ سے بغیر شرکت شفعہ نہیں ہے۔ یہ امام شافعی کی نفلی دلیل ہے اور عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حق شفعہ تو خلاف قیاس ہے کیونکہ اس میں بغیر مالک کی رضامندی کے اسکے مال کا مالک ہونا ہوتا ہے اور اصول یہ مقرر ہے کہ جو چیز خلاف قیاس ہوتی ہے وہ مورد شرع تک رہتی ہے اور بقول شافعی مور د شرع فقط غیر مقسوم جائیداد ہے۔ اور باقی کو مور د شرع اصل مذکور کی وجہ سے قیاس نہیں کر سکتے ۔ معلوم ہوا کہ غیر کیلئے ثبوت شفعہ کی کوئی صورت بھی نہیں ہے وهذا ليس في معناه اور یہ یعنی جار مورد شرع کے معنی میں نہیں ہے۔ یعنی امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں ثبوت شفعہ کا اصل راز یہ ہے کہ مالک کو ہوارہ کا ضرر لاحق نہ ہو یعنی دو شریک ہیں ایک نے اپنا حصہ فروخت کر دیا اب دوسرے ساتھی کو مشتری سے نا چار ہزارہ کرنا پڑے گا تو اس شریک کو بٹوارہ کی مشقت سے بچانے کیلئے حق شفعہ دے دیا گیا۔ لیکن جار میں یہ بات نہیں ہے کیونکہ وہاں اشتراک ہی نہیں ہے اس کو کہا اور یہ یعنی جار نہیں ہے موردِ شرع کے درجہ میں اب اس کی وجہ بتائی۔ اسلئے کہ بنوارہ کی مشقت لازم آتی ہے اس کو اصل میں نہ کہ فرع میں ، اصل سے مراد مور د شرع اور فرع سے مراد غیر مور د شرع یعنی جار، امام شافعی کے دلائل نام ہوئے آگے ہمارے دلائل ہیں۔
شفعہ میں احناف کا نقطہ نظر
ولنا ماروينا ولان ملكه متصل بملک الدخيل اتصال تابيد وقرار فيثبت له حق الشفعة عند وجود المعاوضة بالمال اعتبارا بمورد الشرع وهذا لان الاتصال على هذه الصفة انما انتصب سببا فيه لدفع ضرر الجواران هو مادة المضار على ما عرف وقطع هذه المادة بتملك الاصيل اولى لان الضرر في حقه بازعاجه عن خطة ابائه أقوى وضرر القسمة مشروع لا يصلح علة لتحقيق ضرر غيره
As for establishment (of shuf'ah), it is due to his (peace be upon him) saying: 'Shuf'ah is for a partner who has not divided (the property).' And due to his saying: 'The neighbor of the house is more entitled to the house and land; he shall be waited for, even if he is absent, when their path is one.' And due to his saying: 'The neighbor is more entitled to his suqb.' It was said: O Messenger of Allah, what is suqb? He said: 'His shuf'ah.' And it is narrated: 'The neighbor is more entitled to his shuf'ah.' 
Translation: In any case, establishment (of shuf'ah) is due to the command of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Shuf'ah...' etc., and due to the command of the Prophet: 'The neighbor of the house...' etc., and due to the command of the Prophet: 'The neighbor is more entitled to his suqb.' It was asked: O Messenger of Allah, what is suqb? He said: 'His shuf'ah.' And it is narrated: 'The neighbor is more entitled to his shuf'ah.'
Explanation: Since there are three types of shafi', three hadith are presented for the establishment of shuf'ah for them: (1) Shuf'ah is for a partner who has not divided; this hadith establishes shuf'ah for the partner. (2) The neighbor of the house is more entitled to the house and land; he will be waited for, even if absent, when their path is one; this hadith establishes shuf'ah for the partner in the right of the thing sold. (3) The neighbor is more entitled to his suqb; this hadith establishes shuf'ah for the neighbor. And in one narration: 'The neighbor is more entitled to his shuf'ah.' The author of Hidayah has presented these three hadith.

Shafi'i's view on shuf'ah:
And al-Shafi'i said: There is no shuf'ah by neighborhood because of his (peace be upon him) saying: 'Shuf'ah is only in what has not been divided; when boundaries have been fixed and paths have been separated, then there is no shuf'ah.' And because the right of shuf'ah is deviated from the norms of qiyas, since it involves taking ownership of property from another without his consent. The law (shar') has brought it only for what has not been divided, and this (neighbor) is not in its meaning, because the burden of division (ma'unat al-qismah) falls upon him in the original (asl) and not in the branch (far').
Translation: Al-Shafi'i said: There is no shuf'ah by neighborhood because of the Prophet's saying: 'Shuf'ah is in what has not been divided...' etc., and because the right of shuf'ah is deviated from the ways of qiyas, since it involves owning another's property without his consent, while the law has come with it for undivided property, and this (neighbor) is not in its meaning, because the hardship of division is incumbent on the shafi' in the original (asl) and not in the branch (far').
Explanation: Imam Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) is of the view that shuf'ah is established only for the partner in the property itself; therefore he denies the establishment of shuf'ah due to neighborhood. Then he presents a hadith: 'Shuf'ah is only in property that has not been divided; when boundaries have been fixed and paths have been diverted, then there is no shuf'ah.' In any case, from this hadith it apparently seems that shuf'ah is not established due to neighborhood alone without partnership. This is Shafi'i's transmitted (naqli) proof. His rational (aqli) proof is that the right of shuf'ah is contrary to qiyas, because it involves owning another's property without his consent, and the principle is that whatever is contrary to qiyas remains confined to the scope of the law (mawrid al-shar'). According to Shafi'i, the mawrid al-shar' is only undivided property; the rest cannot be analogized to it. Thus, there is no possibility of establishing shuf'ah for the neighbor. 'And this (neighbor) is not in its meaning' (wa hadha laysa fi ma'naha). That is, Imam Shafi'i says: The real reason (sirr) for shuf'ah is to prevent harm to the owner from having to divide after a partner sells; but the neighbor does not have this because there is no partnership. So the neighbor is not in the category of the mawrid al-shar' because the hardship of division falls upon the original (asl) and not on the branch (far').

Our Hanafi view:
And for us (our proof) is what we have narrated (the hadith), and because his property is connected (muttasil) with the property of the purchaser (al-dukhil) with a connection of permanence and stability; thus the right of shuf'ah is established for him when there is a transaction for money, by analogy (i'tibar) with the mawrid al-shar' (the original case of undivided property). This is because connection (ittisal) in this manner is made a cause (sabab) for preventing the harm of neighbors (daf' dharar al-jiwaran), for it is the source of harms, as is known. Cutting off this source by the owner's (asil) taking possession (tamalluk) is more appropriate, because the harm to him (the neighbor) by being disturbed from his ancestral home is stronger, and the harm of division (qismah) is legislated (mashru') and is not a suitable 'illa (legal cause) for actualizing harm to others.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on the right of pre-emption for neighbors. The Hanafi school proves it with three hadith: (1) 'Shuf'ah is for a partner who has not divided' establishes it for the co-owner; (2) 'The neighbor of the house is more entitled to the house and land, he is waited for even if absent, when their path is one' establishes it for the partner in rights (path/water); (3) 'The neighbor is more entitled to his suqb (shuf'ah)' establishes it for the neighbor. Imam al-Shafi'i opposes the neighbor's shuf'ah, citing a hadith that restricts shuf'ah to undivided property. He argues that shuf'ah is an exception from qiyas (since it forces sale on an unwilling owner) and thus should be confined to the original case (undivided co-ownership). The Hanafi response is twofold: first, they rely on their own hadith; second, they argue by i'tibar (analogy) that permanent connection (ittisal) causes harm (dharar) just as co-ownership does. The harm to a neighbor from a disruptive new owner is even greater than the harm of forced division in co-ownership, so shuf'ah is justified by istihsan (juristic preference). The text concludes that the harm of division is a legislated inconvenience but not a suitable cause to justify harm to others.

Key Terms
السقب (al-suqb): In the hadith, means the right of pre-emption (shuf'ah).
الضرر (al-dharar): Harm; the presence of a harmful neighbor is the basis for establishing shuf'ah.
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning; Shafi'i argues shuf'ah is an exception from qiyas.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference, departing from a clear qiyas due to a stronger evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main rational (aqli) argument of Imam al-Shafi'i against shuf'ah for the neighbor?
A) The neighbor's property is not connected.
B) Shuf'ah is contrary to qiyas and thus confined to undivided property as per the hadith.
C) The neighbor can always buy the property anyway.
D) The hadith about neighbor is weak.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school establishes the neighbor's right of shuf'ah through specific hadith and the principle of istihsan to prevent harm, in contrast to the Shafi'i restriction to co-ownership.

intermediate
10 min
The Hanafi Proof for Shuf'ah by Neighbour and Refutation of Shafi'i's Objection
Dispute between Hanafi and Shafi'i on proof of shuf'ah for neighbour

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi 'illa for shuf'ah and evaluate the Shafi'i objection that shuf'ah for the neighbour contradicts qiyas.

Core Idea
Shuf'ah for the neighbour is proven by permanent connection of ownership, not by harm of division.

This passage defends the Hanafi position that shuf'ah (pre-emption) applies to three categories: partner, participant in rights, and adjacent neighbour. Imam Shafi'i is reported to have argued that shuf'ah for the neighbour is against qiyas because the original case (the partner) is itself an exception. The commentator explains the 'illa of permanent connection and rebuts the alternative 'illa of harm of division.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the three categories of shafi' (sharīk, khalīt, jār) and the Hanafi claim that shuf'ah is proven for all three via hadith and qiyas.
The passage cites three hadith (not quoted) as primary evidence.
2
Identify the opposing view
State Imam Shafi'i's objection: shuf'ah for the neighbour is against qiyas because the original case (partner) is an exception.
This objection is the core of the dispute.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand Shafi'i's reasoning: if the original case is a concession, it cannot be analogized to a new case.
The Hanafi response will show that the 'illa removes this issue.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Explain the Hanafi rebuttal: the 'illa is permanent connection (ittiṣāl ta'bīd wa qarār), which exists in all three; hadith provide explicit proof; shuf'ah is not free but with consideration, so qiyas is valid.
The commentator also rejects the alternative 'illa of harm of division.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: Hanafis grant shuf'ah to the neighbour; Shafi'is (according to this text) do not.
This difference affects property transactions in different legal traditions.

كتاب الشفعة
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۳
ترجمہ اور یہاں دلیل وہ روایات ہیں جو ہم روایت کر چکے ہیں، اور اسلئے کہ شفیع کی ملکیت مشتری کی ملکیت کے ساتھ متصل ہے اتصال تابید و قرار کیسا تھ تو ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ شفیع کیلئے حق شفعہ معاوضہ بالمال کے پائے جانے کے وقت مور د شرع پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے اور یہ حکم اس وجہ سے کہ اس صورت پر اتصال قائم ہوا ہے۔ سبب بن کر مور د شرع میں جوار کے ضرر کو دور کرنے کیلئے اسلئے کہ یہی (جوار) تمام معزتوں کی جڑ ہے جیسا کہ معروف ہے اور اس مادہ ضرور کو ختم کرنا شفیع کے مالک ہونے کے ذریعہ اولیٰ ہے اسلئے کہ ضر شفیع کے حق میں زیادہ قوی ہے اس کے دور کرنے کی وجہ سے اس کے اباء کے خطہ سے اور بٹوارہ کا ضرر مشروع ہے جو اس کے غیر کے ضر رکو ثابت کرنے کیلئے علت بننے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتا۔ تشریح فرماتے ہیں کہ ہم تینوں قسم کے شفیع کیلئے جو شفعہ کے بارے میں تین حدیثیں پیش کر چکے ہیں ۔ جن سے امام شافعی کی تقریر بے جان ہو جاتی ہے کہ مقیس علیہ خلاف قیاس ہے یہ تقریر تو اسی وقت صحیح ہوئی کہ بقیہ دونوں کیلئے احادیث سے شفعہ کا ثبوت نہ ہوتا۔ پھر اگر آپ کی بات کو بالفرض تسلیم کر لیا جائے تو ہم یہ کہیں گے کہ مور د شرع میں شفعہ مفت نہیں ملا بلکہ معاوضہ کے ساتھ ملا ہے یعنی شفیع نے مالی معاوضہ دے کر مشتری سے گھر لیا ہے تو مقیس کے اندر بھی شفعہ کا ثبوت اسی طرح ہونا چاہئے یعنی معاوضہ مال کے ساتھ جبکہ مقیس علیہ کے اندر ثبوت شفعہ خلاف قیاس نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ شفیع کو مقیس علیہ میں شفعہ اسلئے ملا ہے کہ شفیع کی ملکیت مشتری کی ملکیت کے ساتھ متصل ہے اور یہ اتصال عارضی نہیں بلکہ دائمی ہے کیونکہ یہ اپنی زمین کو اٹھا کر لے جائے ایسا نہیں ہو سکتا۔ اس کو مصنف نے اتصال تابید و قرار سے تعبیر کیا ہے اور علت یعنی اتصال مذکور جوار کے اندر بھی موجود ہے لہذا معلوم ہوا کہ منفیس علیہ اور منفیس میں علت جامعہ مشترک ہے پھر اس کو خلاف قیاس کہنا اور باقی کو مور د شرع پر قیاس نہ کرنا کیسے صحیح ہوگا کیونکہ جہاں اس قسم کا اتصال ہوگا تو یہ ثبوت شفعہ کا سبب بنے گا تا کہ ضرر جوار دور ہو سکے اس لئے کہ یہی جوار مضرتوں کی جڑ ہے جیسا کہ برے پڑوسیوں کے درمیان اس کا ہر روز مشاہدہ ہوتا ہے۔ سوال .. جب شفیع کو معضرت ، جوار سے بچانا ہے تو اسکی صورت یہ بھی تو ہوسکتی ہے کہ شفیع کا مکان بھی مشتری کو دلوادیا جائے بجائے اس کے کہ مشتری کا مکان شفیع کو دلوایا جائے؟ جواب تو اس کا جواب دیا و قطع المادة ... الخ سے یعنی اس صورت میں حرج کثیر ہے کیونکہ شفیع کو اس کے آباء واجداد کے گھر سے علیحدہ کرنا لازم آتا ہے اسلئے آسان صورت وہی ہے کہ شفیع کو مشتری کا مکان دلوا دیا جائے ، پھر وضرر القسمہ الخ سے امام شافعی کا جواب ہے کہ آپ نے علت شفعہ ضر ر قسمت بیان کی ہے۔ محل تامل ہے کیونکہ ضر ر قسمت تو امر مشروع ہے لہذا اگر دو شریکوں میں سے کوئی قسمت کا دعوی کرے تو بڑارہ کر دیا جاتا ہے معلوم ہوا کہ امر مشروع دوسرے کو نقصان پہنچانے کی علت نہیں بن سکتا بلکہ علت اتصال تابید ہی ہے جیسا کہ ہم ذکر کر چکے ہیں۔ یہاں تک کہ مصنف نے ثبوت پر گفتگو کی ہے آگے ترتیب پر گفتگو فرمائیں گے۔
Book of Shuf'ah. Ashraf al-Bidayah Urdu Sharh Hidayah Volume 13. Translation: And here the proof are the narrations we have narrated, and because the ownership of the shafi' is connected to the ownership of the purchaser with a permanent and stable connection, then shuf'ah will be established. For the shafi', the right of shuf'ah when consideration of wealth is found, by making qiyas on the case of the Lawgiver, and this ruling because in this situation the connection is established, serving as a cause to remove the harm of adjacency in the case of the Lawgiver, because adjacency is the root of all harms, as is known; and to eliminate this harm by making the shafi' owner is better because the harm is stronger regarding the shafi', due to the fact that it forces him from his ancestral home, and the harm of division is legislated, which does not have the capacity to be a cause that establishes harm to others. Explanation: They say that we have presented three hadith for three types of shafi' regarding shuf'ah, which make Imam Shafi'i's argument invalid that the analogized case is against qiyas; this argument would only be valid if there were no hadith proof for the other two. Then if your statement is hypothetically accepted, we would say that shuf'ah in the case of the Lawgiver was not obtained for free but with consideration, i.e., the shafi' took the house from the purchaser by paying monetary consideration, so the proof of shuf'ah in the analogized case should be in the same way, i.e., with monetary consideration, while in the analogized case the proof of shuf'ah is not against qiyas. Because the shafi' received shuf'ah in the analogized case due to his ownership being connected to the purchaser's ownership, and this connection is not temporary but permanent, because he cannot pick up his land and move it. The author has expressed this as a permanent and stable connection. And this cause, that connection, also exists in adjacency; therefore it is known that the comprehensive cause is common between the analogized case (maqis 'alayh) and the analogized case (maqis). Then how can it be correct to say it is against qiyas and not make qiyas on the case of the Lawgiver for the other? Because wherever this type of connection exists, it will become a cause for proof of shuf'ah so that the harm of adjacency can be removed, because adjacency is the root of harms, as is observed daily between bad neighbors. Question: When the shafi' is to be saved from the harm of adjacency, it is also possible that the shafi''s house be given to the purchaser instead of the purchaser's house being given to the shafi'? Answer: The answer is given by 'wa qat' al-maddah...' i.e., in that case there is great difficulty because it necessitates separating the shafi' from his ancestral home; therefore the easier way is to give the shafi' the purchaser's house. Then 'wa darrar al-qismah...' is a response to Imam Shafi'i that you have made the harm of division the cause of shuf'ah. This is questionable because the harm of division is a legislated matter; if one of two partners demands division, it is done. So it is known that a legislated matter cannot be a cause that causes harm to another. Rather the cause is the permanent connection, as we have mentioned. Up to here, the author has discussed proof; next he will discuss order of priority.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage presents the inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam Shafi'i regarding the proof for the right of pre-emption (shuf'ah) by a neighbour (jār). The Hanafi position, as expounded by the commentator, is that shuf'ah is established by three hadith transmitted for the three types of claimant: partner in the property (sharīk), partner in rights (khalīt), and adjacent neighbour (jār). Imam Shafi'i is reported to have said that shuf'ah for the neighbour is against qiyas because the original case (the partner) is itself an exception. The commentator rebuts this by arguing that the 'illa (effective cause) for shuf'ah is the permanent and stable connection of ownership (ittiṣāl ta'bīd wa qarār), which exists in both the partner and the neighbour. Additionally, shuf'ah in the original case is not free but involves consideration, so qiyas is valid. The commentator also addresses a hypothetical: why not move the shafi' instead? The answer is that it causes greater hardship to remove the shafi' from his ancestral home. Finally, Imam Shafi'i's alternative 'illa of harm of division (ḍarar al-qismah) is rejected because division is a legislated act and cannot be used as a cause to harm another. The correct 'illa is the permanent connection. The passage sets the foundation for the rest of the book of shuf'ah.

Key Terms
شفعة (shuf'ah): The right of pre-emption; the right of a co-owner or neighbour to purchase a sold property by paying its price to the buyer.
اتصال تأبيد و قرار (ittiṣāl ta'bīd wa qarār): Permanent and stable connection of ownership; the cause ('illa) for shuf'ah according to the Hanafis.
جوار (jiwār): Adjacency; being a neighbour; the relationship that gives rise to shuf'ah for the neighbour.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the effective cause ('illa) for shuf'ah according to the Hanafi school as presented in this passage?
A) The harm of division (ḍarar al-qismah)
B) The permanent connection of ownership (ittiṣāl ta'bīd wa qarār)
C) The monetary consideration paid by the buyer
D) The hadith themselves

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school extends shuf'ah to the neighbour based on the permanent connection of ownership, supported by hadith and qiyas, rebutting the Shafi'i objection that it is against qiyas.

Order of Priority in Shuf'ah: Sharīk, Khalīt, Jār
Establishes order and proofs for shuf'ah claimants

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi order of priority in shuf'ah, define the three categories of claimants, and explain the proofs from hadith and rational argument.

Core Idea
The partner in the property itself has the strongest claim, followed by the partner in rights, then the neighbour.

What determines who has the strongest right to pre-empt a sale? The Hanafi school relies on a hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) that establishes a clear hierarchy: the partner in the property itself (sharīk) is most entitled, then the partner in appurtenant rights (khalīt), then the neighbour (jār). This lesson unpacks the linguistic and rational basis for this order, and also addresses the Shafi'i view that the harm of division (ḍarar al-qismah) serves as the cause of shuf'ah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
Distinguish between sharīk (partner in the property itself), khalīt (partner in rights such as right of way or water), and shafi' (neighbour) as defined in the passage.
2
State the order from the hadith
Quote the hadith: 'al-sharīku aḥaqqu min al-khalīṭi, wa al-khalīṭu aḥaqqu min al-shafī'' and note the explicit ranking.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but accepted in fiqh.
3
Analyze the rational proof
Understand why the sharīk's connection is strongest (in every part), then the khalīt's (in benefits), then the neighbour's (mere adjacency). Preference is based on the strength of the cause (sabab).
4
Examine the Shafi'i position
Imam Shafi'i considered the harm of division (ḍarar al-qismah) as the cause of shuf'ah. The Hanafi response is that it is not a valid cause but can serve as a weight (murajjih) to prefer one claimant.
This clarifies why the sharīk is preferred even if the harm of division is similar.
5
Apply the order
In a given scenario with multiple claimants, determine who has the strongest right to shuf'ah based on the hierarchy.
The order is sharīk > khalīt > jār.

Source Text

پھر اسکے اوپر دلیل عقلی پیش کرتے ہیں کہ مبیع میں جس کی شرکت ہے اس کا اتصال اور وں سے قوی ہے کیونکہ یہ اتصال ہر ہر جزء کے اندر ہے اور اس کے بعد حقوق کا اتصال جار کے اتصال سے قومی ہے کیونکہ یہ اتصال منافع ملک میں اتصال ہے اور یہ اصول مسلم ہے کہ 3
سبب کی قوت کی وجہ سے ترجیح حاصل ہوتی ہے اور سبب کی قوت اول میں ہے پھر ثانی میں، لہذا شفعہ ملنے میں بھی یہی ترتیب جاری ہوگی۔ ولان ضرر القسمة ... الخ - سے فرماتے ہیں کہ امام شافعی نے ضرر قسمت کو علت شفعہ قرار دیا تھا مگر وہ علت ثابت نہ ہوسکا لیکن ضرر قسمت مربح تو ہو سکتا ہے یعنی جس صورت میں ضرر قسمت لازم آئے اس کو دوسروں سے متقدم رکھا جائے اور وہ شریک فی معین المبیع ہے۔
Deduction of the order of shuf'ah from the blessed hadith. As for the order, it is due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'The partner has more right than the khalīt, and the khalīt has more right than the shafi'.' So the partner is in the very thing sold, the khalīt is in the rights of the thing sold, and the shafi' is the neighbour. And because the connection through partnership in the sold property is stronger, since it is in every part, and after that the connection in the rights, because it is partnership in the utilities of ownership, and preference is realized by the strength of the cause. And because the harm of division, if it is not valid as a cause, it is valid as a weight (murajjih). Translation: And in any case, the order is because of the Prophet's statement that the partner is more entitled than the khalīt, and the khalīt is more entitled than the shafi'. So the partner is in the property itself, the khalīt is in the rights of the property, and the shafi' is the neighbour. And because the connection through partnership in the property is stronger, since it is in every part, and after that the connection in the rights, because it is connection in the benefits of ownership, and preference is realized by the strength of the cause. And because the harm of division, if it is not valid as a cause, it is valid as a weight (murajjih). Explanation: In the previous discussion, it was said that this statement benefits two things: proof and order. So here they expound the second thing, and present the hadith as evidence: the partner is more deserving than the khalīt, and the khalīt is more deserving than the shafi'. Now we will explain what is meant by sharīk, khalīt, and shafi': he said that the one who has a share in the property itself is called a sharīk, the one who has a share in the rights of the property is called a khalīt, and the neighbour is called a shafi'. Then they present a rational proof: the connection of the one who has partnership in the property is stronger than others because it is in every part, and after that the connection in rights is stronger than the connection of the neighbour, because it is connection in the benefits of ownership. And it is a settled principle that preference is obtained by the strength of the cause, and the strength of the cause is in the first, then in the second. Therefore, the same order will apply in receiving shuf'ah. 'Wa lan darrar al-qismah...' he says: Imam Shafi'i had made the harm of division the cause of shuf'ah, but that could not be established as a cause; however, the harm of division can be a weight (murajjih), i.e., in the situation where the harm of division is necessary, that one should be given precedence over others, and that is the partner in the specified property.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage establishes the order of priority among claimants of shuf'ah. It quotes the hadith: 'The partner has more right than the khalīt, and the khalīt has more right than the shafi'.' The commentator defines the three categories: sharīk is a partner in the very property (nɑfs al-mabī'), khalīt is a partner in the appurtenant rights (such as right of way or water), and shafi' is the adjacent neighbour (jār). Then rational proof is given: the connection of a partner is the strongest because it covers every part of the property; the khalīt's connection is in the benefits and utilities; the neighbour's connection is mere adjacency. Preference is based on the strength of the cause. Finally, the passage addresses Imam Shafi'i's view: he considered the harm of division (ḍarar al-qismah) as the cause. The commentator says that while this harm is not sufficient as an independent cause, it can serve as a weight (murajjih) to prefer one claimant over another, specifically the partner in the specified property. Thus, the order is established by both transmitted text and rational reasoning.

Key Terms
شريك (sharīk): A partner in the property itself (nɑfs al-mabī'); has a share in the very thing sold.
خليط (khalīt): A partner in the appurtenant rights of the property, such as right of way (ṭarīq) or water (shurb).
مرجح (murajjih): A weight or preponderant factor that does not serve as an independent cause but tips the scale in favor of one claimant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The khalīt has a stronger claim than the shafi'
B) The shafi' has a stronger claim than the khalīt
C) They have equal claim
D) Neither has a claim

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi order of shuf'ah is proven by hadith and reason: sharīk precedes khalīt, and khalīt precedes the neighbour; the harm of division is only a weight, not a cause.

Order of Priority in Shuf'ah: Partner Excludes Others
Ruling that with a partner in the property, others have no shuf'ah unless he forfeits

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the order of priority in shuf'ah (preemption) under Hanafi fiqh and identify who is excluded when a partner in the property itself exists.

Core Idea
A partner in the property excludes all others from preemption; only if he forfeits do the next in line get the right.

This lesson clarifies the Hanafi ruling on who has the right of shuf'ah (preemption) when multiple parties have an interest in the property. The key point is that the partner in the property itself (sharīk fī nafs al-mabī') has the strongest claim. The partner in rights (khalīt) and the adjacent neighbour (jār) are excluded unless the primary partner forfeits. Understanding this order prevents incorrect claims and wasted legal effort.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories of potential claimants
List the three groups mentioned: 1) partner in the property itself, 2) partner in rights (path/water), 3) adjacent neighbour.
The partner in property is called 'sharīk fī al-raqaba' or 'sharīk fī nafs al-mabī'.
2
Understand the order of priority
The partner in property is given precedence over all others. The partner in rights and neighbour have no claim while he exists and does not forfeit.
This order is established by the text: 'he is given precedence'.
3
Know the effect of forfeiture
If the partner in property forfeits his right, then the partner in rights gets the claim; if he also forfeits, then the neighbour gets it.
The text says: 'if he forgoes, then the shuf'ah is for the partner in the path; if he forgoes, then the neighbour takes it'.
4
Define the eligible neighbour
The neighbour must be adjacent (mulāṣiq) to the property and have his door in a different alley (not sharing the same entrance).
This distinguishes from a partner in the entrance, who may have a different status.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi variation
Abu Yusuf may have a different definition; the text is cut off, but the main ruling (zahir al-riwayah) is as stated.
The mufta bihi is the order given in al-Hidayah and al-Quduri.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شریک فی نفس السمیع کی موجودگی میں شریک فی الحقوق اور جار شفعہ سے محروم ہوں گے
قال وليس للشريك فى الطريق والشرب والجار شفعة مع الخليط فى الرقبة لما ذكرنا انه مقدم ترجمہ اور نہیں ہے راستہ اور شرب میں شریک کیلئے اور جار کیلئے شفعہ خلیط فی الرقبہ کے ساتھ بوجہ اس دلیل کے جو ہم ذکر کر چکے ہیں
کہ یہ مقدم ہے۔ تشریح جو بات صاحب ہدایہ بیان کر چکے ہیں اسی کو امام قدوری اس طرح بیان فرمارہے ہیں کہ شریک فی نفس السمیع کے ہوتے ہوئے شریک فی الحقوق اور جار کو شفعہ نہیں ملے گا جس کے دلائل گزار چکے ہیں۔
اول کی دست برداری کی صورت میں دوسرے حقدار کو شفع کا حق مل جائے گا، جار کا مصداق
قال فان سلم فالشفعة للشريك في الطريق فان سلم اخذها الجار لما بينا من الترتيب والمراد بهذا الجار الملاصق وهو الذى على ظهر الدار المشفوعة وبابه في سكة اخرى وعن أبي يوسف ان مع وجود
In the presence of a partner in the property itself, the partner in rights and the neighbour are deprived of shuf'ah. He said: And there is no shuf'ah for the partner in the path (right of way) and water (right of irrigation), and for the neighbour, along with the khalīt in the substance (of the property), because of what we have mentioned that he (the partner in substance) is given precedence. Translation: And there is no shuf'ah for the partner in the path and water, and for the neighbour, with the khalīt in the substance, due to the proof we have mentioned that he is given precedence. Explanation: What the author of al-Hidayah has mentioned, Imam al-Quduri expresses as: When a partner in the property itself exists, the partner in rights and the neighbour will not receive shuf'ah; the proofs have been presented. In case of forfeiture by the first, the second entitled person will receive the right of shuf'ah. He said: If he forgoes, then the shuf'ah is for the partner in the path; if he forgoes, then the neighbour takes it, due to the order we have explained. And what is meant by this neighbour is the adjacent one, the one who is at the back of the house subject to shuf'ah and whose door is in a different alley. And from Abu Yusuf, that with the existence... [incomplete]
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage states a clear ruling: when there is a partner in the property itself (sharīk fī nafs al-mabī'), the partner in rights (sharīk fī al-ṭarīq wa al-shurb) and the adjacent neighbour (jār) have no right of shuf'ah. The commentator explains that this is based on the order of priority established earlier: the partner in the property is given precedence. However, if the partner forgoes his right, the next in order (the partner in rights) gets the claim, and if he also forgoes, then the neighbour gets it. The neighbour referred to is the one whose property is adjacent (mulāṣiq) and whose door is in a different alley, i.e., not sharing the same entrance. The passage ends with a mention of Abu Yusuf's view, but the text is cut off; the full view of Abu Yusuf likely concerns whether the neighbour qualifies when the door is in the same alley or similar.

Key Terms
شريك في الطريق والشرب (sharīk fī al-ṭarīq wa al-shurb): A partner in the right of way and water (easement rights); one who shares these appurtenances but not the property itself.
جار ملاصق (jār mulāṣiq): The adjacent neighbour whose property touches the property subject to shuf'ah and whose door is in a different alley.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Only the neighbour
C) Both the partner in rights and the neighbour
D) None are excluded

Key Takeaway
A partner in the property has the strongest claim to shuf'ah; the partner in rights and the adjacent neighbour are only eligible after his forfeiture.
