Priority of Co-owner over Neighbour in Shuf'ah
Explains that a co-owner in a part of a property is preferred over a neighbour for shuf'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the priority of a co-owner over a neighbour in shuf'ah and apply it to cases where the co-owner has a share in only a part of the property.

Core Idea
A co-owner in any part of the property is preferred over a neighbour for shuf'ah, even if the sold part is not his share.

Shuf'ah (pre-emption) is a right that can be exercised by co-owners and neighbours. However, when a co-owner and a neighbour both claim the right, who takes priority? The Hanafi school, based on the stronger connection of ownership, gives priority to the co-owner even if he only owns a share in a wall. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties
Recognize that there are two potential claimants: a co-owner (sharīk) who owns any share, even partial, and a neighbour (jār) who owns no share but is adjacent to the property.
The co-owner's share can be in a specific part like a room, a wall, or any portion.
2
Determine the sold property
Consider whether the sold property is the part where the co-owner has a share or a different part. The ruling applies in both scenarios.
The sold property could be the entire house or a specific unit.
3
Apply the principle of stronger connection
The co-owner is preferred because his connection to the property (ittisāl) is stronger due to ownership, and the entire property is considered one unit (al-buq'ah wāhida).
The proof is talil: the strength of the cause gives preference.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf has two narrations; the more correct one (aṣaḥḥ al-riwāyatayn) gives priority to the co-owner. The mufta bihi position adopts this narration.
Al-Hidayah explicitly mentions this tarjih.
5
Derive the ruling
In both scenarios (sold part is co-owner's share or not), the co-owner takes priority over the neighbour.
The ruling applies to shuf'ah in immovable property.

Source Text

عـلـى الـجـار في المنزل وكذا على الجار في بقية الدار في اصح الروايتين عن أبي يوسف لان اتصاله أقوى والبقعة واحدة ترجمہ اور شریک فی البدیع کبھی شریک ہوتا ہے گھر کے بعض حصہ میں، جیسے گھر کی معین منزل میں یا گھر کی معین دیوار میں اور یہ شریک مذکور (مقدم ہے منزل میں جار پر اور ایسے ہی دار کے بقیہ میں جار پر ابو یوسف سے دو روایتوں میں سے اصح روایت کے مطابق اسلئے کہ اس کا اتصال زیادہ قوی ہے اور بقعہ واحد ہے۔ تشریح دار جس کو حویلی کہتے ہیں اور مظفر نگر کے دیہاتوں میں اس کو بگڑ کہتے ہیں جس کے اندر پھر مختلف لوگوں کے گھر ہوتے ہیں اس کو منزل کہا جاتا ہے پھر اس میں ہر کمرہ بیت کہلاتا ہے۔ اب مسئلہ دیکھئے ایک حویلی میں چند منزلیں ہیں اور سب کا مالک ایک ہے۔ مگر ایک منزل کے اندر صرف ایک شخص کا اشتراک ہے یا اس میں بھی اشتراک نہیں بلکہ صرف دیوار میں کسی کا اشتراک ہے۔ اور دوسرا شخص اور ہے جو اس دار کا پڑوی ہے تو چونکہ اول خواہ ایک حصہ میں شریک ہے مگر ہے تو شریک ۔ اس وجہ سے شریک کو جار پر مقدم رکھا جائے گا۔ خواہ وہ منزل فروخت ہو جس میں اس کا اشتراک ہو یا وہ دوسری منزل فروخت ہو جس میں اس کا اشتراک نہیں ہے۔ دونوں صورتوں میں اس کو جار پر مقدم رکھا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اگر چہ اس منزل میں اس کا حصہ نہیں ہے لیکن اس دار کی دوسری منزل یا کسی دیوار میں اس کا اشتراک تو ہے اور جار کا کچھ بھی اشتراک نہیں ہے اور شریک جار پر مقدم ہوا ہی کرتا ہے جیسا کہ ماقبل میں معلوم ہو چکا ہے۔ لان اتصال الخ - اسلئے کہ شریک کا اتصال جار کے اتصال سے قوی ہے اور قوت سبب سے ترجیح حاصل ہوتی ہے۔ ( کمامر) اور بقعہ واحد ہے یعنی سارا دار ایک ہے لہذا دار کی کسی منزل میں اس کا اشتراک ہوا تو دار میں اشتراک ہے اور شریک مقدم ہوا ہی کرتا ہے۔
Upon the neighbour in the dwelling, and similarly upon the neighbour in the remainder of the house, in the more correct of the two narrations from Abu Yusuf, because his connection is stronger and the space is one. Translation: And a co-owner in the property is sometimes a co-owner in a part of the house, like in a specific dwelling or a specific wall, and this co-owner mentioned is given priority over the neighbour in the dwelling, and likewise over the neighbour in the rest of the house, according to the more correct narration from Abu Yusuf, because his connection is stronger and the space is one. Explanation: A house that is called a courtyard, and in the villages of Muzaffarnagar it is called 'bighara', inside which there are various people's houses, that is called a dwelling, then each room is called a room. Now see the issue: in one courtyard there are several dwellings and all are owned by one person, but in one dwelling only one person has a share, or not even that, but only in a wall someone has a share. And another person is a neighbour of this house. Since the first is a co-owner, albeit in a part, he is still a co-owner. For this reason, the co-owner is given priority over the neighbour. Whether the dwelling sold is the one in which he has a share or another dwelling in which he has no share, in both cases he is given priority over the neighbour. Because even though he has no share in that dwelling, he does have a share in another dwelling or a wall of the house, and the neighbour has no share at all, and the co-owner is always given priority over the neighbour, as has been learned previously. 'Because his connection etc.' means that the co-owner's connection is stronger than the neighbour's connection, and preference is attained due to the strength of the cause. And the space is one, meaning the entire house is one. Therefore, if he has a share in any dwelling of the house, he has a share in the house, and the co-owner is given priority.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from Al-Hidayah explaining the priority of a co-owner over a neighbour in the right of shuf'ah (pre-emption). The author begins by stating that a co-owner in a specific part of a property, such as a room or a wall, is given preference over a neighbour when a part of that property is sold. This applies even if the sold part is not the one in which he has a share, because his connection to the property is stronger due to existing co-ownership. The proof given is that his connection is stronger and the entire property is considered one unit. The commentary elaborates with an example: if a courtyard has multiple dwellings, and a person owns a share in only one wall or one dwelling, he takes priority over a neighbour who has no share at all, whether the sold dwelling is the one with his share or another. This is because the co-owner's right of shuf'ah arises from the continuity of his ownership, which is stronger than the neighbour's mere adjacency. The ruling follows the more correct narration from Abu Yusuf, indicating an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the matter, but the adopted position is that the co-owner is preferred.

Key Terms
شريكة (sharīk): A co-owner in the property, even if only in a part.
جار (jār): A neighbour who does not own any share in the property.
شفعة (shuf‘ah): The right of pre-emption to purchase a sold property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a house has two apartments, and A owns a share in the wall of the house while B is a neighbour of the whole house, and the second apartment (in which A has no share) is sold, who has the right of shuf'ah?
A) A, because he is a co-owner
B) B, because he is a neighbour and the sold apartment is not A's share
C) Both have an equal right
D) Neither has the right

Key Takeaway
A co-owner, even with a share in only a part of the property, is preferred over a neighbour in the right of shuf'ah for the entire property, because his connection is stronger and the property is one unit.

Definition of Specific Pathway for Shuf'ah
Defines specific pathway for shuf'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of a specific pathway (tarīq khāṣṣ) and apply it to determine whether shuf'ah rights arise from co-ownership in a pathway.

Core Idea
A specific pathway is a non-through road — only private dead-ends give shuf'ah rights.

The right of pre-emption (shuf'ah) arises from co-ownership in property, including shared pathways. However, not every shared pathway qualifies. The Hanafi school distinguishes between specific (khāṣṣ) and general (ʿāmm) pathways. This lesson examines the definition of a specific pathway as stated in the text, which is foundational for applying shuf'ah in real estate disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the requirement for shuf'ah
The passage states that the pathway must be specific for shuf'ah to be established through co-ownership. Start by noting this condition.
Co-ownership in a public road does not give shuf'ah.
2
Extract the definition of specific pathway
The author defines the specific pathway as 'that it is not a through road' (an lā yakūna nāfidhan). This means it is a dead-end or private road, not a thoroughfare.
The Arabic term 'ghayr nāfidh' implies a closed or non-penetrating road.
3
Contrast with general pathway
If the road is a through road (nāfidh), it is general and does not qualify. Understand that the opposite of specific is general, which includes public streets and highways.
4
Apply to a scenario
Imagine a shared driveway leading to two houses with a dead-end. This is a specific pathway. A public street shared by many is general. Determine which gives shuf'ah rights.
Only the dead-end driveway qualifies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم لابد ان يكون الطريق او الشرب خاصاحتى يستحق الشفعة بالشركة فيه فالطريق الخاص ان لا يكون نافذا والشرب الخاص ان يكون نهرا لاتجرى فيه السفن وما تجرى فيه فهو عام وهذا عند ابي حنيفة ومحمد وعن أبي يوسف ان الخاص ان يكون نهرا يسقى منه قراحان او ثلثة وما زاد على ذلك فهو عام ترجمہ پھر ضروری ہے یہ کہ طریق یا شرب خاص ہوں ۔ یہاں تک کہ شفیع اس میں شرکت کی وجہ سے شفعہ کا مستحق ہو پس خاص راستہ یہ ہے کہ وہ نافذ نہ ہو اور شرب خاص یہ ہے کہ ایسی نہر ہو جس میں کشتیاں نہ چل سکیں اور جس میں چل سکیں تو وہ عام ہے اور یہ ابو حنیفہ اور محمد کے نزدیک ہے اور ابو یوسف سے منقول ہے کہ خاص یہ ہے کہ ایسی نہر ہو جس سے دویا تین باغ سیراب کئے جاسکیں اور جو اس سے زیادہ ہو تو وہ عام ہے۔ تشریح جہاں راستہ اور شرب کا اتحاد بتایا ہے تو اس میں عموم نہیں بلکہ خاص شرب و طریق مراد ہے ورنہ جی ٹی روڈ میں اشتراک اور گنگا میں اشتراک کی وجہ سے طریق اور شرب خاص نہیں ہوتا اور اس اتحاد کی وجہ سے شفعہ نہیں ملے گا۔ پھر مصنف نے طریق خاص اور شرب خاص کی تعریف فرمائی یعنی جب راستہ نافذ ہو عام راستہ نہ ہو اور راستہ آر پار نہ ہو تو وہ طریق خاص ہے ورنہ عام ہے۔ اور مثلاً دو آدمیوں کا کھیت کے پانی میں اشتر اس سے تو اس کا مطلب یہ نہیں کہ جس نہر سے یہ سیراب کرتا ہے وہ بھی کرے۔ اگر دونوں موری جدا گانہ ہوں تو شرب خاص کی تعریف طرفین نے یہ کی کہ ایسی نہ ہو جس میں کشتیاں چلتی ہوں ورنہ یہ عام شرب کہلائے گا۔ اور امام ابو یوسف نے شرب خاص کی تعریف یوں کی ہے کہ اس سے دو یا تین باغات یا چک بھرے جاتے ہوں اور اگر اس سے زیادہ باغات اس سے سیراب کئے جاتے ہوں تو یہ شرب عام ہے۔ تنبیہ جس نہر میں لوگ اپنی اپنی باری مقرر کئے ہیں وہ نہر صغیر ہے ورنہ نہر کبیر ہے اور بعض فقہاء نے اس کو ہر زمانہ کے مجتہد کی رائے پر چھوڑ دیا اور میٹی نے اس کو اشبہ کہا ہے تو ہمارے دیار میں اجتہایہ سے نکلنے والی نالی شرب خاص کہلائے گی اور اجیہا یہ شرب عام کہلائے گا۔ اور طریق خاص وہ کہلائے گا جس کو کوئی بند نہ کر سکے۔
Then it is necessary that the pathway or the water channel be specific so that the right of pre-emption is established through co-ownership in it. The specific pathway is that it is not a through road. The specific water channel is that it is a river in which ships do not sail, and that in which they sail is general. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. And from Abu Yusuf it is narrated that the specific is that it is a river from which two or three gardens are irrigated, and what exceeds that is general. Translation: Then it is necessary that the pathway or the water channel be specific, so that the pre-emptor is entitled to shuf'ah due to co-ownership in it. So the specific pathway is that it is not a through road, and the specific water channel is that it is a river in which ships cannot sail, and that in which they can sail is general. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. And from Abu Yusuf it is narrated that the specific is that it is a river from which two or three gardens can be irrigated, and what exceeds that is general. Explanation: Where it is stated that the pathway and the water channel are shared, it refers to specific ones, not general ones. Otherwise, co-ownership in a highway or the Ganges does not constitute specific pathway or water channel, and due to that shared use, shuf'ah will not be established. Then the author defined the specific pathway and specific water channel: when the road is not a through road and is not a public road, it is a specific pathway; otherwise it is general. For example, two people share water for their fields, but this does not mean that the river from which one irrigates is the same as the other's. If the water channels are separate, then the definition of specific water channel according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that it is a river in which ships do not sail; otherwise it is called general water channel. And Imam Abu Yusuf defined it as a river from which two or three gardens or plots are irrigated, and if more than that are irrigated, then it is general water channel. Note: A river in which people have fixed their own turns is a small river; otherwise it is a large river. Some jurists left this to the judgement of the mujtahid of each era, and al-Mutee' deemed it more appropriate. So in our country, a canal that comes out of the main canal is called a specific water channel, and the main canal is called a general water channel. And a specific pathway is that which no one can block.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage defines the conditions for shuf'ah based on shared pathway or water channel. The author states that for shuf'ah to be valid, the co-ownership must be in a 'specific' (khas) pathway or water channel, not a public one. A specific pathway is one that is not a through road (nafidh), meaning it is a dead-end lane. A specific water channel is defined differently by Abu Hanifa and Muhammad compared to Abu Yusuf. According to the first two, it is a river or canal that does not allow ships to sail; if ships can sail, it is a general water channel (sharb 'amm). Abu Yusuf defines it as a water channel that irrigates only two or three gardens; if it irrigates more than that, it is general. The commentary explains that shared use of a public road or a large river like the Ganges does not create a right of shuf'ah. The passage also notes that the specific pathway is one that cannot be blocked by anyone, emphasizing its private nature. There is an important note that the determination of 'specific' may vary with time and place, as some jurists leave it to the mujtahid's discretion. This ruling is essential for understanding when shuf'ah can be claimed through shared access rights.

Key Terms
طريق خاص (ṭarīq khāṣṣ): A specific pathway that is not a through road (ghayr nāfidh).
شرب خاص (sharb khāṣṣ): A specific water channel for irrigation, defined variously by different Hanafi imams.
شفعة (shuf‘ah): Right of pre-emption in property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi condition for a pathway to be considered specific (khāṣṣ) for shuf'ah?
A) It must be paved.
B) It must be used by two or more people.
C) It must not be a through road.
D) It must be owned by the government.

Key Takeaway
A pathway must be non-through (private dead-end) to qualify as specific and give shuf'ah rights.

Definition of Specific Water Channel and Intra-Madhhab Ikhtilaf
Defines specific water channel with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi definitions of a specific water channel (sharb khāṣṣ) and determine the practical difference between them regarding shuf'ah rights.

Core Idea
A water channel is specific if ships cannot sail (Abu Hanifa) OR if it irrigates only 2-3 gardens (Abu Yusuf) – the ikhtilaf affects shuf'ah claims.

Just as with pathways, the right of pre-emption (shuf'ah) through a shared water channel requires that the channel be specific (khāṣṣ). However, the Hanafi imams differed on how to define a specific water channel. This lesson unpacks the two definitions from the text – one based on navigability (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) and one based on the extent of irrigation (Abu Yusuf) – and shows how each leads to different practical outcomes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition for shuf'ah via water channel
The passage states that the water channel (sharb) must be specific. Note this condition.
2
Extract the definition of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad
They define specific water channel as a river in which ships do not sail. If ships sail, it is general (public).
Criterion: navigability.
3
Extract the definition of Abu Yusuf
He defines it as a river that irrigates only two or three gardens; if more, it is general.
Criterion: limited benefit.
4
Compare the two definitions
Under Abu Hanifa, a canal that is not navigable but irrigates many fields is still specific, so shuf'ah applies. Under Abu Yusuf, if it irrigates more than three gardens, it is general and no shuf'ah.
The conflict point: navigability vs irrigation extent.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The text presents Abu Hanifa's view first and the commentary uses it, suggesting it is the relied upon position.
The ikhtilaf is acknowledged but the majority view is preferred.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم لابد ان يكون الطريق او الشرب خاصاحتى يستحق الشفعة بالشركة فيه فالطريق الخاص ان لا يكون نافذا والشرب الخاص ان يكون نهرا لاتجرى فيه السفن وما تجرى فيه فهو عام وهذا عند ابي حنيفة ومحمد وعن أبي يوسف ان الخاص ان يكون نهرا يسقى منه قراحان او ثلثة وما زاد على ذلك فهو عام ترجمہ پھر ضروری ہے یہ کہ طریق یا شرب خاص ہوں ۔ یہاں تک کہ شفیع اس میں شرکت کی وجہ سے شفعہ کا مستحق ہو پس خاص راستہ یہ ہے کہ وہ نافذ نہ ہو اور شرب خاص یہ ہے کہ ایسی نہر ہو جس میں کشتیاں نہ چل سکیں اور جس میں چل سکیں تو وہ عام ہے اور یہ ابو حنیفہ اور محمد کے نزدیک ہے اور ابو یوسف سے منقول ہے کہ خاص یہ ہے کہ ایسی نہر ہو جس سے دویا تین باغ سیراب کئے جاسکیں اور جو اس سے زیادہ ہو تو وہ عام ہے۔ تشریح جہاں راستہ اور شرب کا اتحاد بتایا ہے تو اس میں عموم نہیں بلکہ خاص شرب و طریق مراد ہے ورنہ جی ٹی روڈ میں اشتراک اور گنگا میں اشتراک کی وجہ سے طریق اور شرب خاص نہیں ہوتا اور اس اتحاد کی وجہ سے شفعہ نہیں ملے گا۔ پھر مصنف نے طریق خاص اور شرب خاص کی تعریف فرمائی یعنی جب راستہ نافذ ہو عام راستہ نہ ہو اور راستہ آر پار نہ ہو تو وہ طریق خاص ہے ورنہ عام ہے۔ اور مثلاً دو آدمیوں کا کھیت کے پانی میں اشتر اس سے تو اس کا مطلب یہ نہیں کہ جس نہر سے یہ سیراب کرتا ہے وہ بھی کرے۔ اگر دونوں موری جدا گانہ ہوں تو شرب خاص کی تعریف طرفین نے یہ کی کہ ایسی نہ ہو جس میں کشتیاں چلتی ہوں ورنہ یہ عام شرب کہلائے گا۔ اور امام ابو یوسف نے شرب خاص کی تعریف یوں کی ہے کہ اس سے دو یا تین باغات یا چک بھرے جاتے ہوں اور اگر اس سے زیادہ باغات اس سے سیراب کئے جاتے ہوں تو یہ شرب عام ہے۔ تنبیہ جس نہر میں لوگ اپنی اپنی باری مقرر کئے ہیں وہ نہر صغیر ہے ورنہ نہر کبیر ہے اور بعض فقہاء نے اس کو ہر زمانہ کے مجتہد کی رائے پر چھوڑ دیا اور میٹی نے اس کو اشبہ کہا ہے تو ہمارے دیار میں اجتہایہ سے نکلنے والی نالی شرب خاص کہلائے گی اور اجیہا یہ شرب عام کہلائے گا۔ اور طریق خاص وہ کہلائے گا جس کو کوئی بند نہ کر سکے۔
Then it is necessary that the pathway or the water channel be specific so that the right of pre-emption is established through co-ownership in it. The specific pathway is that it is not a through road. The specific water channel is that it is a river in which ships do not sail, and that in which they sail is general. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. And from Abu Yusuf it is narrated that the specific is that it is a river from which two or three gardens are irrigated, and what exceeds that is general. Translation: Then it is necessary that the pathway or the water channel be specific, so that the pre-emptor is entitled to shuf'ah due to co-ownership in it. So the specific pathway is that it is not a through road, and the specific water channel is that it is a river in which ships cannot sail, and that in which they can sail is general. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. And from Abu Yusuf it is narrated that the specific is that it is a river from which two or three gardens can be irrigated, and what exceeds that is general. Explanation: Where it is stated that the pathway and the water channel are shared, it refers to specific ones, not general ones. Otherwise, co-ownership in a highway or the Ganges does not constitute specific pathway or water channel, and due to that shared use, shuf'ah will not be established. Then the author defined the specific pathway and specific water channel: when the road is not a through road and is not a public road, it is a specific pathway; otherwise it is general. For example, two people share water for their fields, but this does not mean that the river from which one irrigates is the same as the other's. If the water channels are separate, then the definition of specific water channel according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that it is a river in which ships do not sail; otherwise it is called general water channel. And Imam Abu Yusuf defined it as a river from which two or three gardens or plots are irrigated, and if more than that are irrigated, then it is general water channel. Note: A river in which people have fixed their own turns is a small river; otherwise it is a large river. Some jurists left this to the judgement of the mujtahid of each era, and al-Mutee' deemed it more appropriate. So in our country, a canal that comes out of the main canal is called a specific water channel, and the main canal is called a general water channel. And a specific pathway is that which no one can block.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage defines the conditions for shuf'ah based on shared pathway or water channel. The author states that for shuf'ah to be valid, the co-ownership must be in a 'specific' (khas) pathway or water channel, not a public one. A specific pathway is one that is not a through road (nafidh), meaning it is a dead-end lane. A specific water channel is defined differently by Abu Hanifa and Muhammad compared to Abu Yusuf. According to the first two, it is a river or canal that does not allow ships to sail; if ships can sail, it is a general water channel (sharb 'amm). Abu Yusuf defines it as a water channel that irrigates only two or three gardens; if it irrigates more than that, it is general. The commentary explains that shared use of a public road or a large river like the Ganges does not create a right of shuf'ah. The passage also notes that the specific pathway is one that cannot be blocked by anyone, emphasizing its private nature. There is an important note that the determination of 'specific' may vary with time and place, as some jurists leave it to the mujtahid's discretion. This ruling is essential for understanding when shuf'ah can be claimed through shared access rights.

Key Terms
طريق خاص (ṭarīq khāṣṣ): A specific pathway that is not a through road (ghayr nāfidh).
شرب خاص (sharb khāṣṣ): A specific water channel for irrigation, defined variously by different Hanafi imams.
شفعة (shuf‘ah): Right of pre-emption in property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the criterion for a specific water channel according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad?
A) It irrigates two or three gardens.
B) It is not navigable by ships.
C) It is shared by at least two people.
D) It is dug by the owners.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines specific water channel primarily as non-navigable, but Abu Yusuf's alternative criterion (limited irrigation) is also acknowledged and can affect the ruling in some cases.

Shuf'ah in a Branching Non-Through Street
Ruling on shuf'ah rights when a non-through street branches from another non-through street

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on shuf'ah to branching non-through streets, distinguishing between upper and lower residents, and justify the ruling using the principle of co-ownership in access rights.

Core Idea
Shuf'ah in a branching street depends on actual co-ownership in the pathway, not mere proximity.

This lesson tackles a specific scenario in Hanafi shuf'ah law: a dead-end lane branches into another dead-end lane. Who holds the right of pre-emption when a house is sold in either street? The ruling hinges on the concept of co-ownership in the shared access way: lower residents use the upper street, but not vice versa. We will analyze the text from Al-Hidayah, its reasoning, and its extension to water channels.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
Picture two non-through (dead-end) streets: an 'upper' street and a 'lower' branch that branches off from it. Only the lower branch's residents must pass through the upper street to exit; the upper residents do not use the lower branch.
2
Apply the Ruling for a Sale in the Lower Branch
If a house is sold in the lower branch, only the residents of that lower branch have shuf'ah. The upper residents have no right because they have no co-ownership in the lower branch's access.
3
Apply the Ruling for a Sale in the Upper Street
If a house is sold in the upper street, both the upper and lower residents have shuf'ah. The lower residents use the upper street, so they share co-ownership in it.
4
Trace the Reasoning
The underlying principle is that shuf'ah arises from co-ownership in the private pathway. Lower residents have a right in the upper street because they need it for access; upper residents have no need for the lower branch, so no co-ownership exists there.
5
Extend by Analogy
The same reasoning applies to a small river from which a smaller river branches: residents on the lower branch have shuf'ah only in their branch, but both have shuf'ah on the upper river. This demonstrates the Hanafi use of qiyas jaliy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان كانت سكة غير نافذة ينشعب منها سكة غير نافذة وهي مستطيلة قبيعت دار في السفلى فلا هل الشفعة خاصة دون اهل العليا وان بيعت في العليا فلا هل السكتين والمعنى ما ذكرنا في كتاب ادب القاضي ولو کان نهر صغير ياخذ منه نهر اصغر منه فهو على قياس الطريق فيما بيناه ترجمہ پس اگر ہو ایسی گلی جو غیر نافذ ہو جس سے دوسری غیر نافذگلی پھوٹ رہی ہو اور یہ (منشعبہ ) لمبی ہو پس بچا گیا کوئی گھر سفلی میں (منشعبہ مستطیلہ میں ) تو صرف اس کے باشندوں کیلئے ہی شفعہ ہے نہ کہ علیا والوں کیلئے شفعہ اور اگر بیچا گیا علی میں تو دونوں گلی والوں کیلئے ہے اور وجہ وہی ہے ہم جس کو کتاب ادب القاضی میں ذکر کر چکے ہیں اور اگر چھوٹی نہر ہو۔ جس سے دوسری اس سے چھوٹی نہر پھوٹ رہی ہو تو وہ بھی راستہ کے قیاس پر ہے اس شفعہ میں جس کو ہم نے بیان کیا ہے۔ تشریح ایک چھوٹی گلی ہے جو غیر نافذہ ہے اور اس سے ایک غیر نافذ ہ گلی اور پھوٹ رہی ہے جس کی صورت یہ ہے تو جو آپ دیکھ رہے ہیں یہ خود ایک چھوٹی گلی ہے جو عام نہیں ہے اور اس سے یہ نیچے والی گلی پھوٹ رہی ہے یہ بھی عام نہیں ہے جو گلی نیچے ہے جب اس کے باشندے باہر جائیں گے تو اوپر والی میں ہو کر جائیں گے اور اوپر والوں کو خروج کیلئے نیچے والی میں آنے کی ضرورت نہیں ۔ معلوم ہوا کہ اوپر والوں کا نیچے والی میں اشتراک نہیں اور نیچے والی کے باشندوں کا اشتراک دونوں میں ہے۔ لہذا اگر نیچے والی گلی میں کوئی گھر فروخت ہو تو اوپر والوں کو شفعہ نہیں ملے گا فقط نیچے والوں کا اشتراک ہے اسلئے دونوں کو چہ والوں کو شفعہ ملے گا۔
If there is a non-through street from which branches another non-through street, and it is elongated, and a house is sold in the lower (branch) street, then only its residents have shuf'ah, not the residents of the upper street. And if it is sold in the upper street, then both streets' residents have shuf'ah. The meaning is what we mentioned in the book Adab al-Qadi. And if there is a small river from which a smaller river takes water, it is on the analogy of the path in what we have explained. And if it is sold in the upper, then both streets' residents have shuf'ah. The reason is what we mentioned in the book Adab al-Qadi. And if there is a small river from which a smaller river takes water, it is on the analogy of the path in the shuf'ah we have explained. Explanation: A small street that is non-through, and from it branches another non-through street, as you see: this itself is a small street that is not public, and from it branches this lower street, also not public. When the residents of the lower street exit, they pass through the upper street, but the upper residents do not need to come into the lower street. Therefore, the upper residents have no share in the lower street, while the lower residents have a share in both. Commentary
This passage addresses a specific scenario in the law of shuf'ah involving branching non-through streets. The ruling is: if there is a main non-through street (upper) and a branch non-through street (lower) that is elongated, and a house is sold in the lower branch, only the residents of that branch have the right of shuf'ah; the residents of the upper street do not. If a house is sold in the upper street, however, both the upper and lower residents have shuf'ah. The reason is that lower residents must pass through the upper street to go out, so they have a co-ownership in the upper, but upper residents do not use the lower street, so they have no co-ownership in the lower. The analogy is extended to small rivers: if a small river branches from a smaller river, the same rule applies—the lower branch residents have shuf'ah when a property on the lower branch is sold, but not vice versa. This ruling is based on the principle of co-ownership in access rights, which is elaborated in the book Adab al-Qadi. The passage demonstrates how shuf'ah rights depend on the actual use and necessity of the shared pathway or water channel.

Key Terms
سكة غير نافذة (sikka ghayr nāfidha): A non-through street, i.e., a dead-end lane.
منشعبة (munsha‘iba): Branching street, the lower street that branches off from the upper.
شفعة (shuf‘ah): Right of pre-emption.

Sharb Khas and Sharb Am in Pre-emption Law
Defining specific and general irrigation rights in pre-emption law

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define sharb khas and sharb am according to the Hanafi school and distinguish between the definitions given by the common view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) and Imam Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
The type of irrigation channel determines pre-emption rights: specific (sharb khas) vs general (sharb am).

Pre-emption (shuf'a) applies to certain shares in property, but not all shared resources. One key distinction is the nature of irrigation rights. This lesson examines how Hanafi jurists define a specific irrigation right (sharb khas) versus a general one (sharb am), and why this classification matters for pre-emption.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definitions of sharb khas
Locate the first definition (common view: channel too small for boats) and the second (Imam Abu Yusuf: irrigates only two or three gardens). Note the criterion each uses.
The 'both parties' likely refers to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
2
Understand the criterion for sharb am
If boats can ply in the channel, or if it irrigates more than three gardens (per Abu Yusuf), it is sharb am. This has implications for pre-emption—general water rights do not trigger shuf'a.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi difference
Abu Yusuf uses a numerical criterion (2-3 gardens) while the common view uses navigability. Recognize that both are valid within the Hanafi school.
Later Hanafi works often prefer the common view, but practical application may vary.
4
Apply the definitions to a concrete scenario
Use the note about canals with fixed turns (small canal) and branching channels. Determine whether a given channel is sharb khas or sharb am under each definition.
The passage mentions that classification may depend on the mujtahid of the age.
5
Connect to pre-emption: why does it matter?
Sharb khas gives co-owners a right of pre-emption (shuf'a) if one sells their share. Sharb am does not. This distinction prevents pre-emption from applying to commonly shared water resources.
The special path (tariq khas) is similarly private and not subject to closure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشفعة
اور مثلاً دو آدمیوں کا کھیت کے پانی میں اشتر اس سے تو اس کا مطلب یہ نہیں کہ جس نہر سے یہ سیراب کرتا ہے وہ بھی کرے۔ اگر دونوں موری جدا گانہ ہوں تو شرب خاص کی تعریف طرفین نے یہ کی کہ ایسی نہ ہو جس میں کشتیاں چلتی ہوں ورنہ یہ عام شرب کہلائے گا۔ اور امام ابو یوسف نے شرب خاص کی تعریف یوں کی ہے کہ اس سے دو یا تین باغات یا چک بھرے جاتے ہوں اور اگر اس سے زیادہ باغات اس سے سیراب کئے جاتے ہوں تو یہ شرب عام ہے۔ تنبیہ جس نہر میں لوگ اپنی اپنی باری مقرر کئے ہیں وہ نہر صغیر ہے ورنہ نہر کبیر ہے اور بعض فقہاء نے اس کو ہر زمانہ کے مجتہد کی رائے پر چھوڑ دیا اور میٹی [؟] نے اس کو اشبہ کہا ہے تو ہمارے دیار میں اجتہایہ سے نکلنے والی نالی شرب خاص کہلائے گی اور اجیہا [؟] یہ شرب عام کہلائے گا۔ اور طریق خاص وہ کہلائے گا جس کو کوئی بند نہ کر سکے۔
Book of Pre-emption. For example, two persons' sharing in the water of a field does not mean that the canal from which one irrigates, the other should also use. If both have separate channels, then the definition of sharb khas (specific irrigation) according to both parties is that it is such that boats do not ply in it; otherwise it is called sharb am (general irrigation). Imam Abu Yusuf defined sharb khas as that by which two or three gardens or plots are irrigated; if more gardens are irrigated, it is sharb am. Note: A canal in which people have fixed their turns is a small canal; otherwise a large canal. Some jurists left this to the opinion of the mujtahid of every age, and Meti [؟] said it is more appropriate. So in our region, a channel branching from a grand canal is called sharb khas, and [؟] is called sharb am. A special path is one that no one can close.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage defines the types of irrigation rights (sharb khas and sharb am) as they relate to pre-emption. The author begins by clarifying that mere shared use of water does not create a right of pre-emption; rather, the nature of the water channel matters. Two definitions are given: first, the common view that sharb khas is a channel too small for boats; second, Imam Abu Yusuf's definition based on the number of gardens irrigated (two or three vs. more). The note (tanbih) further distinguishes small canals (with fixed turns) from large ones, and states that the classification may vary by region and juristic opinion. The passage ends by defining a special path (tariq khas) as one that cannot be closed, indicating a private right of way.

Key Terms
شرب خاص (sharb khas): Specific irrigation right in a channel too small for boats or irrigating only two or three gardens (per Abu Yusuf).
شرب عام (sharb am): General irrigation right in a larger channel used for many gardens or navigable.
طریق خاص (tariq khas): A private path that no one has the right to block.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Two or three
B) Four or five
C) More than five
D) Any number

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school classifies irrigation rights into sharb khas (specific) and sharb am (general), and only the former gives a right of pre-emption.

Pre-emption in Branched Dead-End Alleys
Ruling on pre-emption in a L-shaped dead-end alley system

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the pre-emption rights in a branched dead-end alley system and apply the Hanafi rule based on shared usage, including extension by qiyas to waterways.

Core Idea
Pre-emption follows the path of shared usage; only those who actually share a branch have the right.

In Hanafi fiqh, the right of pre-emption (shuf'a) attaches to properties that share a common right of way, especially in dead-end alleys (sikka ghayr nafidha). This lesson examines a specific configuration: a deeper dead-end alley branching from a shallower one. The ruling hinges on who actually uses the branch where the sale occurs. We will walk through the two scenarios and the qiyas used to extend the rule to waterways.

Guided Path
1
Identify the physical layout
Visualise a main dead-end alley (upper) that a branch (lower) dead-end alley leads off from. The branch is longer and only used by its own residents to exit via the upper alley.
The upper alley is shared by both groups; the lower branch is only used by its own residents.
2
Determine who shares which alley
Residents of the lower branch use both alleys to come and go. Residents of the upper alley only use the upper alley; they never need to enter the lower branch. Hence, the lower branch is exclusively shared among its own residents.
3
Apply the principle from Kitab Adab al-Qadi
The earlier rule states that pre-emption rights depend on shared use of the road. Those who share the road where the property is sold have the right; those who do not share it do not.
This is the asl in the qiyas.
4
Differentiate the two sale scenarios
If a house is sold in the lower branch, only lower branch residents have pre-emption because they alone share that branch. If sold in the upper alley, both groups have pre-emption because the lower residents also share the upper alley.
The ruling is not symmetric.
5
Extend via qiyas to waterways
The same reasoning applies to a small river from which a smaller river branches. Pre-emption rights on water usage follow the same pattern: only those who actually draw from a branch have a right in that branch.
This is a qiyas jaliy (clear analogy) based on the shared illa: extent of actual sharing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان كانت سكة غير نافذة ينشعب منها سكة غير نافذة وهي مستطيلة قبيع فيها دار في السفلى فلا لأهل الشفعة خاصة دون اهل العليا وان بيعت في العليا فلا لأهل السكتين والمعنى ما ذكرنا في كتاب ادب القاضي ولو کان نهر صغير ياخذ منه نهر اصغر منه فهو على قياس الطريق فيما بيناه۔ ترجمہ: پس اگر ہو ایسی گلی جو غیر نافذ ہو جس سے دوسری غیر نافذ گلی پھوٹ رہی ہو اور یہ (منشعبہ) لمبی ہو پس بچا گیا کوئی گھر سفلی میں (منشعبہ مستطیلہ میں) تو صرف اس کے باشندوں کیلئے ہے شفعہ ہے نہ کہ علیا والوں کیلئے شفعہ اور اگر بیچا گیا علیا میں تو دونوں گلی والوں کیلئے ہے اور وجہ وہی ہے ہم جس کو کتاب ادب القاضی میں ذکر کر چکے ہیں اور اگر چھوٹی نہر ہو جس سے دوسری اس سے چھوٹی نہر پھوٹ رہی ہو تو وہ بھی راستہ کے قیاس پر ہے اس شفعہ میں جس کو ہم نے بیان کیا ہے۔ تشریح: ایک چھوٹی گلی ہے جو غیر نافذہ ہے اور اس سے ایک غیر نافذ گلی اور پھوٹ رہی ہے جس کی صورت یہ ہے تو جو آپ دیکھ رہے ہیں یہ خود ایک چھوٹی گلی ہے جو عام نہیں ہے اور اس سے یہ نیچے والی گلی پھوٹ رہی ہے یہ بھی عام نہیں ہے جو گلی نیچے ہے جب اس کے باشندے باہر جائیں گے تو اوپر والی میں ہو کر جائیں گے اور اوپر والوں کو خروج کیلئے نیچے والی میں آنے کی ضرورت نہیں ۔ معلوم ہوا کہ اوپر والوں کا نیچے والی میں اشتراک نہیں اور نیچے والی کے باشندوں کا اشتراک دونوں میں ہے۔ لہذا اگر نیچے والی گلی میں کوئی گھر فروخت ہو تو اوپر والوں کو شفعہ نہیں ملے گا فقط نیچے والوں کا اشتراک ہے اسلئے دونوں کو چہ والوں کو شفعہ ملے گا۔
If there is a non-through road from which another non-through road branches, and it is elongated, and a house in the lower part is sold, then only the residents of the lower road have pre-emption, not the residents of the upper road. And if sold in the upper part, then both roads' residents have pre-emption. The meaning is what we mentioned in Kitab Adab al-Qadi. And if there is a small river from which a smaller river takes water, then it is upon the analogy of the road in what we have explained. Translation: So if there is a non-through alley from which another non-through alley branches, and it is elongated, then if a house is sold in the lower part (the branched elongated one), then only its residents have pre-emption, not the upper residents. And if sold in the upper part, then both alleys' residents have pre-emption. The reason is the same as we mentioned in Kitab Adab al-Qadi. And if there is a small river from which another smaller river branches, then it is upon the analogy of the road in this pre-emption that we have explained. Explanation: There is a small alley that is non-through, and from it another non-through alley branches. The form is as you see: this itself is a small alley that is not public, and from it this lower alley branches; this too is not public. When the residents of the lower alley go out, they pass through the upper one, but the upper residents do not need to enter the lower one for egress. So it is known that the upper ones do not share in the lower alley, while the lower residents share in both. Therefore, if a house is sold in the lower alley, the upper ones do not get pre-emption; only the lower ones have share, so both [the lower?] get pre-emption.

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed ruling on pre-emption in a specific configuration of dead-end alleys (sikka ghayr nafidha). The case is where a deep dead-end alley branches from another dead-end alley that opens to the main road. The ruling differentiates based on which part is sold: if a house in the lower (inner) branch is sold, only the residents of that branch have pre-emption because the upper residents do not share the lower branch; if a house in the upper outer branch is sold, both groups have pre-emption because the lower residents use the upper branch to exit. The proof is analogy to a similar rule in Kitab Adab al-Qadi, and the same principle applies to waterways. The commentary elaborates with a diagram: the upper alley is shared by all, but the lower alley is only used by its own residents.

Key Terms
سكة غير نافذة (sikka ghayr nafidha): A dead-end road or alley that is not a thoroughfare, only serving its residents.
منشعب (munsha'ib): Branched off; a secondary alley deriving from a primary one.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a house is sold in the lower (inner) branch of a dead-end alley system, who has the right of pre-emption?
A) Only residents of the lower branch
B) Residents of both upper and lower branches
C) Only residents of the upper branch
D) No one has pre-emption

Key Takeaway
Pre-emption rights in branched dead-end alleys are determined by actual shared usage of the specific branch where the property is sold.

Placing Beams on a Wall Does Not Create Partnership Pre-emption
Rule that placing beams on a wall only gives neighbor pre-emption, not partner pre-emption

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between shafi' shirkah and shafi' jiwār, and apply the Hanafi rule that placing beams on a wall does not create partnership pre-emption.

Core Idea
Placing beams gives neighbor-right, not ownership — the illa for partnership is land, not beams.

Pre-emption (shuf'ah) in Hanafi fiqh grants a right to acquire sold property, classified by the relationship to the property. This passage clarifies that a physical encroachment like placing beams on a wall does not transform a neighbor into a co-owner for pre-emption purposes. The ruling hinges on the effective cause (illa): partnership in the real estate itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two pre-emptor types
Recognize the Arabic terms shafi' shirkah (partner pre-emptor) and shafi' jiwār (neighbor pre-emptor) and their definitions.
2
State the ruling
The author rules that a person placing beams becomes shafi' jiwār, not shafi' shirkah. Note the explicit negation and affirmation.
3
Extract the illa (cause)
The text states: 'because the effective cause is partnership in the real estate'. Understand that shared ownership of the land is the operative cause for partnership pre-emption.
The illa is derived from the Arabic phrase 'li-anna al-'illa hiya al-shirkah fi al-'iqār'.
4
Apply the illa to the scenario
Placing beams does not make one a co-owner of the land or house; it only creates a right of use (servitude). Therefore the illa is absent, and only neighbor pre-emption remains.
Contrast with joint ownership of the wall itself, which would involve shared land.
5
Note the practical consequence
A shafi' jiwār has a weaker pre-emption right; if a partner (shafi' shirkah) exists, the neighbor's right is superseded.
This hierarchy is important in actual property disputes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولا يكون الرجل بالجذوع على الحائط شفيع شركة ولكنه شفيع جوار لان العلة هي الشركة في العقار وبوضع الجذوع لا يصير شريكا فى الدار الا انه جار ملازق قال والشريك في الخشبة تكون على حائط الدار جار لما بينا۔ ترجمہ: فرمایا مصنف نے اور نہیں ہوگا مرد دیوار پر کڑی رکھنے کی وجہ سے شفیع شرکت لیکن وہ شفیع جوار ہے اسلئے کہ علت وہ زمین میں شرکت ہے اور کڑی رکھنے کی وجہ سے وہ دار میں شریک نہیں ہوگا مگر وہ جار ملازق ہے فرمایا محمد نے اور ان لکڑیوں میں شریک جو گھر کی دیوار میں ہوں جار ہے اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے۔ تشریح: ماقبل میں جہاں شرکت دیوار کی بحث آئی تھی اس سے مراد یہ ہے کہ جس زمین پر دیوار ہے اس جگہ میں دونوں کا اشتراک ہو اور اگر جگہ ایک کی ہے اور دونوں نے مل کر اس کو تعمیر کر لیا تو یہ دیوار میں شرکت نہیں کہلائے گی۔ اس کو مصنف نے فرمایا کہ اگر دیوار پر دونوں کی کڑی رکھی ہوئی ہے لیکن وہ دیوار ایک کی ملکیت ہے تو اس کی وجہ سے وہ شریک فی الدار نہیں ہوگا۔ لہذا اس کو شفیع شرکت نہیں کہیں گے۔ البتہ شفیع جوار ہے اسلئے کہ شفیع شرکت ہونے کی علت زمین میں اشتراک ہے جو یہاں مفقود ہے اور محض کڑی رکھنے کی وجہ سے وہ دار کا شریک نہیں ہوگا۔ البتہ جار ملاصق ہے جس کی تفسیر ماقبل میں گذر چکی ہے۔
He (the author) said: A man does not become a pre-emptor by partnership (shafi' shirkah) merely by placing beams on a wall; rather he is a pre-emptor by adjacency (shafi' jiwār) because the effective cause is partnership in the real estate, and by placing beams he does not become a partner in the house, except that he is an adjoining neighbor. He (Imam Muhammad) said: And the partner in the wood that is on the wall of a house is a neighbor due to what we have explained. Translation: The author said: A man does not become a pre-emptor by partnership due to placing beams on a wall; rather he is a pre-emptor by adjacency because the cause is partnership in the land, and by placing beams he does not become a partner in the house, but he is an adjoining neighbor. Imam Muhammad said: And the partner in the beams that are on the house's wall is a neighbor due to the reason we have explained. Explanation: In the previous discussion of partnership in a wall, it meant that both share the land under the wall. If the land belongs to one and they both built the wall together, it is not called partnership in the wall. The author says: If both have placed beams on a wall, but the wall is owned by one, then he does not become a partner in the house. Therefore he is not called a pre-emptor by partnership. However, he is a pre-emptor by adjacency because the cause for partnership pre-emption is partnership in the land, which is absent here. Merely placing beams does not make him a partner in the house. But he is an adjoining neighbor, whose explanation came earlier.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage distinguishes between two types of pre-emptors: shafi' shirkah (partner pre-emptor) and shafi' jiwār (neighbor pre-emptor). The ruling is clear: merely placing beams (jadhū') on a neighbor's wall does not make one a partner in the property; thus one does not acquire the right of pre-emption as a partner. Instead, one retains only the right of a neighbor (shafi' jiwār). The reason (illa) is that partnership pre-emption requires shared ownership of the real estate itself, which is absent here. The beams constitute a right of easement but not co-ownership. Imam Muhammad's additional quote reinforces that even a partner in the beams is only a neighbor. The commentary explains that true partnership in a wall requires joint ownership of the land beneath it; placing beams does not confer that.

Key Terms
شفيع شركة (shafi' shirkah): A pre-emptor who is a partner in the property itself (shared ownership).
شفيع جوار (shafi' jiwār): A pre-emptor who is an adjoining neighbor but not a co-owner.
علة (illa): The effective cause for partnership pre-emption: shared ownership of the real estate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What type of pre-emptor does a person become when he places his beams on a neighbor's wall?
A) Shafi' shirkah
B) Shafi' jiwār
C) Both
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
Placing beams on a wall does not make one a co-owner; hence one is only a neighbor pre-emptor (shafi' jiwār), not a partner pre-emptor (shafi' shirkah).

Division of Pre-emption Rights: Per Capita or Proportional to Shares?
Dispute on division of pre-emption rights

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on dividing pre-emption rights among multiple pre-emptors, explain the Shafi'i counter-argument, and identify the practical consequence of the difference.

Core Idea
Pre-emption is divided by heads, not shares — a right to remove a stranger is equal for all co-owners.

This lesson presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute regarding the distribution of pre-emption rights when multiple co-owners are entitled. The Hanafi school holds that the right is divided equally per capita, regardless of ownership shares. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that pre-emption is a benefit of ownership and should follow the proportional shares. Understanding this dispute illuminates the different conceptual foundations of pre-emption in the two schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State the Hanafi ruling: pre-emption is divided by number of heads (per capita), not by ownership shares. State the Shafi'i position: it is divided according to the measures of shares (proportional to ownership).
Both positions are directly stated in the text.
2
Analyze the Shafi'i proof
The Shafi'i proof is a qiyas (analogy): pre-emption is a benefit (marfaq) of ownership, like profit, produce, offspring, and fruit. Since those benefits are divided proportionally to shares, pre-emption should be as well.
Identify the asl (original case) and far' (new case) in this qiyas.
3
Consider the Hanafi response
The text does not provide the Hanafi response here, but the standard Hanafi rebuttal distinguishes pre-emption from other benefits: pre-emption is not a generated benefit but a right to acquire the share of a stranger, attached to the property as a whole, not to individual shares. Thus, it is equally applicable to all co-owners regardless of share size.
This distinction is crucial for understanding the Hanafi position.
4
Determine the practical difference
Work through a concrete example: Two co-owners, A (1/4 share) and B (3/4 share). A third owner sells his 1/4 share. Hanafi: A and B each get 1/2 of the sold share. Shafi'i: A gets 1/4 of the sold share, B gets 3/4.
This thamarah al-khilaf shows the real-world impact of the dispute.
5
Note the tarjih within the Hanafi school
The Hanafi school relies on its position (per capita) and it is the mufta bihi. The Shafi'i position is acknowledged but not adopted.
Tarjih is based on the nature of pre-emption as a right of removal, not a profit-generating benefit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال واذا اجتمع الشفعاء فالشفعة بينهم على عدد رؤسهم ولا يعتبر اختلاف الاملاك وقال الشافعي هي على مقادير الانصباء لان الشفعة من مرافق الملك الا يرى انها لتكميل منفعته فاشبه الربح والغلة والولد والثمرة
He said: When pre-emptors gather, pre-emption is among them according to the number of heads, and difference in ownership is not considered. Al-Shafi'i said: It is according to the measures of shares because pre-emption is from the benefits of ownership. Do you not see that it is for the completion of its benefit, so it resembles profit, produce, offspring, and fruit.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute about the division of the pre-emption right when multiple parties are entitled. The Hanafi position, stated here, is that pre-emption is divided equally among the pre-emptors by number of persons (heads), regardless of their respective ownership shares. For example, if two partners own unequal shares, and a third party's share is sold, the pre-emption right is divided equally between the two partners, not proportionally to their shares. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that pre-emption is a benefit (marāfiq) of ownership, and like other benefits such as profit, rent, offspring, and fruit, it should be divided according to ownership shares. The Hanafi proof is likely based on the idea that pre-emption is a right attached to the property as a whole, not to individual shares, and it is a remedy to remove a stranger, which is equally applicable to all co-owners. The commentary would typically provide the Hanafi response, but this excerpt only presents the two positions.

Key Terms
عدد الرؤوس (adad al-ru'us): Division by number of persons (per capita), regardless of ownership size.
مقادير الانصباء (maqadir al-ansiba): Division according to the measures of shares (proportional to ownership).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how is the right of pre-emption divided among multiple co-owners?
A) According to the value of each person's share
B) According to the number of persons (heads)
C) According to the oldest owner
D) Decided by lot

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, pre-emption rights are divided equally among co-owners per capita, not by ownership shares, because the right is to remove a stranger, which is equally applicable to all.

Pre-emption in Shared Water Channels: Main vs Branch
Ruling on pre-emption in shared water channels

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the pre-emption rights when a shared water channel has a main and a branch, and distinguish which owners have the right.

Core Idea
Pre-emption follows the specific common channel, not all partners.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the right of pre-emption (shuf'ah) in shared water channels. The passage clarifies that the right depends on which part of the channel is sold: the main channel or a branch. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correct application in property disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognise that there is a main water channel and a branch channel emerging from it. All owners share the main channel, but only certain owners share the branch.
The analogy is also applied to shared lanes.
2
Apply to the main channel
If land on the main channel is sold, both sets of owners (those on the main and those on the branch) have the right of pre-emption because all share the main channel.
This is because the main channel is common to all.
3
Apply to the branch channel
If land on the branch channel is sold, only those whose property lies along that branch have pre-emption rights. Owners on the main channel cannot claim pre-emption because they do not have a direct common right in the branch.
The branch is not accessible to main channel owners for egress/ingress.
4
Generalise the principle
The ruling is based on the principle that pre-emption attaches to the specific common path (sikkah) or channel that serves the property sold. It is not merely based on broader neighbourhood or adjacency.
Reference is made to the book Adab al-Qadi for the underlying reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اور اگر اسی طرح دو نہریں ہوں تو اس کا بھی یہی حکم ہے یعنی ایک نالی ہے اس میں سے دوسری چھوٹی نالی نکل رہی ہے تو اوپر والی میں سب کا اشتراک ہے اور نیچے والی میں پیچھے والوں کا اشتراک ہے۔ لہذا اگر او پر زمین فروخت ہو تو حق شفعہ دونوں فریق کیلئے ہے۔ اور اگر نیچے فروخت ہو تو صرف ان لوگوں کو شفعہ ملے گا جن کی یہاں زمین ہے۔ اوپر والے آکر نیچے والی گلی میں اپنے مکانون کا دروازہ نہیں کھول سکتے ہیں اور نیچے والے اوپر والی میں اپنے مکان کا دروازہ کھول سکتے ہیں تو ایسے ہی شفعہ کا مسئلہ ہے۔ اس کو مصنف نے فرمايا و المعنى ما ذكر في كتاب ادب القاضی وہ وجہ یہی ہے۔۔ فان كانت سكة غير ..... الخ كان تامہ ہے اسلئے غیر مرفوع ہوگا۔
And if there are two waterways similarly, this same ruling applies, that is, there is a main channel from which another smaller channel emerges. So in the upper channel, all share, and in the lower channel, those behind share. Thus, if land on the upper [channel] is sold, the right of pre-emption is for both parties. And if the lower [channel] is sold, pre-emption will only be for those whose land is here. Those on the upper cannot open doors of their houses into the lower lane, but those on the lower can open doors into the upper lane. Similarly is the matter of pre-emption. The author said: 'And the meaning is what was mentioned in the book Adab al-Qadi' – that is the reason. ... 'So if there is a lane other than ... etc.' – it is complete, so it will be non-elevated [i.e., not marfu'].
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage states a ruling about pre-emption (shuf'ah) rights when there is a shared water channel or lane with a branch. The ruling differentiates between the main channel and the branch. If the main channel is sold, all owners who share it have pre-emption rights. But if the branch channel is sold, only those whose property lies along that branch have the right. The author refers to the reasoning found in the book Adab al-Qadi, indicating that the logic is based on the principle that pre-emption follows the specific common access way. The commentary emphasizes that the ruling is not a marfu' (elevated) tradition but a juristic deduction.

Key Terms
شفعہ (shuf'ah): Right of pre-emption: the right to buy property that has been sold to a third party, based on partnership or adjacency.
سكة (sikkah): Lane or path that is shared by multiple property owners.
شریک (sharīk): Partner, specifically one who shares ownership in property or a right.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) All owners in the main channel
B) Only owners whose property is along the branch
C) Both main and branch owners equally
D) No one has pre-emption

Key Takeaway
Pre-emption rights in shared water channels are determined by which specific channel serves the property sold, not by broader partnership.

Beams on Wall Do Not Confer Partnership Pre-emption
Ruling that placing beams on a wall gives only neighborly pre-emption, not partnership pre-emption

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the distinction between shuf'at al-shirkah and shuf'at al-jiwār to a scenario of physical attachment without co-ownership.

Core Idea
Placing beams on a wall does not create partnership pre-emption; only neighborly pre-emption applies.

In this passage, we examine a key distinction in Hanafi pre-emption law: the difference between a co-owner and a neighbor. You will learn why simply using a neighbor's wall does not elevate you to a partner in the property, and how the legal cause (illa) of actual co-ownership determines the strength of the pre-emption right.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? Placing beams on a neighbor's wall. The ruling is that this does not give partnership pre-emption (shuf'at al-shirkah).
2
Locate the proof
The proof is the illah (legal cause): the cause for partnership pre-emption is actual co-ownership in the property (shirkah fi al-'iqār).
This is a qiyas reasoning.
3
Apply qiyas
The original case (asl) is co-ownership; the new case (far') is placing beams without co-ownership. Since the illah is absent, the ruling of the asl does not transfer.
The illah is jaliyyah (clear).
4
Determine the outcome
Only neighborly pre-emption (shuf'at al-jiwār) applies, because the person is an attached neighbor (jār mulāṣiq).
5
Note the supplementary ruling
Even being a partner in the beams themselves does not change this; one remains a neighbor, not a partner in the house.
Imam Muhammad's statement confirms this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دیوار پر کڑیاں رکھنے سے شریک فی السبیع نہیں بلکہ شفیع جوار ہے
قال ولا يكون الرجل بالجذوع على الحائط شفيع شركة ولكنه شفيع جوار لان العلة هي الشركة في العقار وبوضع الجذوع لا يصير شريكا فى الدار الا انه جار ملازق قال والشريك في الخشبة تكون على حائط الدار جار لما بينا
ترجمہ فرمایا مصنف نے اور نہیں ہوگا مرد د یوار پر کڑی رکھنے کی وجہ سے شفیع شرکت لیکن وہ شفیع جوار ہے اسلئے کہ علت وہ زمین میں شرکت ہے اور کڑی رکھنے کی وجہ سے وہ دار میں شریک نہیں ہوگا مگر وہ جار ملازق ہے فرمایا محمد نے اور ان لکڑیوں میں شریک جو گھر کی دیوار میں ہوں جار ہے اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے۔
تشریح ماقبل میں جہاں شرکت دیوار کی بحث آئی تھی اس سے مراد یہ ہے کہ جس زمین پر دیوار ہے اس جگہ میں دونوں کا اشتراک ہو اور اگر جگہ ایک کی ہے اور دونوں نے مل کر اس کو تعمیر کر لیا تو یہ دیوار میں شرکت نہیں کہلائے گی۔
اس کو مصنف نے فرمایا کہ اگر دیوار پر دونوں کی کڑی رکھی ہوئی ہے لیکن وہ دیوار ایک کی ملکیت ہے تو اس کی وجہ سے وہ شریک فی الدار نہیں ہوگا۔ لہذا اس کو شفیع شرکت نہیں کہیں گے۔ البتہ شفیع جوار ہے اسلئے کہ شفیع شرکت ہونے کی علت زمین میں اشتراک ہے جو یہاں مفقود ہے اور محض کڑی رکھنے کی وجہ سے وہ دار کا شریک نہیں ہوگا۔ البتہ جار ملاصق ہے جس کی تفسیر ماقبل میں گذر چکی ہے۔ پہلے قال کے فاعل صاحب ہدایہ ہیں اور دوسرے قال کے فاعل امام محمد ہیں۔ ان کا ہی قول جامع صغیر کی کتاب البیوع میں مذکور ہے جس بات کو امام محمد نے جامع صغیر میں فرمایا ہے۔ اس بات کو مصنف نے پہلے قال کے تحت بیان فرمایا ہے۔ دوسرے قال کے تحت الشریک.... الخ مبتدا ہے اور جار اس کی خبر ہے اور تكون علیٰ حائط الدار خشبہ کی صفت ہے۔
Placing beams on a wall does not make one a partner in the path, but rather a neighbor pre-emptor. He said: 'A man does not become a pre-emptor of partnership by placing beams on a wall; rather, he is a pre-emptor of adjacency, because the cause is partnership in real estate, and by placing beams he does not become a partner in the house, except that he is an attached neighbor.' He said: 'And the partner in the wood that is on the wall of the house is a neighbor due to what we have explained.' The author translated: 'He said: A man is not by placing beams on the wall a pre-emptor of partnership, but he is a pre-emptor of adjacency because the cause is partnership in land, and by placing beams he does not become a partner in the house, except he is an attached neighbor. Muhammad said: And the partner in the pieces of wood that are in the wall of the house is a neighbor due to the proof we have mentioned.' Explanation: In the previous discussion about partnership in a wall, the meaning is that both share in the land on which the wall is built. If the land is owned by one and both jointly constructed the wall, this is not called partnership in the wall. The author said: If both have placed beams on the wall, but the wall is owned by one, he does not become a partner in the house due to that. Therefore, he is not called a pre-emptor of partnership. Rather, he is a pre-emptor of adjacency because the cause of being a pre-emptor of partnership is partnership in land, which is absent here. Purely placing beams does not make him a partner in the house. Rather, he is an attached neighbor, whose definition has passed earlier. The subject of the first 'he said' is the author of Hidayah, and the subject of the second 'he said' is Imam Muhammad. His statement is mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir, book of sales. The author has explained that under the first 'he said'. Under the second 'he said', 'al-Sharik...' is the subject and 'jar' is the predicate, and 'takunu' ala ha'it al-dar' is the description of 'khashabah'.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage clarifies the distinction between two types of pre-emption: shuf'at al-shirkah (partnership pre-emption) and shuf'at al-jiwār (neighborly pre-emption). The ruling states that merely placing beams (jadhū') on a neighbor's wall does not make one a co-owner of the house. Therefore, one does not have the stronger form of pre-emption based on partnership. However, one does have the weaker form based on adjacency (jiwār). The cause (illa) for partnership pre-emption is actual co-ownership in the property (shirkah fi al-'iqār). Placing beams does not establish co-ownership; it only creates physical attachment. Imam Muhammad further states that even if one is a partner in the beams themselves (i.e., the wood is jointly owned), that still only makes one a neighbor, not a partner in the house. The commentary also explains that the discussion about a shared wall refers to partnership in the land under the wall, not joint construction on one's own land.

Key Terms
شفیع شرکت (shafi' sharikat): A pre-emptor whose right is based on being a co-owner in the property.
شفیع جوار (shafi' jiwār): A pre-emptor whose right is based on being an attached neighbor, not a co-owner.
علة (illah): The legal cause or effective reason that justifies a ruling.
جذوع (jadhū'): Beams or timbers placed on a wall.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, what type of pre-emption does a person have if they place beams on a neighbor's wall without co-ownership?
A) Shuf'at al-shirkah (partnership pre-emption)
B) Shuf'at al-jiwār (neighborly pre-emption)
C) No pre-emption at all
D) Both types equally

Key Takeaway
The legal cause (illa) for partnership pre-emption is actual co-ownership in the property; mere physical attachment does not confer this right.

Pre-emption Distribution: Heads vs Shares
Inter-madhhab dispute on pre-emption distribution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on distribution of shuf'ah among multiple pre-emptors and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-evidence using the Hanafi rebuttal.

Core Idea
Pre-emption is divided by heads, not shares, because the cause (connection) is equal for all pre-emptors.

In this passage from Al-Hidayah, we encounter a classic inter-madhhab dispute: when several pre-emptors have unequal ownership shares, is the pre-emption right divided equally or proportionally? The Hanafi school, following the matn of Quduri, holds that it is divided equally by number of heads. Imam al-Shafi'i argues for proportional division based on an analogy to other benefits of property. This lesson unpacks the proofs, the rebuttal, and the practical consequences of this disagreement.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling and its basis
The matn states pre-emption is divided by number of heads, not by ownership size. The key is that all pre-emptors share the same cause (sabab): connection (ittisal).
The cause of entitlement (sabab al-istihqaq) is equal, so the right is equal.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position and its proof
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that pre-emption is a benefit of property (min marafiq al-milk) and thus should be proportional to ownership, like profit, crop, offspring, and fruit.
He presents examples from trade, cultivation, slave-girl's child, and garden fruit.
3
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafi response denies the analogy: pre-emption involves taking ownership of another's property, not a fruit of one's own (tamlik milk ghayrihi la yaj'al thamara min thamarat milkihi). The cause (connection) is equal, so the right is equal.
If only one pre-emptor existed, he would take full pre-emption, indicating completeness of the cause.
4
Work through the examples
The Shafi'i examples (profit, crop, child, fruit) are distinguished because they are direct benefits of property, whereas pre-emption is a right to acquire another's share—not a benefit of ownership itself.
The Hanafi proof emphasizes that multiplicity of connection does not strengthen the cause.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, if three partners with shares 60%, 30%, 10% pre-empt a sold share, Hanafis give each 1/3 of the sold portion; Shafi'is give proportional shares (60%, 30%, 10% of the sold portion).
This difference arises from the underlying usul: equality of cause vs proportionality of benefit.

ولنا انهم استووا في سبب الاستحقاق وهو الاتصال فيستوون في الاستحقاق الايرى انه لو انفرد واحد منهم استحق كمال الشفعة وهذا أية كمال السبب وكثرة الاتصال تؤذن بكثرة العلة والترجيح يقع بقوة في الدليل لا بكثرته ولا قوة ههنا لظهور الأخرى بمقابلته و تملک ملک غيره لا يجعل ثمرة من ثمرات ملکه بخلاف الثمرة واشباهها
ترجمہ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ سب استحقاق کے سبب میں برابر ہیں اور وہ اتصال ہے تو استحقاق کے اندر برابر ہوں گے کیا یہ
He said: 'When pre-emptors gather, pre-emption is among them according to the number of their heads, and differences in ownership are not considered.' Al-Shafi'i said: 'It is according to the measure of shares, because pre-emption is among the benefits of ownership. Do you not see that it is for the completion of its benefit, so it resembles profit, crop, offspring, and fruit.' Translation: Quduri said: 'When several pre-emptors gather, pre-emption is among them according to the number of their heads, and differences in ownership are not considered.' Al-Shafi'i said: 'Pre-emption will be according to the extent of shares, because pre-emption is among the benefits of property. Do you not see that pre-emption is for the completion of the benefit of property, so it resembles profit, crop, offspring, and fruit.' Explanation: Four men bought a house, for example, for 100 rupees: one has 50, one has 30, one has 15, and one has 5. Now the one with 5 sells his share; there are three pre-emptors. The question: will pre-emption be given to these three equally or in proportion to ownership? The Hanafis said that all will receive equally, meaning the count of heads will be considered, not the amount of shares. Imam al-Shafi'i said that the benefits of property wherever they are obtained are distributed in proportion to ownership, and pre-emption is also a benefit of property because it is given so that the pre-emptor can benefit from his property. So pre-emption's purpose is the completion of benefit of property. On that, he presented some evidence: 1) Two men bought something for trade for 15 rupees, one had 10 and the other 5, no condition was made, and they sold it for 18 rupees. So 2 rupees go to the one with 10 and 1 rupee to the one with 5, because their ownership is in that proportion. 2) Two men bought land, one had 10,000 and the other 5,000 rupees. Then they cultivated it, and the crop was produced, so the first gets two-thirds and the second gets one-third, because their ownership is in that proportion. 3) Two men bought a slave-girl for 15 rupees, one had 10 and the other 5. Then they married her off, and a child was born who is their slave. He was sold for, say, 15 rupees, so the first gets 10 and the second 5, according to ownership proportion. 4) Two men bought a garden similarly, then its fruit was sold, and the profit is also divided in proportion to ownership. Imam al-Shafi'i said that the case of pre-emption is similar; it will also be given in proportion to ownership. We [Hanafis] said division is by heads. Hanafi proof: And for us, they are equal in the cause of entitlement, which is connection (ittisal), so they are equal in entitlement. Do you not see that if one of them were alone, he would be entitled to full pre-emption? And this indicates completeness of the cause. And multiplicity of connection does not indicate multiplicity of the cause, and preference is based on strength of evidence, not multiplicity, and there is no strength here due to the appearance of other [reasoning] in opposition. And taking ownership of another's property does not become a fruit of one's own property, unlike fruit and its like. Translation: And our proof is that these all are equal in the cause of entitlement, which is connection, so they will be equal in entitlement. Do you not see that if one of them were alone, he would be entitled to full pre-emption? ...
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the distribution of pre-emption (shuf'ah) when multiple pre-emptors hold shares of different sizes in the property. The Hanafi position, attributed to the matn of Quduri, is that pre-emption is divided equally among the pre-emptors (by number of heads), regardless of the size of their respective ownership stakes. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that pre-emption should be divided proportionally to each pre-emptor's ownership share, because pre-emption is a benefit of property, analogous to profit, crop, offspring, and fruit, all of which are distributed proportionally. The Hanafi response rebuts this analogy: pre-emption involves taking ownership of another's property, which is not a fruit of one's own property. The cause for pre-emption entitlement is connection (ittisal), and all pre-emptors are equal in this cause, so they must be equal in right. If only one pre-emptor existed, he would take the full right; thus, the entitlement is complete for each, and they equally share the right.

Key Terms
سبب الاستحقاق (sabab al-istihqaq): The cause of entitlement to pre-emption, which in this context is connection (ittisal) to the property.
اتصال (ittisal): Connection or contiguity of ownership, the basis for pre-emption right.
عدد الرؤوس (adad al-ru'us): Count of heads; distribution based on number of pre-emptors, not their shares.
منافع الملک (manafi' al-milk): Benefits of ownership, including usufruct and proceeds.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if three partners with different shares have pre-emption rights, how is the property distributed?
A) Proportionally to their original ownership shares
B) Equally, by number of heads
C) It goes to the one with the largest share
D) It is sold and the money is divided proportionally

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distributes pre-emption equally among co-owners by the number of heads, based on their equal connection to the property, rejecting the Shafi'i proportional analogy.

Distribution of Shuf'a Among Multiple Pre-emptors
Presents Hanafi position and Shafi'i objection on shuf'a distribution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on shuf'a distribution, explain the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i objection, and calculate the thamarah al-khilaf in a given scenario.

Core Idea
Shuf'a is divided equally by number of pre-emptors, not by share size.

This lesson examines a classic inter-madhhab dispute: when multiple co-owners claim the right of pre-emption (shuf'a) after a share is sold, should the sold share be divided equally among them or proportionally to their existing shares? The Hanafi school, following a strict causal analysis, argues for equal division by headcount, while the Shafi'i school analogizes shuf'a to other benefits of ownership. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to evaluate competing qiyas arguments.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: shuf'a is divided equally among pre-emptors according to their number (عدد الرؤوس), not the size of their shares.
This is the position of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection
Understand Imam al-Shafi'i's argument: shuf'a is a benefit of ownership, like profits, crops, offspring, and fruit—all divided proportionally to shares.
The Shafi'i view uses qiyas: shuf'a is analogous to manafi' al-milk.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
Study the Hanafi argument: the cause (illa) of shuf'a is adjacency (ittisal), which is equal in all pre-emptors. Preference is by strength of proof, not quantity. Shuf'a is not a fruit of ownership.
The key principle: 'al-tarjih bi-quwwat al-dalil la bi-kathratihi.'
4
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
Calculate the practical difference: given specific shares, compare equal division versus proportional division.
For example, 50%, 30%, 20% shares; if 10% is sold, Hanafi: 3.33% each; Shafi'i: 5%, 3%, 2%.

كتاب الشفعة

تشریح ایک گھر کو چار آدمیوں نے مل کر خرید ا مثلاً سوروپے میں ایک کے پچاس روپے ہیں ، ایک کے تھیں، ایک کے پندرہ اور ایک کے پانچ ۔ اب پانچ والا اپنا حصہ فروخت کرتا ہے جس کے تین شفیع ہیں۔ اب سوال یہ ہے کہ شفعہ تو ان تینوں کو ملے گا مگر برابر ملے گا یا ملک کے تناسب سے ملے گا۔ احناف نے کہا کہ سب کو برابر ملے گا یعنی عد دروس کا اعتبار ہوگا حصے اور سہام کی مقدار نہیں دیکھی جائے گی ۔ امام شافعی نے کہا کہ ملک کے منافع جہاں بھی حاصل ہوں گے وہ ملک کے تناسب سے تقسیم ہوتے اور شفعہ بھی منفعت ملک ہے چونکہ وہ اسی لئے تو دیا گیا ہے کہ شفیع اپنی ملک سے انتفاع کر سکے گویا کہ شفعہ کا مقصد منفعت ملک کی تعمیل ہے جس پر انہوں نے کچھ شواہد تو پیش کئے ہیں :- ا دو آدمیوں نے پندرہ روپے میں کوئی چیز تجارت کیلئے خریدی ، ایک کے دس روپے اور دوسرے کے پانچ اور شرط کچھ کی نہیں اور اٹھارہ روپے میں اس چیز کو فروخت کر دیا تو دو روپے دس والے کو اور ایک روپیہ پانچ والے کو ملے گا۔ کیونکہ ان کی ملکیت اسی تناسب سے ہے۔
