Definition of Wasi and Limits of His Authority
Defining the wasi and distinguishing from qayyim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the wasi in Hanafi fiqh, distinguish him from a qayyim, and state the conditions under which his sale is invalid.

Core Idea
A wasi may preserve and sell, but his sale is void if at a gross loss or if all heirs are capable adults.

Understanding the role of a wasi (executor) is essential in Islamic estate management. The Hanafi school carefully delineates what a wasi may and may not do, especially regarding selling the deceased's property. This lesson defines the term, contrasts it with a qayyim (a mere custodian), and highlights critical limits on the wasi's authority to transact.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the Shari'ah definition of wasi
Read the definition: a wasi is appointed to both preserve and dispose of a deceased person's property and to care for minor children. Note the dual authority.
2
Distinguish wasi from qayyim
Identify the key difference: a wasi has both preservation and disposition powers; a qayyim has only preservation, no authority to sell or transact.
This distinction is unique to the Hanafi school.
3
Recognize invalid sales by a wasi
Two situations render a wasi's sale invalid: (1) selling a valuable item for a grossly low price (e.g., 25,000 for 1,000), and (2) when all heirs are adults and capable of managing their own affairs.
The first prevents harm to the estate; the second removes the need for an executor.
4
Understand when a wasi's sale is permissible
If the deceased has no debts, the wasi acts like a seller where his intervention is genuinely needed (e.g., when there are minor heirs or debts). This is derived from the principle 'fima yajuzu bay'uh'.
The wasi's authority is not unlimited; it is conditioned by necessity and benefit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبیہ وہی کسے کہتے ہیں؟ الوصى شرعاً من يقام لاجل الحفظ والتصرف في مال الرجل واطفاله بعد الموت والفرق بين الوصى والقيم ان الوصى يفوض اليه الحفظ والتصرف والقيم يفوض اليه الحفظ دون التصرف كذا في قواعد الفقه ص 543 بعض جگہ وصی کا تصرف جائز نہیں ہوتا۔ مثلاً پچیس ہزار کی چیز ایک ہزار میں فروخت کرنے لگے۔ اسی طرح اگر سارے ورثاء بالغ ہوں تو بھی وصی کی بیع جائز نہ ہوگی ۔ اگر میت پر قرض نہ ہو تو مصنف نے فیما یجوز بیعہ کہ کر یہ بتایا ہے کہ وصی بائع کے درجہ میں وہاں ہے۔ جہاں اس کا تصرف جائز ہوگا۔
Note: What is a wasi? In Shari'ah, the wasi is one who is appointed for the preservation and disposition of a man's property and his children after death. The difference between a wasi and a qayyim is that the wasi is entrusted with both preservation and disposition, while the qayyim is entrusted with preservation only, without disposition. As in Qawa'id al-Fiqh, p. 543. In some places, the wasi's disposition is not permissible. For example, if he tries to sell something worth twenty-five thousand for one thousand. Similarly, if all the heirs are adults, the wasi's sale would not be valid. If the deceased has no debt, the author (in 'fima yajuzu bay'uh') indicates that the wasi is in the position of a seller where his disposition is permissible.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'wasi' (executor) as per Shari'ah: a person appointed to safeguard and manage the property and minor children of a deceased person. It distinguishes the wasi from a qayyim (guardian): the wasi has authority over both preservation and disposition (e.g., selling), while the qayyim may only preserve the property, not transact with it. The passage then notes exceptions where the wasi's disposition (specifically sale) is not valid: if he sells at a grossly undervalued price (e.g., a 25,000 item for 1,000) or if all heirs are adults and capable of managing their own affairs. Additionally, if the deceased has no debts, the hadith 'fima yajuzu bay'uh' (concerning what is permissible to sell) indicates that the wasi acts like a seller only where his intervention is needed.

Key Terms
الوصى (al-wasi): One appointed to preserve and dispose of a deceased person's property and care for his minor children after death.
القيم (al-qayyim): A guardian appointed only for preservation, without authority to sell or transact.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is a wasi's sale of an orphan's property considered invalid?
A) When the sale is at a fair market price.
B) When the property is sold for a grossly undervalued price or when all heirs are adults.
C) When the sale is for the benefit of the orphans.
D) When the property is sold after obtaining court permission.

Key Takeaway
A wasi's authority to sell is conditional: it becomes invalid if the sale is at a gross undervalue or when all heirs are capable adults.

Conflict of Witnesses: Shafi' vs. Mushtari
Intra-Hanafi dispute over witness precedence in shuf'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on conflicting witness testimony between the shafi' and mushtari and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa/Muhammad vs. Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
When both shafi’ and buyer present witnesses, the shafi’ may choose his price — harmonizing evidence as two separate sales.

In pre-emption (shuf'ah), disputes often arise over the sale price. When both the pre-emptor and the buyer produce witnesses testifying to different prices, which testimony prevails? This passage from Al-Hidayah presents an intra-Hanafi dispute. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that the testimonies can be reconciled as two separate sales, allowing the shafi' to choose the lower price. Abu Yusuf argues that the buyer's evidence is more confirming and should prevail.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their claims
The shafi' (pre-emptor) and mushtari (buyer) each bring witnesses to establish the sale price, likely claiming different amounts.
2
State the ruling of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad
They hold that the shafi's evidence prevails, because both testimonies can be true if two separate sales occurred; thus the shafi' may choose the price he prefers.
3
State Abu Yusuf's opposing view
Abu Yusuf argues the buyer's evidence is more confirming (akthar ithbatan) and should be accepted, analogizing to cases where seller's evidence prevails over buyer's, agent over principal, and buyer from enemy territory over original owner.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response distinguishing the analogies
The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) distinguish each analogy: in seller-buyer dispute, two consecutive contracts cannot coexist without annulment of the first; in the agent case, similar reasoning applies. Here, no such impossibility exists because the shafi' is not a party to the first contract.
5
Determine the practical consequence and the mufta bihi
If Abu Yusuf's view is followed, the shafi' must pay the higher price. The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, allowing the shafi' to pay the lower price.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ أَقَامَا الْبَيِّنَةَ فَالْبَيِّنَةُ لِلشَّفِيعِ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَمُحَمَّدٍ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ الْبَيِّنَةُ بَيِّنَةُ الْمُشْتَرِي لِأَنَّهَا أَكْثَرُ إِثْبَاتًا فَصَارَ كَبَيِّنَةِ الْبَائِعِ وَالْوَكِيلِ وَالْمُشْتَرِي مِنَ الْعَدُوِّ. وَلَهُمَا أَنَّهُ لَا تَنَافِيَ بَيْنَهُمَا فَيُجْعَلُ كَالْمَوْجُودَ بَيْعَانِ وَلِلشَّفِيعِ أَنْ يَأْخُذَ بِأَيِّهِمَا شَاءَ وَهَذَا بِخِلَافِ الْبَائِعِ مَعَ الْمُشْتَرِي لِأَنَّهُ لَا يَتَوَالَى بَيْنَهُمَا عَقْدَانِ إِلَّا بِانْفِسَاخِ الْأَوَّلِ وَهُهُنَا الْفَسْخُ لَا يَظْهَرُ فِي حَقِّ الشَّفِيعِ.
And if both produce the evidence, then the evidence is for the shafi' according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: The evidence is the evidence of the mushtari because it is more confirming, so it becomes like the evidence of the seller, the agent, and the buyer from the enemy. And for them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad): There is no contradiction between them, so it is as if two sales exist, and the shafi' has the right to take by whichever he wishes. And this is different from the case of seller with buyer because two contracts do not follow consecutively between them except by the annulment of the first, and here the annulment does not appear with respect to the shafi'.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of witnesses (bayyinah) when both the pre-emptor (shafi') and the buyer (mushtari) bring evidence about the price. The text from Al-Quduri states the ruling: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that the shafi's witnesses are preferred, while Abu Yusuf holds that the buyer's witnesses are preferred. Abu Yusuf's reasoning is that the buyer's evidence is more affirming (akthar ithbatan) because it seeks to establish a higher price, similar to cases where the seller's evidence prevails over the buyer's, or the agent's over the principal's, or the purchaser from enemy territory over the original owner. In response, the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) argue that there is no inherent contradiction between the two sets of evidence; both can be harmonized by assuming that two separate sales occurred. Consequently, the shafi' may choose to take the property at the price he prefers. This differs from the seller-buyer dispute because in that case, two consecutive contracts cannot exist without the first being annulled, and annulment does not occur in favor of the shafi'.

Key Terms
الشفعة (al-shuf'ah): The right of pre-emption, allowing a co-owner or neighbor to purchase the sold share at the price paid by the buyer.
الشفيع (al-shafi'): The pre-emptor, the person entitled to take the sold property by shuf'ah.
المشترى (al-mushtari): The buyer who purchased the property from the original seller.
البينة (al-bayyinah): Evidence, specifically witness testimony (shahadah) that establishes a claim in court.
العدو (al-'aduww): The enemy, referring to non-Muslims in dar al-harb from whom a Muslim purchases property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, why is the shafi's evidence preferred over the buyer's when both produce witnesses?
A) Because the shafi' has a stronger claim to the property
B) Because the two testimonies can be reconciled as two separate sales, allowing the shafi' to choose
C) Because the buyer's witnesses are biased
D) Because the seller's consent is required

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school harmonizes conflicting witness testimony in shuf'ah by treating it as two possible sales, giving the shafi' the benefit of choosing the price.

10 min
Preemptor's Evidence Accepted Over Buyer's When Price Disputed
Ruling that preemptor's evidence is accepted due to possibility of two sales

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on conflicting evidence in preemption, explain the qiyas reasoning from the master-slave case, and distinguish it from seller-buyer disputes.

Core Idea
When preemptor and buyer dispute the price, both testimonies can be true if two sales occurred; the preemptor chooses the lower price.

This passage tackles a classic Hanafi procedural ruling: when the preemptor and the buyer disagree on the price paid for property, whose evidence prevails? The Hanafi school, relying on the principle of tathbiq (reconciliation), accepts the preemptor's evidence, reasoning that both parties' testimonies can be harmonized by assuming two separate transactions occurred. This lesson walks you through the proof, the analogy to the master-slave case, and the crucial distinction from seller-buyer disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute and parties
The preemptor (shafi') and the buyer (mushtari) present conflicting testimonies about the sale price. The preemptor claims a lower price; the buyer claims a higher one.
The preemptor has a right to take the property at the actual price paid.
2
Understand the Hanafi claim: no contradiction
The author asserts that there is no real contradiction between the two testimonies because they can be reconciled (tathbiq) by assuming two sales occurred: one at the higher price and another at the lower price.
Reconciliation is preferred over rejecting one testimony.
3
Analyse the qiyas to the master-slave case
The Hanafi school analogizes this case to a master-slave dispute over the price for freedom. In both, both statements can be true if separate promises/sales are assumed.
The illa is the possibility of reconciliation without contradiction.
4
Distinguish from seller-buyer dispute
In a seller-buyer price dispute, a second contract would require rescinding the first, which is not permissible without clear evidence. Hence, the reconciliation does not apply there.
Abu Yusuf accepts the seller's evidence in seller-buyer disputes.
5
Apply the ruling
The preemptor's evidence is accepted; he may take the property at the price he proves. He has the choice to pick whichever of the two assumed sales benefits him.
This protects the preemptor's right while honoring both witnesses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمہ اور طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ان دونوں کے درمیان کوئی منافات نہیں ہے۔ پس یوں قرار دیا جائے گا گویا کہ موجود دو بیع ہیں اور شفیع کیلئے حق ہے کہ ان دونوں میں سے جس کے بدلے میں چاہے لے لے اور یہ حکم بائع اور مشتری کے باہمی اختلاف کے خلاف ہے۔ اسلئے کہ ان دونوں کے درمیان دو عقد متوالی نہیں ہو سکتے مگر اول کے فتح ہونے کے ساتھ اور یہاں فتح ظاہر نہیں ہو گا شفیع کے حق میں۔ تشریح یہاں سے حضرات طرفین کی دلیل ہے کہ شفیع کا بینہ معتبر ہے نہ کہ مشتری کا ۔ اگر چہ شفیع کے گواہ ایک ہزار کی گواہی دیتے ہیں اور مشتری کے دو ہزار کی۔ کے باوجود ان دونوں کے درمیان کوئی تعارض نہیں بلکہ تطبیق ممکن ہے کہ پہلے بائع اور مشتری میں دو ہزار میں معاملہ ملے ہوا ہو اور پھر بائع نے ہزار کم کر دیتے ہوں یا از سرنو دوسری مرتبہ ایک ہزار میں بیچ کر لی ہو تو جب دو بیچ یہاں مانی جاسکتی ہیں اور شفیع کو یہ اختیا ہے کہ جس میں اس کو نفع ہے اس صورت کو اختیار کر لے۔ لہذا اس کو اختیار ہے کہ جونسی بیچ کے سبب سے چاہے اس گھر کو شفعہ میں لے لے۔ سوال جیسے آپ نے یہ تاویل کر کے شفیع کے بینہ کو معتبر قرار دیا ہے۔ ایسے ہی اگر بائع اور مشتری کے درمیان اختلاف ہو جائے تو وہاں بھی مشتری کے بینہ کا اعتبار ہونا چاہئے ۔ مگر وہاں آپ نے ابو یوسف کے قول کے مطابق بائع کے بینہ کو معتبر مانا ہے؟ جواب شفیع کے حق میں دو متوالی عقد حسب مذکور چل سکتے ہیں اور بائع ومشتری کے حق میں دوسرا عقد جاری ہونے کیلئے اول کا انفساخ ضروری ہے اس لئے ہم نے یہ تاویل وہاں جاری نہیں کی۔ اور پہلی صورت میں فتح کا ظہور عاقدین کے درمیان ہوگا۔ شفیع کے حق میں نہ ہو گا۔ اس لئے یہ تاویل چلی گئی۔ خلاصہ کلام بائع اور مشتری کے مسئلہ کو مشتری اور شفیع کے مسئلہ پر قیاس کرنا قیاس مع الفارق ہے۔ کیونکہ دونوں کے درمیان مناسبت نہیں ہے۔ مشتری اور شفیع کا مسئلہ ایسا ہے جیسے آقا اور غلام کا مسئلہ کہ غلام کہتا ہے کہ مولیٰ نے کہا تھا کہ اگر تو ہزار روپے دے دے تو تو آزاد ہے اور مولی کہا ہے کہ میں نے یوں کہا تھا کہ اگر تو دو ہزار روپے دے دے تو تو آزاد ہے۔ تو ہم نے ان دونوں میں تطبیق دی اور کہا کہ غلام نے ان دونوں میں سے جو مقدار بھی ادا کر دی تو وہ آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ یہی حال شفیع کا ہے۔ مجمع الانہر ص ۴۵۸ ج ۲ پر ہے، ولانه يمكن صدق البينين بجريان العقد مرتين فيجعلان موجودين فالشفيع ياخذ بايها شاء
Translation: And the proof of the two parties (shafi' and mushtari) is that there is no contradiction between them. So it will be decided as if two sales exist, and the shafi' has the right to take whichever of the two he wishes as the price. This ruling is contrary to the case of disagreement between seller and buyer, because between those two, two consecutive contracts cannot occur except with the rescission of the first, and rescission is not apparent here in the right of the shafi'. Explanation: Here the proof of the two parties is that the evidence of the shafi' is reliable, not that of the buyer. Even if the shafi''s witnesses testify for one thousand and the buyer's for two thousand, there is no contradiction between them; rather, reconciliation is possible: perhaps first the seller and buyer agreed on two thousand, then the seller reduced it by a thousand, or he sold it anew for one thousand a second time. Thus two sales can be assumed here, and the shafi' has the choice to adopt whichever benefits him. Therefore he has the right to take the house in preemption by whichever sale he wishes. Question: If you have thus reconciled the preemptor's evidence, similarly if there is a disagreement between seller and buyer, shouldn't the buyer's evidence be accepted? But there you, according to Abu Yusuf, accepted the seller's evidence. Answer: In the preemptor's right, two consecutive contracts can occur as mentioned, whereas in the seller-buyer's right, for a second contract to occur, the first must be rescinded, so we did not apply that reconciliation there. In the first case, the rescission is apparent between the contracting parties, not in the preemptor's right, so the reconciliation applies. Summary: To analogize the seller-buyer case to the buyer-preemptor case is an analogy with a difference because there is no correspondence between them. The preemptor-buyer case is like the master-slave case where the slave says the master said 'If you give one thousand rupees, you are free,' and the master says 'I said if you give two thousand rupees, you are free.' We reconciled them and said the slave becomes free by paying whichever amount he fulfills. This is the situation of the shafi'. In Majma' al-Anhur, volume 2 page 458: 'And because both evidences can be true by the contract occurring twice, so they are both considered existing, and the preemptor takes whichever he wishes.'
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage establishes the ruling that when the preemptor (shafi') and the buyer (mushtari) disagree on the price, the preemptor's evidence is accepted over the buyer's. The passage type is a ruling with proof (talil) and includes a question-answer clarifying the distinction from the seller-buyer dispute. The author, following the Hanafi school, argues that the two conflicting pieces of evidence can be reconciled by positing that two separate sales took place: one at the higher price and another at the lower price. Since the preemptor's right is to take the property at the price actually paid, he can choose whichever sale he prefers. The proof is rational ('aqli) based on the possibility of reconciliation (tathbiq), not a direct textual source. The author compares this to the master-slave case: if the master promises freedom for a certain payment and disputes the amount, the slave becomes free by paying whatever amount he proves. Similarly, the preemptor takes the property at the price he proves. The passage also addresses a potential objection: why not apply the same reasoning to seller-buyer disputes? The author explains that in a seller-buyer dispute, a second contract cannot occur without rescinding the first, but in the preemptor's case, no rescission is needed because the preemptor is not a party to the original contract. Thus, the Hanafi position is that the preemptor's evidence is accepted, and this ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah as reflected in Majma' al-Anhur. The key legal principle is that when evidence can be reconciled, it is done so to uphold both testimonies.

Key Terms
شفیع (shafi'): The preemptor who has the right to purchase property that has been sold to a third party by paying the sale price to the buyer.
بینہ (bayyinah): Legal evidence, usually testimonial witnesses, presented in court to prove a claim.
تطبیق (tatbiq): Reconciliation or harmonization of apparently conflicting evidence by positing separate events or circumstances.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the preemptor (shafi') brings witnesses that the price was 1000 and the buyer brings witnesses that it was 2000, how does the Hanafi school resolve this conflict?
A) The preemptor's evidence is rejected because the buyer's evidence is stronger.
B) The buyer's evidence is accepted because he paid the price.
C) The preemptor's evidence is accepted, and he may take the property at 1000.
D) The case is dismissed due to conflicting evidence.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts the preemptor's evidence in a price dispute because it can be reconciled with the buyer's by assuming two sales, and the preemptor must have the actual price he pays.

Refuting Abu Yusuf's Analogies on Preemptor's Evidence
Refuting Abu Yusuf's analogies in preemption evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the preemptor-buyer case from the agent-principal and enemy-sale cases in Hanafi fiqh and explain why the preemptor's evidence is accepted.

Core Idea
In preemption, the preemptor's evidence is accepted because his claim does not require rescission, unlike other analogies.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute where Imam Abu Yusuf analogized the preemption case to other evidentiary scenarios to argue that the buyer's evidence should be accepted. The author of Al-Hidayah refutes these analogies, affirming the Zahir al-Riwayah position that the preemptor's evidence prevails. Understanding the distinction hinges on whether reconciliation of evidence is possible without assuming a rescission of the sale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central issue
Recognize that the dispute is about whose evidence is accepted when the preemptor (shafi') and buyer (mushtari) disagree on the price paid for the property.
The preemptor claims a lower price to take possession at that price; the buyer claims a higher price to deter preemption.
2
Examine Abu Yusuf's first analogy (agent-principal)
Abu Yusuf argued that just as in an agent-principal dispute over price, the agent's (or buyer's) evidence is accepted, so too in preemption the buyer's evidence should be accepted. The Hanafi response distinguishes: in the agent case, reconciliation would require assuming the agent rescinded the first sale, which is not permissible without proof, but in preemption the preemptor's right is separate and does not involve rescission.
The text also notes that Imam Muhammad's narration (via Ibn Sama'ah) actually says the principal's evidence is accepted, further weakening the analogy.
3
Examine Abu Yusuf's third analogy (buyer from enemy)
Abu Yusuf cited the case where a buyer purchases from an enemy and disputes with the original owner; there the buyer's evidence is often accepted. The Hanafi response: first, Imam Muhammad in al-Siyar al-Kabir states the original owner's evidence is accepted. Second, even if the buyer's evidence were accepted, the reasoning is that rescission is needed, unlike preemption.
The key is that in enemy sale, the second contract cannot coexist with the first without rescission.
4
Understand the key distinction: tatbiq without rescission
In preemption, the preemptor's claim does not require the first sale to be rescinded; he simply exercises a right to take the property at the price paid. Therefore, the two claims (preemptor says lower price, buyer says higher) can be reconciled by assuming two separate sales (one actual, one claimed), but in agent-principal and enemy sale cases, reconciliation would force the assumption of a rescission that has no basis.
This is the core of the Hanafi tarjih: the preemptor's evidence is binding (mulzima) whereas the buyer's is not.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position is that the preemptor's evidence is accepted, following Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad (Zahir al-Riwayah). Abu Yusuf's view is rejected because the analogies fail on distinction.
This ruling remains operative in Hanafi fatwa today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل کا جواب ایک نظیر سے
وهو التخريج لبيئة الوكيل لانه كالبائع والموكل كالمشترى منه كيف وانها ممنوعة على ماروى عن محمد ترجمہ اور یہی تخریج ہے وکیل کے بینہ کی اس لئے کہ وکیل بائع کے مثل ہے اور موکل وکیل سے خریدنے والے سے مثل ہے کیسے ہو سکتا ہے یہ ( بینہ وکیل کا قیاس بین مشتری پر ) حالانکہ یہ ممنوع ہے اس روایت کے مطابق جو ہم محمد سے مروی ہے۔ تشریح یہاں سے حضرت مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ ہم نے امام ابو یوسف کو جواب دیتے ہوئے جو تقریر بائع اور مشتری کے اختلاف میں کی ہے۔ بالکل یہی تقریر وکیل اور موکل کے اختلاف میں کی جائے گی۔ یعنی جس طرح بائع اور مشتری کے اختلاف کی صورت میں تطبیق ممکن نہیں وجہ مذکور کے مطابق اسی طرح وکیل اور مؤکل کے اختلاف کی صورت میں تطبیق ممکن نہیں ۔ مگر عقد اول کو فتح مان کر اور مشتری اور شفیع کے اختلاف میں تطبیق ممکن ہے کیونکہ فسخ کا ظہور شفیع کے حق میں نہ ہوگا۔
خلاصہ کلام بائع اور مشتری کی صورت میں جیسے بائع کا بینہ معتبر ہوا ایسے ہی وکیل اور موکل کی صورت میں وکیل کا بینہ معتبر ہوگا۔ مگر مشتری اور شفیع کی صورت میں شفیع کا بینہ معتبر ہوگا۔ اور شفیع کو ان دونوں پر قیاس کرنا صحیح نہ ہوگا۔
اسی مضمون کو مصنف نے وهو التخريج .... الخ سے بیان کیا ہے یعنی یہی تقریر مذکور نکالنے والی ہے اور مخرج ہے۔ اس مسئلہ کیلئے جو وکیل کے بعینہ سے متعلق ہے۔ کیونکہ وکیل ایسا ہے جیسے بائع ، اور مؤکل ایسا ہے جیسے مشتری ۔
كيف وانها... الخ ۔ فرماتے ہیں کہ جو تقریر ہم نے اب تک کی ہے یہ تو ظاہر الروایہ کے مطابق ہے جس میں وکیل کے بعینہ کا اعتبار کیا گیا ہے۔ ورنہ ابن سماعہ نے امام محمد سے یہ روایت کیا ہے کہ وکیل اور موکل کے اختلاف کی صورت میں موکل کا بینہ معتبر ہو گا نہ کہ وکیل کا۔ لہذا اگر اس روایت کا اعتبار کیا جائے پھر تو امام ابو یوسف کا وکیل والے مسئلہ کو استشہاد میں پیش کرنا ہی درست نہ ہوگا ۔ اس کو فرمایا کہ یہ قیاس کیسے ہو سکتا ہے۔ حالانکہ امام محمد کی روایت کے مطابق یہ ممنوع ہے۔
امام ابو یوسف کے تیسرے استشہاد کا جواب
واما المشترى من العدو قلنا ذكر في السير الكبير ان البيئة بيئة المالك القديم فلنا ان نمنع وبعد التسليم نقول لا يصح الثاني هناك الا بفسخ الاول اما ههنا بخلافه ولان بينة الشفيع ملزمة وبينة المشترى غير ملزمة والبينات للالزام
ترجمہ اور بہر حال دشمن سے خریدنے والا تو ہم کہیں گے کہ سیر کبیر میں مذکور ہے کہ مالک قدیم کابینہ معتبر ہوگا۔ تو ہمارے لئے حق ہے کہ ہم انکار کر دیں اور تسلیم کرنے کے بعد ہم کہیں گے کہ وہاں عقدثانی صبح نہ ہوگا۔ مگر اول فسخ کر کے بہر حال یہاں اس کے خلاف ہے اور اسلئے کہ شفیع کا بینہ لازم کرنے والا ہے اور مشتری کا بعینہ لازم کرنے والا نہیں ہے اور بینات الزام کیلئے ہے۔ تشریح امام ابو یوسف نے اپنے قول پر تین شواہد پیش کئے تھے ان میں سے دو کا جواب ہو چکا ہے یہ تیسرے کا جواب ہے کہ آپ نے فرمایا که مشتری من العدو اور مالک قدیم کے اختلاف کی صورت میں مشتری کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔ حالانکہ امام محمد نے سیر کبیر میں فرمایا ہے کہ صورت مذکورہ میں مالک قدیم کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔ لہذا ہمیں حق ہے کہ یوں عرض کر دیں کہ
اس مسئلہ کو استشہاد میں پیش کرنا مفید نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ایسے مقام پر ایسی جزئی پیش کی جاتی ہے جو خصم کے نزدیک مسلم ہو۔ اور چلئے اگر ہم تسلیم بھی کر لیں کہ مشتری من العدو کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔ پھر بھی ہم یہ عرض کریں گے کہ اس کی وجہ وہی ہے جو گذر چکی۔ یعنی دونوں کے درمیان تطبیق کی صورت نہیں ہے۔ علاوہ عقد اول کو مسخ ماننے کے۔
اور مشتری اور شفیع والا مسئلہ اس سے جدا گانہ ہے کہ وہاں شفیع کے حق میں فسخ کا ظہور نہیں ہوگا۔
خلاصہ کلام مشتری اور شفیع کے مسئلہ پر ان تینوں کو نہ شواہد بنا کر پیش کیا جاسکتا ہے اور نہ ان پر مشتری اور شفیع کے مسئلہ کو قیاس کیا جا سکتا ہے ان وجوہات کی وجہ سے جو مذکور ہوئیں۔
Translation: Answer to Imam Abu Yusuf's proof by an example: This is the deriving of the evidence of the agent because he is like the seller, and the principal is like the buyer from him. How can this (analogy of agent's evidence to buyer's evidence) be allowed while it is prohibited according to what was narrated from Muhammad. Explanation: The author says that the same reasoning we gave in the seller-buyer dispute will be applied to the agent-principal dispute. That is, just as reconciliation is not possible in the seller-buyer case for the reason mentioned, similarly reconciliation is not possible in the agent-principal case, except by assuming rescission of the first contract, but in the preemptor-buyer case, reconciliation is possible because rescission is not apparent in the preemptor's right. Summary: In the seller-buyer case, the seller's evidence is accepted; similarly, in the agent-principal case, the agent's evidence is accepted. But in the buyer-preemptor case, the preemptor's evidence is accepted. To analogize the preemptor to these two is incorrect. The author expressed this meaning with 'This is the deriving...' i.e., this same reasoning is the extraction and derivation for the issue of the agent's evidence, because the agent is like the seller, and the principal like the buyer. 'How can this be...' He says that the reasoning we have given so far is according to the Zahir al-Riwayah, which accepts the agent's evidence. Otherwise, Ibn Sama'ah narrated from Imam Muhammad that in the agent-principal dispute, the principal's evidence is accepted, not the agent's. Therefore, if that narration is considered, then Abu Yusuf's citing the agent case as an example is not valid. He said: how can this analogy be made while it is prohibited according to Imam Muhammad's narration. Answer to Imam Abu Yusuf's third evidence: As for the buyer from the enemy, we say it is mentioned in al-Siyar al-Kabir that the evidence is that of the old owner. So we have the right to deny it. And after accepting it, we say that there the second contract is not valid except by rescinding the first, which is contrary to here. And because the preemptor's evidence is binding, while the buyer's evidence is not binding, and evidences are for binding. Explanation: Imam Abu Yusuf presented three proofs for his statement; two have been answered. This is the answer to the third. He said that in the dispute between the buyer from the enemy and the old owner, the buyer's statement is accepted. But Imam Muhammad said in al-Siyar al-Kabir that in the mentioned case, the old owner's statement is accepted. So we have the right to say that presenting this issue as an example is not beneficial because such a precedent is only presented when it is accepted by the opponent. And even if we accept that the buyer from the enemy's statement is accepted, we still say that the reason is the same as before: there is no possibility of reconciliation except by assuming rescission of the first. The buyer-preemptor case is different because there rescission is not apparent in the preemptor's right. Summary: These three cases cannot be presented as evidence for the buyer-preemptor case, nor can the buyer-preemptor case be analogized to them, for the reasons mentioned.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage contains an intra-Hanafi dispute where the author refutes three arguments of Imam Abu Yusuf concerning the acceptance of evidence in preemption disputes. The first argument analogized to the agent-principal dispute, but the author distinguishes it by noting that in the agent-principal case, reconciliation is not possible without rescission, whereas in the preemptor-buyer case it is. The author also points out that according to a narration from Imam Muhammad via Ibn Sama'ah, in the agent-principal case the principal's evidence is accepted, not the agent's, so Abu Yusuf's analogy fails even if that narration is used. The second argument (not explicitly mentioned here) is presumably the seller-buyer dispute already addressed in the previous lesson. The third argument analogizes to the case of buying from an enemy (a non-Muslim hostile) where the buyer's evidence is accepted. The author refutes this by citing Imam Muhammad's view in al-Siyar al-Kabir that the old owner's evidence is accepted. Even if one accepted the buyer's evidence in that case, the reasoning is different because there the second contract requires rescission of the first, which is not required in preemption. The author concludes that all three analogies are invalid. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that the preemptor's evidence is accepted over the buyer's. The authority weight of this ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah as per Imam Muhammad, and the opposing views of Abu Yusuf are overridden.

Key Terms
وکیل (wakil): An agent appointed by the principal to perform a sale or purchase.
موکل (muwakkil): The principal who appoints the agent.
مشتری من العدو (mushtari min al-'aduww): A buyer who purchases property from an enemy (non-Muslim belligerent) during war, which may have special rulings regarding ownership.
بينة الشفيع (bayyinat al-shafi'): The evidence presented by the preemptor to prove the sale price.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The analogy is accepted, so the buyer's evidence is preferred.
B) The analogy is rejected because in the agent-principal case, reconciliation is not possible without rescission, while in preemption it is.

Key Takeaway
The preemptor's evidence is accepted because his claim does not require rescission of the sale, unlike the analogies cited by Abu Yusuf.

Preemptor's Testimony versus Buyer's Testimony: Rational Proof and Rebuttal of Analogy
Refutation of Imam Abu Yusuf's third evidence and rational proof for preemptor's testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whose testimony is authoritative in a shuf'a price dispute and explain the rational proof (dalil aqli) that supports it.

Core Idea
The preemptor's testimony is authoritative because it binds the buyer; the buyer's testimony cannot force the preemptor to buy.

In a shuf'a dispute, the preemptor and buyer may disagree on the sale price. Whose testimony should the qadi accept? This lesson explores the Hanafi position, which gives precedence to the preemptor's testimony based on a rational proof: testimony serves to impose an obligation (ilzam), and only the preemptor's testimony can bind the other party. We also examine how Imam Abu Yusuf's analogy to the agent-principal case is rejected, and how his third precedent—the buyer from the enemy—is distinguished.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue and the Hanafi position
State the core question: whose testimony prevails when preemptor and buyer dispute the price? The Hanafi position (Zahir al-Riwayah) is that the preemptor's testimony is authoritative.
This is the starting point; understand the practical impact on the outcome.
2
Understand the rational proof (ilzam)
The passage argues that testimony is for binding (ilzam). The preemptor's testimony can force the buyer to sell at the proven price, whereas the buyer's testimony cannot force the preemptor to buy. Thus, the binding effect resides with the preemptor.
Contrast: if buyer proves a higher price, preemptor can walk away; no binding on him.
3
Examine Imam Abu Yusuf's third precedent (buyer from enemy)
Abu Yusuf analogized the preemptor-buyer dispute to the case of a buyer from a usurper (dealing with enemy property). The rebuttal cites al-Siyar al-Kabir: the original owner's testimony is authoritative, not the buyer's.
Even if we accept the buyer's testimony there, it is because annulment of the first contract is needed, unlike here.
4
Distinguish the agent-principal case
In the agent-principal dispute, the Zahir al-Riwayah says the agent's testimony is authoritative (like seller-buyer). But Ibn Sama'ah narrates from Imam Muhammad that the principal's testimony is authoritative. This variation does not affect the preemptor rule because the preemptor is not analogous to an agent.
The preemptor's unique binding effect (ilzam) sets it apart.
5
Summarize the mufta bihi and practical consequence
The relied-upon position is the preemptor's testimony. As a result, if the preemptor proves a lower price, the buyer must sell at that price; if the buyer proves a higher price, the preemptor can abandon the claim.
This protects the preemptor from being forced into an unfavorable purchase.

اختلاف کی صورت میں تطبیق ممکن نہیں ۔ مگر عقد اول کو فتح مان کر اور مشتری اور شفیع کے اختلاف میں تطبیق ممکن ہے کیونکہ فسخ کا ظہور شفیع کے حق میں نہ ہوگا۔ خلاصہ کلام بائع اور مشتری کی صورت میں جیسے بائع جواب ہے کہ آپ نے فرمایا که مشتری من العدو اور مالک قدیم کے اختلاف کی صورت میں مشتری کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔ حالانکہ امام محمد نے سیر کبیر میں فرمایا ہے کہ صورت مذکورہ میں مالک قدیم کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔ لہذا کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔ پھر بھی ہم یہ عرض کریں گے کہ اس کی وجہ وہی ہے جو گذر چکی۔ یعنی دونوں کے درمیان تطبیق کی صورت نہیں ہے۔ علاوہ عقد اول کو مسخ ماننے کے۔ اور مشتری اور شفیع والا مسئلہ اس سے جدا گانہ ہے کہ وہاں شفیع کے حق میں فسخ کا ظہور نہیں ہوگا۔ خلاصہ کلام مشتری اور شفیع کے مسئلہ پر ان تینوں کو نہ شواہد بنا کر پیش کیا جاسکتا ہے اور نہ ان پر مشتری اور شفیع کے مسئلہ کو قیاس کیا جا سکتا ہے ان وجوہات کی وجہ سے جو مذکور ہوئیں۔ پھر طرفین کی جانب سے دلیل عقلی پیش کی گئی جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ بینہ کا کام الزام ہے۔ لہذا جس کے بعینہ میں الزام ہو اس کا بینہ معتبر ہوگا۔ اب ہم نے دیکھا کہ الزام شفیع کے بعینہ میں ہے نہ کہ مشتری کے، اسلئے کہ اگر مشتری نے دو ہزار پر بیع ثابت کر دی تو شفیع شفعہ کو چھوڑ دے۔ یہ کر سکتا ہے مشتری اس پر کچھ لازم نہیں کر سکتا۔ اور اگر شفیع ہزار پر بیچ ثابت کر دے تو مشتری کو مکان اسی قیمت پر دینا ہوگا۔ لہذا معلوم ہوا کہ لازم کرنے والا شفیع کا بینہ ہے مشتری کا نہیں لہذا جو ملزم ہو اس کا اعتبار کرنا پڑے گا۔
Reconciliation is not possible in the case of dispute, but by considering the first contract as valid, reconciliation is possible between the buyer and the preemptor because annulment does not manifest in favor of the preemptor. Summary: In the case of seller and buyer, just as the seller's testimony is authoritative, similarly in the case of agent and principal, the agent's testimony is authoritative. But in the case of buyer and preemptor, the preemptor's testimony is authoritative. And it is not correct to analogize the preemptor to those two. The author expressed this meaning with 'wa huwa al-takhreej...' etc. That is, this discussion is extractive and is a derivation for this issue related to the agent's testimony. Because the agent is like the seller, and the principal is like the buyer. 'Kayfa wa annaha...' etc. He says: The discussion we have had so far is according to Zahir al-Riwayah, in which the agent's testimony is considered. Otherwise, Ibn Sama'ah narrated from Imam Muhammad that in the case of dispute between agent and principal, the principal's testimony is authoritative, not the agent's. Therefore, if this narration is considered, then Imam Abu Yusuf's presenting the agent's issue as a precedent would not be correct. He said: How can this analogy be? While according to Imam Muhammad's narration, it is prohibited. The answer to Imam Abu Yusuf's third istishhad: 'Wa amma al-mushtari min al-'aduww qulna dhukira fi al-Siyar al-Kabir anna al-bayyinata bayyinatu al-maliki al-qadimi falana an namna' wa ba'da al-taslim naqulu la yasihhu al-thani hunaka illa bi faskhi al-awwal amma hahuna bikhilafihi wa li'anna bayyinata al-shafi'i mulzimatum wa bayyinatu al-mushtari ghayr mulzima wa al-bayyinatu lil-ilzam.' Translation: And regarding the one who buys from the enemy, we say: It is mentioned in al-Siyar al-Kabir that the testimony is the testimony of the original owner. So we have the right to deny, and after acceptance we say that the second contract there is not valid except by annulling the first. Here it is different. And because the preemptor's testimony is binding and the buyer's testimony is not binding, and testimonies are for binding. Elaboration: Imam Abu Yusuf presented three precedents for his statement, two have been answered; this is the answer to the third. You said that in the case of dispute between the buyer from the enemy and the original owner, the buyer's statement is authoritative. However, Imam Muhammad said in al-Siyar al-Kabir that in the mentioned case, the original owner's statement is authoritative. Therefore, we have the right to say that presenting this issue as a precedent is not useful. Because at such a place, a detail is presented that is accepted by the opponent. And even if we accept that the buyer from the enemy's statement is authoritative, we would still say that the reason is what has passed, i.e., there is no possibility of reconciliation except by considering the first contract as annulled. And the issue of buyer and preemptor is separate from that because there annulment does not appear in favor of the preemptor. Summary: The three cannot be presented as precedents for the issue of buyer and preemptor, nor can the issue of buyer and preemptor be analogized to them, due to the reasons mentioned. Then, from both sides, a rational proof was presented, the gist of which is that the function of testimony is binding. Therefore, the testimony of the one against whom binding occurs will be authoritative. Now we see that binding occurs in the preemptor's case, not the buyer's, because if the buyer proves the sale at two thousand, the preemptor can leave the pre-emption; he can do this, the buyer cannot impose anything on him. And if the preemptor proves the sale at one thousand, the buyer must give the property at that price. Therefore, it is known that it is the preemptor's testimony that is binding, not the buyer's. So the one who imposes must be considered.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute and rational proof regarding whose testimony is authoritative in a shuf'a case when the preemptor and buyer disagree on the price. The author begins by stating that reconciliation (tatbiq) is not possible in the case of dispute between seller and buyer, but by treating the first contract as valid, reconciliation is possible between buyer and preemptor because annulment (faskh) does not manifest in favor of the preemptor (i.e., the preemptor's right arises without annulling the buyer's contract). The summary is that in the seller-buyer dispute, the seller's testimony is authoritative; in the agent-principal dispute, the agent's testimony is authoritative; but in the buyer-preemptor dispute, the preemptor's testimony is authoritative. Analogizing the preemptor to the seller or agent is incorrect. The author then explains that the discussion so far is according to Zahir al-Riwayah (the well-known position in Imam Muhammad's works), but Ibn Sama'ah narrated from Imam Muhammad that in the agent-principal case, the principal's testimony is authoritative, not the agent's. If that narration is accepted, then Imam Abu Yusuf's precedent (istishhad) of the agent case would be invalid. The text then answers Imam Abu Yusuf's third precedent: the case of a buyer from a usurper (al-mushtari min al-'aduww). The reply cites al-Siyar al-Kabir where Imam Muhammad states that the original owner's testimony is authoritative, contradicting Abu Yusuf's claim. Even if we accept that the buyer's testimony is authoritative there, it differs because reconciliation is only possible by annulling the first contract, whereas in the preemptor case, no annulment is needed. Finally, a rational proof (dalil 'aqli) is given: testimony is for binding (ilzam). The preemptor's testimony is binding because if he proves a lower price, the buyer must sell at that price; if the buyer proves a higher price, the preemptor can simply walk away. Thus, the preemptor's testimony imposes a binding obligation, so it is authoritative.

Key Terms
شفعة (shuf'a): The right of pre-emption: the ability of a co-owner or neighbor to purchase a property that has been sold to a third party at the same price.
شفیع (shafi'): The preemptor who exercises the right of shuf'a.
بینہ (bayyina): Legal testimony or evidence, especially from two witnesses, used to prove a claim in court.
الزام (ilzam): The binding effect of testimony that imposes an obligation on the opposing party.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the rational proof in this passage, why is the preemptor's testimony considered authoritative over the buyer's in a price dispute?
A) The preemptor is a more reliable witness because he is not a party to the original contract.
B) The preemptor's testimony can bind the buyer to sell at the proven price, while the buyer's testimony cannot force the preemptor to buy.
C) The preemptor always has two witnesses and the buyer only has one.
D) The buyer's testimony is not admissible because he is the defendant.

Key Takeaway
The preemptor's testimony is authoritative in price disputes because it carries the element of ilzam (binding obligation), a principle derived from the purpose of testimony itself.

Preemptor Pays at Seller's Stated Price When Price Disputed Before Payment
Ruling on preemptor's payment when seller and buyer dispute price before payment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the preemptor's obligation when seller and buyer dispute the price before payment, and explain the two rational proofs supporting it.

Core Idea
When seller and buyer disagree on price before payment, the preemptor pays the seller's claimed price because ownership stems from the seller's offer.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in the law of pre-emption (shuf'a): the seller and buyer have disputed the sale price, and before the seller has received payment, the preemptor comes to exercise his right. At what price must the preemptor pay? The Hanafi school, as recorded by Imam al-Quduri, provides a clear ruling supported by two complementary proofs. Let's walk through the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute scenario
The seller and buyer disagree on the sale price; the seller claims a lower amount, the buyer claims a higher amount. The seller has not yet taken possession of the price (qabd al-thaman).
This condition is crucial: the seller's demand for payment is still outstanding.
2
State the ruling
Imam al-Quduri rules that the preemptor takes the property at the price claimed by the seller, not the buyer. This is the mufta bihi position.
The buyer's higher claim is treated as if the seller has remitted the difference.
3
Analyze the first proof: the two possibilities
If the seller's claim is true, pre-emption is established at that price. If the buyer's claim is true, the seller's lower claim is construed as a remission (hitt) of part of the price, which benefits the preemptor.
In both scenarios, the seller's statement produces the same outcome for the preemptor.
4
Analyze the second proof: the seller's ijab
The preemptor's right to ownership derives from the seller's offer (ijab). Therefore, the seller's statement regarding the price is authoritative as long as his claim remains (i.e., he hasn't received payment).
This is a rational proof (talil) based on contract formation principles.
5
Apply to a concrete example
Example: Seller says price is 1000, buyer says 2000. The preemptor pays 1000. If truth is with seller, pre-emption is at 1000. If truth is with buyer, seller is deemed to have remitted 1000, which passes to the preemptor.
The preemptor never pays more than the seller's claim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بائع اور مشتری کا شمن میں اختلاف ہوا بائع کم اور مشتری زیادتی کا دعوی کرے اور بائع نے ثمن پر ابھی قبضہ نہیں کیا ہے تو شفیع کس شمن سے وصول کرے گا قال واذا ادعى المشترى ثمنا وادعى البائع اقل منه ولم يقبض الثمن اخذها الشفيع بما قاله البائع وكان ذالک خطأ عن المشترى وهذا لان الامر ان كان على ما قال البائع فقد وجبت الشفعة به وان كان على ما قال المشترى فقد حط البائع بعض الثمن وهذا الحط يظهر فى حق الشفيع على ما تبين ان شاء الله تعالى ولان التملك على البائع بايجابه فكان القول قوله في مقدار الثمن ما بقيت مطالبته فياخذ الشفيع بقوله ترجمہ امام قدوری نے فرمایا اور جبکہ مشتری نے شمن کا دعوی کیا اور بائع نے اس سے کم کا دعویٰ کیا۔ حالانکہ بائع نے ثمن پر قبضہ نہیں کیا تو شفیع اس مکان کو اس مقدار سے لے گا۔ جو بائع کہہ رہا ہے اور یہ مشتری کے اوپر سے کم کرنا ہوگا۔ اور یہ اسلئے کہ بات اگر ایسے ہی ہے جو بائع کہہ رہا ہے تو شفعہ اسی مقدار کے مطابق ثابت ہو گا اور بات اگر ایسی ہے جو مشتری کہہ رہا ہے تو بائع نے شمن کی بعض مقدار کو کم کر دیا ہے اور یہ کی شفیع کے حق میں ظاہر ہوگی ۔ تفصیل کے مطابق جس کو ہم انشاء اللہ تعالیٰ بیان کریں گے اور اسلئے کہ بائع پر مالک ہونا اسکے ایجاب کی جہ سے ہے تو جب تک اس کا مطالبہ باقی ہے مقدارشن میں اسی کا قول معتبر ہوگا تو شفیع بائع کے قول کے مطابق لے گا تشریح ابھی تک بائع نے شمن پر قبضہ نہیں کیا اور بائع ایک ہزار روپے میں بیچنا بتاتا ہے اور مشتری دو ہزار میں تو یوں سمجھیں گے کہ شفیع نے کچھ من کم کر دیا اور یہ کی شفیع کے حق میں بھی ظاہر ہوگی۔ لہذا شفیع بائع کے قول کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے شمن کی کم مقدار پر دار مشفوعہ کو لے گا کیونکہ نفس الامر میں یا تو بائع حق پر ہے یا مشتری۔ پہلی صورت میں تو بائع کا قول معتبر ماننے میں کچھ کلام ہی نہیں اور دوسری صورت میں اس کوشن کے کم کر دینے پر محمول کیا جائے گا۔ لہذا بہر صورت بائع کے قول کا اعتبار ہوگا۔ لان التملك ... الخ - سے دلیل عقلی پیش کرتے ہیں کہ شفیع کو شفعہ ملنے کی وجہ بائع کا ایجاب ہے یعنی بائع کے ایجاب کی وجہ سے شفیع کو حق تملک حاصل ہوا ہے۔ لہذا جب بات یوں ہے تو جب تک بائع کا مطالبہ ( من ) باقی ہے اس کا قول معتبر ہو گا۔
The seller and buyer disputed over the price; the seller claimed a lower amount and the buyer claimed a higher amount, and the seller has not yet taken possession of the price. So with which price will the preemptor take? He (Al-Quduri) said: And when the buyer claims a price and the seller claims less than it, and he has not taken possession of the price, the preemptor takes it (the property) at what the seller said, and that will be a reduction from the buyer. This is because if the matter is as the seller says, then the pre-emption becomes established accordingly; and if it is as the buyer says, then the seller has remitted some of the price, and this remission appears in favor of the preemptor, as will be explained, God willing. And because ownership is based on the seller's offer, so his statement is authoritative regarding the amount of the price as long as his demand remains; thus the preemptor takes according to his statement. Translation: Imam Al-Quduri said: And when the buyer claims a price and the seller claims less than it, while the seller has not taken possession of the price, then the preemptor will take the property at the amount the seller says, and this will be a reduction from the buyer. This is because if the matter is as the seller says, then the pre-emption is established accordingly; and if the matter is as the buyer says, then the seller has remitted some of the price, and this remission will appear in favor of the preemptor, according to the detail we will explain, God willing. And because ownership of the seller is due to his offer, so as long as his claim remains, his statement regarding the amount of the price is authoritative, so the preemptor takes according to his statement. Elaboration: The seller has not yet taken possession of the price; the seller says he sold for one thousand rupees, and the buyer says for two thousand. So it will be understood that the seller has remitted some amount, and this remission will also appear in favor of the preemptor. Therefore, the preemptor, relying on the seller's statement, will take the pre-empted property at the lower amount, because in reality either the seller is correct or the buyer. In the first case, there is no issue with considering the seller's statement authoritative; in the second case, it will be construed as a remission of the price. So in both cases, the seller's statement is authoritative. 'Li'anna al-tamalluk...' etc. – he presents a rational proof: the reason the preemptor gets pre-emption is the seller's offer, i.e., due to the seller's offer, the preemptor obtains the right of ownership. So when this is the case, as long as the seller's claim (of the price) remains, his statement is authoritative.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from Imam al-Quduri's text (matn) on the law of pre-emption (shuf'a). The scenario: the seller and buyer disagree on the sale price before the seller has received payment. The preemptor (shafi') chooses to exercise his right of pre-emption. The question is: at what price should he pay? The ruling: the preemptor pays the amount claimed by the seller, and the buyer is considered to have remitted the difference. The reasoning is twofold: (1) If the seller's claim is true, then the pre-emption right is established at that price. If the buyer's claim is true, then the seller's lower claim is taken as a remission (hitt) of part of the price, and this remission benefits the preemptor. (2) The preemptor's right to ownership stems from the seller's offer (ijab); therefore, the seller's statement regarding the price is authoritative as long as his claim remains unpaid (i.e., he has not yet received the price). The Urdu commentary explains with an example: seller says 1,000, buyer says 2,000. The preemptor pays 1,000. If the truth is with the buyer, the seller has effectively given a discount of 1,000, which passes to the preemptor. The underlying principle is that the seller's offer is the basis of the preemptor's right, so the seller's word on the price is taken.

Key Terms
ثمن (thaman): The sale price in a contract of sale.
ایجاب (ijab): The offer made by the seller, which is the basis for the preemptor's right of ownership.
حط (hitt): Remission or reduction of a part of the price by the seller.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the ruling in this passage, if the seller and buyer disagree on the price before payment, at what price does the preemptor take the property?
A) The price claimed by the buyer.
B) The price claimed by the seller.
C) The average of the two prices.
D) The market value determined by experts.

Key Takeaway
The preemptor always pays the seller's claimed price when the price is disputed before payment, because the seller's offer is the basis of the preemptor's right.

Shafi' Follows Seller's Price When Seller Has Not Received Payment
Ruling on which party's price the shafi' adopts when seller and buyer dispute and seller has not taken payment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when seller and buyer dispute the price and the seller has not received payment, and explain the legal reasoning (talil) based on the seller's offer (ijab).

Core Idea
The shafi' pays the seller's lower price because his pre-emption right originates from the seller's offer.

In pre-emption (shuf'ah), disputes about the price can arise between seller and buyer. This lesson examines a specific scenario where the seller has not yet taken payment. The Hanafi school rules that the shafi' must take the property at the price claimed by the seller, not the buyer. Understanding the underlying reasoning—based on the legal cause of the seller's offer—is crucial for applying this ruling correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize the key elements: seller and buyer dispute the price (seller claims less, buyer claims more), and seller has not yet taken possession of the price.
This condition (seller unpaid) is essential; the ruling differs if seller has been paid.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The shafi' takes the property at the price claimed by the seller, not the buyer.
This is the mufta bihi position from Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Understand the dual-case reasoning
The text explains two possibilities: if seller is truthful, then price is his; if buyer is truthful, then seller's lower claim is a reduction benefiting the shafi'.
In either case, the shafi' pays the lower price.
4
Locate the legal cause (illah)
The shafi's ownership right arises from the seller's offer (ijab), so the seller's word is authoritative as long as his claim (matalibah) remains.
This is the proof: 'wa lianna al-tamalluka 'ala al-ba'i'i bi ijabihi'.

بائع اور مشتری کا شمن میں اختلاف ہوا بائع کم اور مشتری زیادتی کا دعوی کرے اور بائع نے ثمن پر ابھی قبضہ نہیں کیا ہے تو شفیع کس شمن سے وصول کرے گا

قال واذا ادعى المشترى ثمنا وادعى البائع اقل منه ولم يقبض الثمن اخذها الشفيع بما قاله البائع وكان ذالک خطأ عن المشترى وهذا لان الامر ان كان على ما قال البائع فقد وجبت الشفعة به وان كان على ما قال المشترى فقد حط البائع بعض الثمن وهذا الحط يظهر فى حق الشفيع على ما تبين ان شاء الله تعالى ولان التملك على البائع بايجابه فكان القول قوله في مقدار الثمن ما بقيت مطالبته فياخذ الشفيع بقوله

ترجمہ امام قدوری نے فرمایا اور جبکہ مشتری نے شمن کا دعوی کیا اور بائع نے اس سے کم کا دعویٰ کیا۔ حالانکہ بائع نے ثمن پر قبضہ نہیں کیا تو شفیع اس مکان کو اس مقدار سے لے گا۔ جو بائع کہہ رہا ہے اور یہ مشتری کے اوپر سے کم کرنا ہوگا۔ اور یہ اسلئے کہ بات اگر ایسے ہی ہے جو بائع کہہ رہا ہے تو شفعہ اسی مقدار کے مطابق ثابت ہو گا اور بات اگر ایسی ہے جو مشتری کہہ رہا ہے تو بائع نے شمن کی بعض مقدار کو کم کر دیا ہے اور یہ کی شفیع کے حق میں ظاہر ہوگی ۔ تفصیل کے مطابق جس کو ہم انشاء اللہ تعالیٰ بیان کریں گے اور اسلئے کہ بائع پر مالک ہونا اسکے ایجاب کی جہ سے ہے تو جب تک اس کا مطالبہ باقی ہے مقدارشن میں اسی کا قول معتبر ہوگا تو شفیع بائع کے قول کے مطابق لے گا تشریح ابھی تک بائع نے شمن پر قبضہ نہیں کیا اور بائع ایک ہزار روپے میں بیچنا بتاتا ہے اور مشتری دو ہزار میں تو یوں سمجھیں گے کہ شفیع نے کچھ من کم کر دیا اور یہ کی شفیع کے حق میں بھی ظاہر ہوگی۔ لہذا شفیع بائع کے قول کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے شمن کی کم مقدار پر دار مشفوعہ کو لے گا کیونکہ نفس الامر میں یا تو بائع حق پر ہے یا مشتری۔ پہلی صورت میں تو بائع کا قول معتبر ماننے میں کچھ کلام ہی نہیں اور دوسری صورت میں اس کوشن کے کم کر دینے پر محمول کیا جائے گا۔ لہذا بہر صورت بائع کے قول کا اعتبار ہوگا۔ لان التملك ... الخ - سے دلیل عقلی پیش کرتے ہیں کہ شفیع کو شفعہ ملنے کی وجہ بائع کا ایجاب ہے یعنی بائع کے ایجاب کی وجہ سے شفیع کو حق تملک حاصل ہوا ہے۔ لہذا جب بات یوں ہے تو جب تک بائع کا مطالبہ ( من ) باقی ہے اس کا قول معتبر ہو گا۔
The seller and buyer disputed about the price: the seller claimed less and the buyer claimed more, and the seller had not yet taken possession of the price. So with what price will the shafi' take? He (al-Quduri) said: When the buyer claims a price and the seller claims less than it, and he (the seller) has not taken possession of the price, the shafi' takes it (the property) with what the seller said, and that is a reduction from the buyer. This is because if the matter is as the seller said, then the right of pre-emption is established with that; and if it is as the buyer said, then the seller has reduced some of the price, and this reduction appears in favor of the shafi' as will be explained, Allah willing. And because ownership is based on the seller's offer (ijab), so his word is authoritative regarding the amount of the price as long as his claim remains, so the shafi' takes according to his word. (Then the Urdu commentary explains the same: The shafi' takes the house for the amount the seller says, and this is a reduction for the buyer. The rational proof is that the shafi' gets his right to own from the seller's offer, so the seller's statement is authoritative as long as his claim remains.)

Commentary
This is a ruling from the Hanafi school on the dispute between seller and buyer about the price when the seller has not yet received payment, and the shafi' (pre-emptor) wishes to take the property. The passage begins by stating the scenario: the buyer claims a higher price, the seller claims a lower price, and the seller has not yet taken payment. The ruling is that the shafi' takes the property at the price stated by the seller. The commentary explains the rationale: if the seller is telling the truth, then pre-emption is established at that price; if the buyer is telling the truth, then the seller's lower claim is considered a reduction of the price, which benefits the shafi'. The legal basis (dalil) is that the shafi's right of ownership arises from the seller's offer (ijab), so as long as the seller's claim (that he has not been fully paid) remains, his word is authoritative concerning the amount of the price. Thus, in either case, the shafi' pays the lower price claimed by the seller. This ruling is found in the Mukhtasar of al-Quduri and is part of the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
الشفيع (al-shafi'): The pre-emptor who has the right to take the sold property by paying its price.
الثمن (al-thaman): The price paid for the sold property, which is disputed between seller and buyer.
الإيجاب (al-ijab): The offer made by the seller that initiates the contract and gives rise to the shafi's right.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Shafi' Takes at Seller's Price After Mutual Oaths and Rescission
Ruling on the shafi's price after mutual oaths and rescission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the shafi' taking at the seller's price after mutual oaths and rescission, and explain the legal rationale.

Core Idea
The shafi' takes at seller's price even after rescission—rescission does not nullify the shafi's right.

When the seller and buyer dispute the price and the property is still with the seller, they undergo a procedure of mutual oaths (tahaluf). If both swear, the sale is rescinded, but the shafi' (pre-emptor) retains the right to take the property at the price claimed by the seller. This lesson explains the two possible outcomes and the reasoning behind preserving the shafi's right.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute scenario
The seller claims a higher price, the buyer a lower price, and the sold property is still in the seller's possession. This triggers the tahaluf procedure.
No evidence is available for either party.
2
Understand the first outcome: one party refuses the oath
If either the seller or buyer refuses to take an oath, the price is set according to the other party's claim. The shafi' then takes the property at that established price.
The refusing party's claim is disregarded.
3
Understand the second outcome: both parties take oaths
If both swear, the judge rescinds the sale (faskh). However, the shafi' still takes the property at the seller's claimed price.
Rescission does not affect the shafi's pre-existing right.
4
Apply the legal rationale
The dalil: 'lianna faskh al-bay' la yujibu butlan haqq al-shafi''—rescission does not nullify the shafi's right. The right attached at the moment of sale and survives the rescission.
This is based on qiyas and the principle that the shafi's right is independent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولو ادعى البائع الاكثر يتحالفان ويترادان و ايهما نكل ظهران الثمن ما يقوله الآخر فياخذها الشفيع بذالك وان حلفا يفسخ القاضى البيع على ما عرف وياخذها الشفيع بقول البائع لان فسخ البيع لا يوجب بطلان حق الشفيع

ترجمہ اہم قدوری نے فرمایا اور اگر بائع اکثر کا دعوی کرے تو دونوں قسم کھائیں اور عقد کو پھیر لیں اور ان دونوں میں سے جس نے قسم سے انکار کیا تو یہ بات ظاہر ہوگی کہ یمن وہ ہے جس کو دوسرا کہہ رہا ہے تو شفیع اس گھر کو اسی مقدار پر لے گا اور اگر دونوں نے قسم کھالی تو معروف طریقہ کے مطابق قاضی بیع کو مسخ کر دے گا اور شفیع اس دار کو بائع کے قول کے مطابق لے گا۔ اس لئے کہ بیچ کا فسح شفیع کے حق کے بطلان کو واجب نہیں کرتا۔ تشریح . اگر بائع اور مشتری میں مقدار شمن میں اختلاف ہوا اور میچ ابھی تک بائع کے قبضہ میں ہے اور بائع شمن زیادہ بتاتا ہے اور مشتری کم، تو جس کے پاس گواہ ہوں وہ گواہ پیش کرے۔ اگر دونوں میں کوئی بھی گواہ پیش نہ کر سکے تو دونوں سے حلف لیا جائیگا ۔ اب دو صورتیں ہیں یا تو کوئی ایک قسم سے انکار کرے گا یا دونوں قسم کھائیں گے اگر پہلی صورت ہو تو جس نے قسم سے انکار کیا بنے اس کے مخالف کی بات کا اعتبار ہو گا اور شمن کی مقدار دے کر شفیع گھر کو لے لے گا۔ اور اگر دونوں قسم کھا لیں تو قاضی بائع اور مشتری کے درمیان بیع کو فسخ کر دے گا۔ جب بیچ عاقدین کے درمیان شیخ ہو گی تو صرف بائع کا قول معتبر رہا اور شفیع شمن کی وہ مقدار دے کر جو بائع بتارہا ہے، اس مکان کو لے لے گا اور ناقدین کے درمیان بیچ کا فسخ ہو جان شفیع کے حق کو باطل نہیں کرتا جیسا کہ ماقبل میں گذر چکا ہے۔
He said: If the seller claims the larger (price), they (the parties) take oaths and return (the transaction), and whichever of them refuses the oath, it becomes apparent that the price is what the other says, so the shafi' takes it with that. If they both take oaths, the judge rescinds the sale according to what is known, and the shafi' takes (the property) by the seller's statement, because rescission of the sale does not necessitate nullification of the shafi's right. (Urdu commentary: If the seller claims more and the buyer claims less, and the sold property is still in the seller's possession, they take oaths. If one refuses, the other's price is accepted and the shafi' takes at that price. If both take oaths, the sale is rescinded, but the shafi' still takes at the seller's stated price because rescission does not void the shafi's right.)
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This is a ruling from the Hanafi school on a dispute between seller and buyer about the price when the seller claims a higher amount and the buyer claims a lower amount, and the sold property is still in the seller's possession. The passage begins by stating the scenario: the seller claims a higher price, the buyer a lower price. The procedure is that if they have no evidence, they take oaths. If one refuses the oath, the price stated by the other is established, and the shafi' takes at that price. If both take oaths, the judge rescinds the sale. However, the shafi' still takes the property at the price stated by the seller. The reason (dalil) is that rescission of the sale does not invalidate the shafi's right, which was already established by the original contract. This ruling is found in al-Quduri's Mukhtasar and is part of the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
التحالف (al-tahaluf): The mutual taking of oaths by both parties when there is a dispute and no evidence.
الفسخ (al-faskh): Rescission or annulment of the sale contract by the judge due to the mutual oaths.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The sale is rescinded and the shafi' takes at the seller's price
C) The sale is confirmed at the buyer's price
D) The shafi' may choose between the two prices

Key Takeaway
The shafi' takes at the seller's price even after rescission because rescission does not nullify the shafi's right.

Shafi' Follows Buyer's Price When Seller Has Taken Payment
Ruling on shafi' when seller has taken payment, with qiyas to a stranger.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the shafi's price when the seller has taken payment and explain the legal reasoning that ends the seller's involvement.

Core Idea
Once the seller receives the price, he becomes a stranger; the shafi' follows the buyer's price alone.

Shafi' (pre-emption) disputes often involve a buyer, seller, and the pre-emptor disagreeing on the price. The Hanafi school distinguishes cases based on whether the seller has actually taken the payment. This lesson addresses the scenario where the seller has already received the price, making his statement irrelevant and leaving only the buyer's word to determine the shafi's buyback amount.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The passage deals with the situation where the seller has taken possession (qabd) of the price from the buyer. This is a key condition that changes the ruling.
2
State the ruling
The shafi' takes the property at the price stated by the buyer. The seller's statement is completely ignored.
The ruling is from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, part of Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Analyze the legal reasoning (ta'lil)
The reason given: when the seller receives the price, the contract's ruling is concluded (intahā ḥukm al-‘aqd), he leaves the midst, and becomes like a stranger (ajnabī). A stranger has no stake in the transaction, so his word holds no weight in the dispute.
This is a qiyas: the seller after qabd is analogized to a stranger.
4
Contrast with the previous case
The text references an earlier ruling where the seller had not taken payment. In that situation, the seller's statement was still relevant. The present case is an exception to that general rule.
The prior case is explained in earlier parts of the text (not included in this passage).
5
Identify the thamarah (practical consequence)
The practical effect: the shafi' can only rely on the buyer's price. The seller cannot influence the buyback amount, protecting the shafi' from potential collusion or inflation.

Source Text

قال وان كان قبض الثمن اخذبما قال المشترى ان شأولم يلتفت الى قول البائع لانه لما استوفى الثمن انتهى حكم العقد وخرج هو من البين وصار كالاجنبى وبقى الاختلاف بين المشترى والشفيع وقد بيناه

ترجمہ اہم قدوری نے فرمایا اور اگر بائع شمن پر قبضہ کر چکا ہوتو شفیع لے گا اس مقدار کے ساتھ جو مشتری کہہ رہا ہے اگر چاہے اور بائع کے قول کی جانب التفات نہیں کی جائے گا۔ اسلئے کہ جب وہ شمن کو وصول کر چکا ہے تو عقد کا حکم پورا ہو گیا اور بائع درمیان سے نکل گیا اور اجنبی کے مثل ہو گیا اور اختلاف باقی بچا مشتری اور شفیع کے درمیان اور ہم اس کو بیان کر چکے ہیں۔ تشریح اب تک جو گفتگو تھی اس صورت میں تھی کہ بائع نے شمن پر قبضہ نہ کیا ہو اور اگر بائع شمن پر قبضہ کر چکا ہے تو اب وہ اجنبی کے مثل ہو گیا اور درمیان سے بالکل نکل گیا۔ بلکہ اب تو اختلاف مشتری اور شفیع کاباقی رہ گیا اور ماقبل میں مسئلہ گذر چکا ہے کہ جب مشتری اور شفیع کے درمیان اختلاف ہو تو مشتری
He said: If he (the seller) has taken possession of the price, he (the shafi') takes (the property) with what the buyer said, if he wishes, and no attention is paid to the seller's statement, because when he has received the price, the ruling of the contract is concluded, and he leaves the midst and becomes like a stranger, and the dispute remains between the buyer and the shafi', and we have explained it (previously). (Urdu commentary: If the seller has taken possession of the price, the shafi' takes the property at the amount the buyer states, and the seller's statement is ignored because he has become like a stranger; the dispute is now between the buyer and the shafi', and the ruling for that has already been given.)
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This is a ruling from the Hanafi school on a dispute about the price when the seller has already received payment. The passage begins by stating the scenario: the seller has taken the price, and now the buyer and seller dispute the amount. In this case, the shafi' takes the property at the price stated by the buyer, and the seller's statement is not considered. The reason (dalil) is that once the seller has received the price, the contract is concluded from his side; he becomes a stranger to the transaction. The dispute is now solely between the buyer and the shafi'. The ruling for when the shafi' and buyer dispute was previously explained (in earlier lessons). This ruling is from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar and is part of the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
القبض (al-qabd): Taking physical or constructive possession of the price by the seller, which ends his involvement in the dispute.
الأجنبي (al-ajnabi): A stranger or outsider who has no stake in the transaction; here refers to the seller after receiving payment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The seller's price
B) The buyer's price
C) The average of both
D) The shafi' chooses

Key Takeaway
When the seller has taken payment, the shafi' follows the buyer's price because the seller's interest in the transaction ceases.

Dispute on Price When Seller Has Not Taken Possession
Explains ruling when seller and buyer differ on price, property in seller's possession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when the seller and buyer dispute the price before the seller has taken possession, and explain how the pre-emptor's right survives rescission.

Core Idea
The pre-emptor's right survives even after the sale is rescinded due to a price dispute.

In a pre-emption (shuf'a) scenario, when the seller and buyer disagree on the price while the property is still in the seller's hands, the Hanafi school provides a detailed procedure involving mutual oaths and potential rescission. Critically, the pre-emptor's right is not lost if the sale is annulled. This lesson unpacks the ruling from the Mukhtasar al-Quduri and its commentary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The property is still in the seller's possession. The seller claims a higher price; the buyer claims a lower price. Neither has witnesses.
This is the precondition for applying the mutual oath procedure.
2
Trace the mutual oath procedure
If one party refuses the oath, the other party's price is accepted. If both swear, the judge rescinds the sale.
Mutual oaths (tahāluf) are a common Hanafi method for resolving price disputes.
3
Determine the pre-emptor's position after rescission
After rescission, the pre-emptor takes the property at the price stated by the seller (the higher price).
The buyer is out of the picture; only the seller's statement remains reliable.
4
Understand the legal basis
Rescission of the sale does not nullify the pre-emptor's right. The right is attached to the property itself, not to the contract.
This is a key Hanafi principle: shuf'a is a right that persists despite contract annulment.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school generally does not allow pre-emption for property not yet delivered to the buyer, restricting the scope of shuf'a.
Hanafi school expands the right to protect co-owners and neighbors.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولو ادعى البائع الاكثر يتحالفان ويترادان و ايهما نكل ظهران الثمن ما يقوله الآخر فياخذها الشفيع بذالك وان حلفا يفسخ القاضى البيع على ما عرف وياخذها الشفيع بقول البائع لان فسخ البيع لا يوجب بطلان حق الشفيع
ترجمہ: اہم قدوری نے فرمایا اور اگر بائع اکثر کا دعوی کرے تو دونوں قسم کھائیں اور عقد کو پھیر لیں اور ان دونوں میں سے جس نے قسم سے انکار کیا تو یہ بات ظاہر ہوگی کہ یمن وہ ہے جس کو دوسرا کہہ رہا ہے تو شفیع اس گھر کو اسی مقدار پر لے گا اور اگر دونوں نے قسم کھالی تو معروف طریقہ کے مطابق قاضی بیع کو مسخ کر دے گا اور شفیع اس دار کو بائع کے قول کے مطابق لے گا۔ اس لئے کہ بیچ کا فسح شفیع کے حق کے بطلان کو واجب نہیں کرتا۔
تشریح: اگر بائع اور مشتری میں مقدار شمن میں اختلاف ہوا اور میچ ابھی تک بائع کے قبضہ میں ہے اور بائع شمن زیادہ بتاتا ہے اور مشتری کم، تو جس کے پاس گواہ ہوں وہ گواہ پیش کرے۔ اگر دونوں میں کوئی بھی گواہ پیش نہ کر سکے تو دونوں سے حلف لیا جائیگا ۔ اب دو صورتیں ہیں یا تو کوئی ایک قسم سے انکار کرے گا یا دونوں قسم کھائیں گے اگر پہلی صورت ہو تو جس نے قسم سے انکار کیا بنے اس کے مخالف کی بات کا اعتبار ہو گا اور شمن کی مقدار دے کر شفیع گھر کو لے لے گا۔ اور اگر دونوں قسم کھا لیں تو قاضی بائع اور مشتری کے درمیان بیع کو فسخ کر دے گا۔ جب بیچ عاقدین کے درمیان شیخ ہو گی تو صرف بائع کا قول معتبر رہا اور شفیع شمن کی وہ مقدار دے کر جو بائع بتارہا ہے، اس مکان کو لے لے گا اور ناقدین کے درمیان بیچ کا فسخ ہو جان شفیع کے حق کو باطل نہیں کرتا جیسا کہ ماقبل میں گذر چکا ہے۔ بائع نے شمن پر قبضہ کر لیا تو وہ ایک اجنبی کی طرح ہے
He said: If the seller claims the greater (price), they take mutual oaths and return (the transaction), and whichever of them refuses the oath, the price becomes apparent as the other says, so the pre-emptor takes it (the property) with that (price). If they both swear, the judge rescinds the sale according to what is known, and the pre-emptor takes it according to the seller's statement, because rescission of the sale does not necessitate nullification of the pre-emptor's right. Translation: The important Quduri said: If the seller claims the greater, both take oaths and revoke the contract. Whichever refuses the oath, it becomes apparent that the price is what the other says, so the pre-emptor takes this house at that amount. If both take oaths, the judge rescinds the sale in the known manner, and the pre-emptor takes this house according to the seller's statement, because rescission of the sale does not necessitate nullification of the pre-emptor's right. Explanation: If the seller and buyer differ on the amount of price and the property is still in the seller's possession, and the seller states a higher price while the buyer states a lower price, then whoever has witnesses presents them. If neither can present witnesses, both are made to take oaths. Two cases: either one refuses the oath or both take oaths. In the first case, the one who refused the oath, the statement of the opponent is relied upon, and the pre-emptor takes the house by paying that amount. If both take oaths, the judge rescinds the sale between seller and buyer. When the sale is rescinded between the contracting parties, only the seller's statement is reliable, and the pre-emptor takes this house by paying the amount the seller stated. The rescission of the sale between the parties does not invalidate the pre-emptor's right, as previously discussed. If the seller has taken possession of the price, he becomes like a stranger.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding pre-emption (shuf'a) when the seller and buyer dispute the price while the property remains in the seller's possession. The ruling is from the matn of Quduri, expanded by the commentator. The key scenario: the seller claims a higher price, the buyer a lower one, and the property is still with the seller. If neither has witnesses, mutual oaths are administered. If one refuses, the other's price stands. If both swear, the sale is rescinded, but the pre-emptor still has the right to take the property at the seller's stated price. The reason given is that rescission between the original parties does not negate the pre-emptor's right. This illustrates the strength of shuf'a in Hanafi fiqh: it survives even the cancellation of the underlying sale. The commentary emphasizes that after rescission, only the seller's word on the price is considered because the buyer is out of the picture.

This ruling follows the general Hanafi principle that shuf'a is an established right that cannot be easily defeated. The authority weight is Zahir al-Riwayah as it appears in Quduri's Mukhtasar, a widely transmitted work.

Key Terms
شفعة (shuf'a): The right of a co-owner or neighbor to purchase a property sold to an outsider, compensating the buyer.
شفيع (shafi'): The person entitled to pre-emption, who takes the property from the buyer.
ثمن (thaman): The price paid by the buyer to the seller.
تحالف (tahāluf): Mutual oath-taking by two parties disputing a transaction, leading to rescission if both swear.
فسخ (faskh): Rescission or annulment of a contract by a judge due to irreconcilable dispute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens when both seller and buyer swear oaths regarding the price, and the property is still with the seller?
A) The pre-emptor takes the property at the buyer's price
B) The judge rescinds the sale, and the pre-emptor takes at the seller's price
C) The sale stands, and the pre-emptor has no right
D) The seller's price is accepted without oath

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the pre-emptor's right to the property remains intact even after the sale is rescinded due to a price dispute, with the pre-emptor paying the seller's stated price.
